PREFACE
   This code of the City of Dawson, as supplemented, contains ordinances up to
and including ordinance 309, passed June 3, 2025. Ordinances of the City
adopted after said ordinance supersede the provisions of this code to the
extent that they are in conflict or inconsistent therewith. Consult the City
office in order to ascertain whether any particular provision of the code has
been amended, superseded or repealed.
      American Legal Publishing
      Cincinnati, Ohio

the ordinances listed.
ADOPTING ORDINANCE
ORDINANCE 259
ORDINANCE ADOPTING CITY CODE OF THE CITY OF DAWSON
The city of Dawson adopts the provisions of the city code of Dawson, Minnesota,
2005. The provisions of this code shall be held to be minimum requirements and
shall be liberally construed in favor of the governing body and shall not be
deemed a limitation or repeal of any other powers granted by state statutes.
The 2005 city code is adopted for the orderly administration of city affairs,
for the purpose of protecting public health, safety, morals, comfort,
convenience and general welfare, protecting and preserving resources, promoting
orderly development within the city,
Section 1:   Administration
Section 2:   Boards And Commissions
Section 3:   Business And License Regulations
Section 4:   Public Health And Safety
Section 5:   Police Regulations
Section 6:   Motor Vehicles And Traffic
Section 7:   Public Ways And Property
Section 8:   Public Utilities
Section 9:   Franchises
Section 10:   Building Regulations
Section 11:   Zoning Regulations
Section 12:   Subdivision Regulations
Section 13:   Flood Control
Passed and approved:      /s/ Merlin Ellefson   
         Mayor
January 17, 2006

TITLE 1
ADMINISTRATION
CHAPTER 1
DAWSON CITY CODE
SECTION:
1-1-1: Title
1-1-2: Purpose
1-1-3: Acceptance
1-1-4: Amendments
1-1-5: Code Alterations
1-1-6: Use And Sale
1-1-7: Supplemental Materials
1-1-1: TITLE:
Upon the adoption by the city council, this code is hereby declared to be and
shall hereafter constitute the official city code of Dawson. This city code of
ordinances shall be known and cited as the DAWSON CITY CODE and is hereby
published by authority of the city council and shall be supplemented to
incorporate the most recent legislation of the city as provided in section
1-1-4 of this chapter. Any reference to the number of any section contained
herein shall be understood to refer to the position of the same number, its
appropriate chapter and title heading, and to the general penalty clause
relating thereto, as well as to the section itself, when reference is made to
this code by title in any legal documents. (2005 Code)
1-1-2: PURPOSE:
The purpose of this code is to effect a general revision and codification of
the ordinances of the city so as to revise and present in an orderly manner the
provisions of the ordinances of a general nature of the city, add such
provisions as may promote the efficient operation of the city and the public
welfare, and eliminate obsolete and unneeded ordinance provisions. (1982 Code §
1.112)
1-1-3: ACCEPTANCE:
The city code, as hereby presented in printed form, shall hereafter be received
without further proof in all courts and in administrative tribunals of this
state as the ordinances of the city of general and permanent effect, except the
excluded ordinances enumerated in section
1-2-1 of this title. (2005 Code)
1-1-4: AMENDMENTS:
   A.   Code Amendments: This code may be amended by subsequent ordinances.
Amendments shall be deemed incorporated into this code, and repeals shall take
effect, as of the effective date of the amending ordinance. Reference to this
code, or any part of it, shall be deemed to include this code as amended.
Amendments shall be constructed in accordance with the manifest intent of the
city council in their enactment even though the amendments are irregular or
deficient for some reason in the manner in which they amend this code. (1982
Code § 1.511)
   B.   Transition Provisions:
      1.   Existing Rights And Liabilities: The repeal of any ordinance or
portion of it upon the enactment of this code, or of any amendment to it, shall
not affect in any manner rights and liabilities existing at that time. Any act
done, offense committed, right accruing, or liability, penalty, forfeiture or
punishment incurred or assessed prior to the effective date of this code or of
any amendment shall not be affected by the enactment of this code or the
amendment. (1982 Code § 1.711)
      2.   Continuing Of Existing Rates And Requirements: This code provides
that the council shall, by resolution, establish various rates, requirements
and other matters. Until the city council does so on any subject, the rates,
requirements and other matters required to be established by resolution shall
remain, insofar as they remain applicable, the same as they existed prior to
the enactment of this code. (1982 Code § 1.712)
   C.   Form; Codification: Any ordinance amending this code shall set forth
the title, chapter and section number of the section or sections to be amended,
and this shall constitute sufficient compliance with any statutory requirement
pertaining to the amendment or revision by ordinance of any part of this code.
All such amendments or revisions by ordinance shall be immediately forwarded to
the codifiers, and the said ordinance material shall be prepared for insertion
in its proper place in each copy of this code. Each such replacement page shall
be properly identified and shall be inserted in each individual copy of the
city code. (2005 Code)
1-1-5: CODE ALTERATIONS:
It shall be deemed unlawful for any person to alter, change, replace or deface
in any way any section or any page of this code in such a manner that the
meaning of any phrase or order may be changed or omitted. Replacement pages may
be inserted according to the official instructions when so authorized by the
city council. The city clerk shall see that the replacement pages are properly
inserted in the official copies maintained in the office of the city clerk. Any
person having custody of a copy of the city code shall make every effort to
maintain said code current as to the most recent ordinances passed. Such person
shall see to the immediate insertion of new or replacement pages when such are
delivered or made available to such person through the office of the city
clerk. Said code books, while in actual possession of officials and other
interested persons, shall be and remain the property of the city and shall be
returned to the office of the city clerk when directed so to do by order of the
city council. (2005 Code)
1-1-6: USE AND SALE:
   A.   Copies For Public Inspection: The city clerk shall keep copies of this
code and amendments to it for public inspection. (1982 Code § 1.211)
   B.   Sale And Distribution: The city clerk shall keep copies of this code
and amendments to it for sale at a reasonable charge. The city clerk may
distribute without charge copies of this code and amendments to it for use by
public officials, the judiciary and other persons when the municipal welfare
will be served by doing so. (1982 Code § 1.212)
1-1-7: SUPPLEMENTAL MATERIALS:
Any table of contents, appendices, index and all other supplemental materials
which may from time to time be printed with this code shall not be considered a
part of this code. They are intended for convenience only. (1982 Code § 1.313)
CHAPTER 2
SAVING CLAUSE
SECTION:
1-2-1: Repeal Of General Ordinances
1-2-2: Public Ways And Public Utility Ordinances
1-2-3: Court Proceedings
1-2-4: Conflict With Charter
1-2-5: Severability Clause
1-2-6: Notice Of Asserted Invalidity
1-2-7: No Right Of Action Against City Created
1-2-8: Notice Requirements
1-2-1: REPEAL OF GENERAL ORDINANCES:
All general ordinances of the city passed prior to the adoption of this code
are hereby repealed, except such as are included in this code or are by
necessary implication herein reserved from repeal (subject to the saving
clauses contained in the following sections), and excluding the following
ordinances which are not hereby repealed: tax levy ordinances; appropriation
ordinances; ordinances relating to boundaries and annexations; franchise
ordinances and other ordinances granting special rights to persons or
corporations; contract ordinances and ordinances authorizing the execution of a
contract or the issuance of warrants; salary ordinances; ordinances
establishing, naming or vacating streets, alleys or other public places;
improvement ordinances; bond ordinances; ordinances relating to elections;
ordinances relating to the transfer or acceptance of real estate by or from the
city; and all special ordinances. (2005 Code)
1-2-2: PUBLIC WAYS AND PUBLIC UTILITY ORDINANCES:
No ordinance relating to railroad crossings with streets and other public ways,
or relating to the conduct, duties, service or rates of public utilities shall
be repealed by virtue of the adoption of this code or by virtue of the
preceding section, excepting as this code may contain provisions for such
matters, in which case, this code shall be considered as amending such
ordinance or ordinances in respect to such provisions only. (2005 Code)
1-2-3: COURT PROCEEDINGS:
   A.   No new ordinance shall be construed or held to repeal a former
ordinance whether such former ordinance is expressly repealed or not, as to any
offense committed against such former ordinance or as to any act done, any
penalty, forfeiture or punishment so incurred, or any right accrued or claim
arising under the former ordinance, or in any way whatever to affect any such
offense or act so committed or so done, or any penalty, forfeiture or
punishment so incurred or any right accrued or claim arising before the new
ordinance takes effect, save only that the proceedings thereafter shall conform
to the ordinance in force at the time of such proceeding, so far as
practicable. If any penalty, forfeiture or punishment may be mitigated by any
provision of a new ordinance, such provision may be, by consent of the party
affected, applied to any judgment announced after the new ordinance takes
effect.
   B.   This section shall extend to all repeals, either by express words or
implication, whether the repeal is in the ordinance making any new provisions
upon the same subject or in any other ordinance.
   C.   Nothing contained in this chapter shall be construed as abating any
action now pending under or by virtue of any general ordinance of the city
herein repealed, and the provisions of all general ordinances contained in this
code shall be deemed to be continuing provisions and not a new enactment of the
same provisions; nor shall this chapter be deemed as discontinuing, abating,
modifying or altering any penalty accrued or to accrue, or as affecting the
liability of any person, firm or corporation, or as waiving any right of the
city under any ordinance or provision thereof in force at the time of the
adoption of this code. (2005 Code)
1-2-4: CONFLICT WITH CHARTER:
In case any provision of this code conflicts with any provision of the city
charter, the charter provision shall control. (1982 Code § 1.416)
1-2-5: SEVERABILITY CLAUSE:
Unless otherwise provided with respect to particular provisions, all provisions
of this code shall be severable. If any provision of this code is held invalid
or suspended, the remaining provisions shall remain valid and in operation
unless the court finds that the valid provisions are so essentially connected
with and so dependent upon the void provision that the court cannot presume the
council would have enacted the remaining valid provisions without the void one,
or unless the court finds the remaining valid provisions, standing alone, are
incomplete and are incapable of being executed in accordance with the intent of
the city council. (1982 Code § 1.418)
1-2-6: NOTICE OF ASSERTED INVALIDITY:
When the validity of any part of this code is drawn into question in any action
to which the city is not a party, the party asserting the invalidity shall
notify the city attorney of such contention as soon as practicable. (1982 Code
§ 1.419)
1-2-7: NO RIGHT OF ACTION AGAINST CITY CREATED:
This code includes various provisions for licensure, approval, investigation,
inspection and regulation of businesses and activities. These provisions have
been enacted to assist the city in promoting public health, safety and welfare.
It is not the intention of the city council that any person shall rely upon the
city or its agents in any licensure, approval, investigation, inspection or
other regulation. Unless expressly provided otherwise, no provision of this
code relieves any person of the responsibility for that person's own protection
or the protection of others. Nor shall any provision create any right of action
against the city or its agents that would not exist without the provision.
Neither the city nor its agents shall have any liability by reason of the
enforcement of, or failure to enforce, any provision of this code. (1982 Code §
1.420)
1-2-8: NOTICE REQUIREMENTS:
Whenever any provision of this code requires notice to be given to any person,
the notice shall be in writing. Unless personal, published, posted or some
other method of notice in required, notice may be given by regular or certified
mail at the person's last known address, by delivery to the person personally,
by leaving the notice for the person at the person's usual place of abode with
a person of suitable age and discretion then residing there, or by any method
of service sufficient for service of process in a civil suit. Published or
posted notice may be given where permitted by law, charter, or this code, and
shall be given when required. Failure to give notice or defects in the notice
shall not invalidate the proceeding for which notice was required if a good
faith effort was made to give the notice required, if due to special
circumstances the notice could not be given, if the person not receiving notice
or receiving defective notice was not prejudiced thereby or if the person
received actual notice in some other manner. (1982 Code § 1.421)
CHAPTER 3
DEFINITIONS
SECTION:
1-3-1: Construction Of Words
1-3-2: Grammar And Punctuation
1-3-3: Definitions, General
1-3-4: Substantially Similar Prior Provisions
1-3-5: Irreconcilable Provisions
1-3-6: Catchlines
1-3-1: CONSTRUCTION OF WORDS:
   A.   In construing this code, the following rules shall govern unless their
observance would involve a construction inconsistent with the manifest intent
of the city council or be repugnant to the context of the relevant provisions
of this code:
      1.   Words and phrases shall be construed according to rules of grammar
and according to their common and approved usage, but technical words and
phrases and such others as have acquired a special meaning or are defined in
this code shall be construed according to their special meaning or definition.
      2.   The singular includes the plural, and the plural includes the
singular.
      3.   Words used in the past or present tense include the future.
      4.   General words are restricted in meaning by particular words. (1982
Code § 1.411)
      5.   As used in this code, "may" is permissive and "shall" is mandatory,
except that, unless expressly provided otherwise, "shall" is directory when
used with reference to the duties of any officer or employee of the city. (1982
Code § 1.412)
   B.   The word "ordinance" contained in the ordinances of the city has been
changed in the content of this code to "title", "chapter", "section" and/or
"subsection" or words of like import for organizational and clarification
purposes only. Such change to the city's ordinances is not meant to amend
passage and effective dates of such original ordinances. (2005 Code)
1-3-2: GRAMMAR AND PUNCTUATION:
Grammatical errors shall not invalidate any provision of this code. A
transposition of words and clauses may be resorted to when a sentence is
without meaning as it stands. Punctuation shall not control over the intent of
the city council in the enactment of a provision. Words and phrases which do
not conflict with the obvious purpose and intent of a provision nor in any way
affect its scope and operation may be added when necessary to the proper
interpretation of the provision. (1982 Code § 1.413)
1-3-3: DEFINITIONS, GENERAL:
When used in this code, the following terms shall have the meaning given to
them in this section, except as further defined in relation to specific
provisions of this code, or unless another intention clearly appears:
AGENT: A person acting on behalf of another with authority conferred, either
expressly or by implication.
CHARTER: The city charter of the city of Dawson.
CITY: The city of Dawson, county of Lac Qui Parle, state of Minnesota.
CLERK: The city clerk of the city of Dawson.
CODE: The municipal code of the city of Dawson.
COUNCIL: Unless otherwise indicated, the city council of the city of Dawson.
COUNTY: The county of Lac Qui Parle, state of Minnesota.
EMPLOYEES: Whenever reference is made in this code to a city employee by title
only, this shall be construed as though followed by the words "of the city of
Dawson".
GENDER: A word importing either the masculine or feminine gender only shall
extend and be applied to the other gender and to persons.
LICENSE: The permission granted for the carrying on of a business, profession
or occupation.
NUISANCE: Anything offensive to the sensibilities of reasonable persons, or any
act or activity creating a hazard which threatens the health and welfare of
inhabitants of the city, or any activity which by its perpetuation can
reasonably be said to have a detrimental effect on the property of a person or
persons within the community.
OCCUPANT: As applied to a building or land, shall include any person who
occupies the whole or any part of such building or land whether alone or with
others.
OFFENSE: Any act forbidden by any provision of this code or the omission of any
act required by the provisions of this code.
OFFICERS: Whenever reference is made in this code to a city officer by title
only, this shall be construed as though followed by the words "of the city of
Dawson".
OPERATOR: The person who is in charge of any operation, business or profession.
OWNER: As applied to a building or land, shall include any part owner, joint
owner, tenant in common, joint tenant or lessee of the whole or of a part of
such building or land.
PERSON: Any individual, firm, partnership, association, organization or
corporation. It also includes any executor, administrator, trustee, receiver or
other representative appointed by law. As applied to partnerships, associations
and organizations, it includes the partners, members and employees. As applied
to corporations, it includes the officers, agents and employees.
PERSONAL PROPERTY: Shall include every description of money, goods, chattels,
effects, evidence of rights in action and all written instruments by which any
pecuniary obligation, right or title to property is created, acknowledged,
transferred, increased, defeated, discharged or diminished and every right or
interest therein.
RETAILER: Unless otherwise specifically defined, shall be understood to relate
to the sale of goods, merchandise, articles or things direct to the consumer.
RIGHT OF WAY: The privilege of the immediate use of the roadway or other
property.
STATE: The state of Minnesota.
STREET: Shall include alleys, lanes, courts, boulevards, public ways, public
squares, public places and sidewalks.
TENANT: As applied to a building or land, shall include any person who occupies
the whole or any part of such building or land, whether alone or with others.
TREASURER: The city treasurer of the city of Dawson.
WHOLESALER AND WHOLESALE DEALER: Unless otherwise specifically defined, shall
be understood to relate to the sale of goods, merchandise, articles or things
to persons who purchase for the purpose of resale.
WRITTEN, IN WRITING: May include printing and any other mode of representing
words and letters, but when the written signature of any person is required by
law to any official or public writing or bond, it shall be in the proper
handwriting of such person, or in case such person is unable to write, by such
person's proper mark. (1982 Code § 1.417; amd. 2005 Code)
1-3-4: SUBSTANTIALLY SIMILAR PRIOR PROVISIONS:
Insofar as provisions of this code are the same or substantially the same as
preexisting ordinance provisions, and insofar as any amendment to the code
reenacts then existing provisions of the code, the later provisions shall be
construed as a continuation of the earlier provision. (1982 Code § 1.414)
1-3-5: IRRECONCILABLE PROVISIONS:
Provisions are to be construed so that effect may be given to each. In case of
conflict, they shall be construed as follows, in the priority listed:
   A.   If a special provision is in irreconcilable conflict with a general
provision, the special provision shall prevail and be construed as an exception
to the general provision unless the general provision has been enacted later
and shows a manifest intent of the city council that the general provision
shall prevail.
   B.   If enacted at different times, the latest in date of enactment shall
prevail.
   C.   If part of the same provision or set of provisions, the provision,
portion or clause last in position shall prevail.
   D.   Provisions shall be liberally construed to effect the well being of the
city and to promote good government at minimum expense. (1982 Code § 1.415)
1-3-6: CATCHLINES:
The catchlines of the several sections of the city code are intended as mere
catchwords to indicate the content of the section and shall not be deemed or
taken to be titles of such sections, nor be deemed to govern, limit, modify or
in any manner affect the scope, meaning or intent of the provisions of any
division or section hereof, nor unless expressly so provided, shall they be so
deemed when any of such sections, including the catchlines, are amended or
reenacted. (2005 Code)
CHAPTER 4
GENERAL PENALTY
SECTION:
1-4-1: General Penalty
1-4-2: Separate Violations
1-4-3: Costs Of Prosecution
1-4-4: Application Of Provisions
1-4-5: Application To City Personnel
1-4-6: Enforcement
1-4-1: GENERAL PENALTY:
   A.   Petty Misdemeanors: Whenever an act or omission is declared by this
code, or by any law or code adopted by reference in this code, to be a petty
misdemeanor or a petty offense, any person violating the provision shall, upon
conviction, be subject to a fine of not more than three hundred dollars
($300.00).
   B.   Misdemeanors And Penalty For Other Offenses: Except when declared to be
a petty misdemeanor or a petty offense, or except when another lesser penalty
is expressly provided, any person violating any provision of this code, or any
law or code adopted by reference in this code, shall, upon conviction, be
subject to a fine of not more than one thousand dollars ($1,000.00) or
imprisonment for not more than ninety (90) days, or both such fine and
imprisonment. (Ord. 265, 3-6-2007)
   C.   Administrative Offenses: Any person violating an administrative rule,
or any offense that would otherwise be a misdemeanor or petty misdemeanor for
which the city has established a scheduled penalty, shall be subject to the
scheduled penalty not to exceed one thousand dollars ($1,000.00) for each
offense. The determination as to whether to treat an offense as an
administrative offense, petty misdemeanor or misdemeanor shall be up to the
discretion of the complainant. (Ord. 274, 12-2-2008)
1-4-2: SEPARATE VIOLATIONS:
Unless otherwise provided, each act or omission in violation of this code
constitutes a separate offense. A separate offense shall be deemed committed
each day upon which a violation continues. (1982 Code § 1.613)
1-4-3: COSTS OF PROSECUTION:
Whenever any person is convicted of a violation of any provision of this code,
the costs of prosecution may be added. (1982 Code § 1.614)
1-4-4: APPLICATION OF PROVISIONS:
   A.   Scope: The penalty provided in this chapter shall be applicable to
every section of this code the same as though it were a part of each and every
separate section. Any person convicted of a violation of any section of this
code where any duty is prescribed or obligation imposed, or where any action
which is of a continuing nature is forbidden or is declared to be unlawful,
shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor.
   B.   Prosecuting Officer Discretion: In all cases where the same offense is
made punishable or is created by different clauses or sections of this code,
the prosecuting officer may elect under which to proceed; but not more than one
recovery shall be had against the same person for the same offense; provided,
that the revocation of a license or permit shall not be considered a recovery
or penalty so as to bar any other penalty being enforced.
   C.   General Application: Whenever the doing of any act or the omission to
do any act constitutes a breach of any section or provision of this code and
there shall be no fine or penalty specifically declared for such breach, the
provisions of this chapter shall apply. (2005 Code)
1-4-5: APPLICATION TO CITY PERSONNEL:
No provision of this code designating the duties of any officer or employee
shall be so construed as to make such officer or employee liable for any fine
or penalty provided for a failure to perform such duty, unless the intention of
the city council to impose such fine or penalty on such officer or employee is
specifically and clearly expressed in the section creating the duty. (2005
Code)
1-4-6: ENFORCEMENT:
In the event of a violation or threatened violation of this code, the city
council, in addition to other remedies specified in this code or otherwise
allowed by law, may cause any lawful action to be taken or proceeding to be
commenced to prevent, restrain, correct or abate the violation or threatened
violation. (1982 Code § 1.616)
CHAPTER 5
MAYOR AND CITY COUNCIL 1
SECTION:
1-5-1: City Council Meetings
1-5-2: Compensation
 
Notes
1 1. See also city charter.
1-5-1: CITY COUNCIL MEETINGS 1 :
   A.   Regular Meetings: Regular meetings of the city council shall be held on
the first Tuesday of each month at seven thirty o'clock (7:30) P.M. (1982 Code
§ 2.311)
   B.   Special And Adjourned Meetings: The city council may, at any regular
meeting, establish a date, time and place for holding an adjourned or special
meeting. At other times, special meetings may be called by the mayor or by any
two (2) members of the city council by writing filed with the city clerk, who
shall then mail or deliver a notice to each council member of the time and
place of the meeting at least twenty four (24) hours before the meeting, unless
it is impossible to give twenty four (24) hours' notice due to the urgency of
the meeting, in which case notice shall be given as soon as possible. Notice of
any special meeting not called at the time of a regular meeting shall be posted
at the city hall, and, when time permits, published in the official newspaper.
(1982 Code § 2.312)
   C.   Place Of Meetings: All meetings, including special and adjourned
meetings, shall be held at the city council chambers in the city hall, except
that the city council may adjourn any meeting to some other place, or hold a
special meeting at some other place, for the convenience of the public or where
the nature of the matter under consideration makes it reasonably necessary to
consider the matter at the other place. (1982 Code § 2.313)
 
Notes
1 2. See also city charter chapter three, MSA § 412.191, subd. 2.
1-5-2: COMPENSATION 1 :
   A.   Mayor: The mayor shall be paid one thousand two hundred dollars
($1,200.00) annually for attending regular meetings of the city council. The
mayor shall be paid twenty five dollars ($25.00) for each special or adjourned
meeting of the city council attended.
   B.   City Council: Each council member shall be paid nine hundred dollars
($900.00) annually for attending regular meetings of the city council. Each
council member shall be paid twenty five dollars ($25.00) for each special or
adjourned meeting of the city council attended. (Ord. 205, 11-7-1988; amd. 2005
Code)
   C.   Date Of Change: Unless a later date is established in any ordinance
changing the compensation of the mayor or of the city council, no change in
salary enacted pursuant to the authority granted in Minnesota Statutes
Annotated section 415.11 shall take effect until after the next succeeding
municipal election, and until that date the salary shall remain as last
previously established. (1982 Code § 2.333)
 
Notes
1 3. MSA § 415.11.
CHAPTER 6
CITY OFFICERS AND EMPLOYEES
SECTION:
1-6-1: Officers
1-6-2: City Manager
1-6-3: City Clerk
1-6-4: City Treasurer
1-6-5: Additional Offices And Employees
1-6-6: Personnel Policy
1-6-7: Criminal History Background Checks
1-6-1: OFFICERS 1 :
The city shall have such officers as have been established by charter. Pursuant
to the authority granted by charter, other offices may be established by the
city council by ordinance. (1982 Code § 2.111)
 
Notes
1 1. See city charter, chapter one, 1.03, sections 5 and 6, and chapter four;
  MSA § 412.111.
1-6-2: CITY MANAGER 1 :
   A.   Office Created: The office of city manager is hereby created in the
city.
   B.   Appointment; Removal: The city manager shall be appointed and removed
as provided in the city charter, chapter one, 1.03, section 3. The city manager
shall be appointed for an indefinite period of time and shall be paid for his
services at such a salary as the city council from time to time may determine.
   C.   Bond: The city manager shall be bonded at city expense, through a
position bond (faithful performance) which will indemnify the city in the
amount of fifty thousand dollars ($50,000.00).
   D.   Powers And Duties: The city manager shall be the chief administrative
officer of the city and shall perform the following duties and as set forth in
chapter one, 1.03, section 4 of the city charter:
      1.   Supervision and management of the various subordinate offices,
agencies and departments of the city.
      2.   Coordinate the administration of the various divisions and
departments of the city.
      3.   Make recommendations to the city council regarding personnel
policies, employment and dismissal of subordinate officers and employees.
      4.   Develop and issue all administrative rules, regulations and
procedures necessary to ensure the proper functioning of and coordination with
all departments. Such rules, regulations and procedures shall be consistent
with federal and Minnesota law, city ordinances, and written city council
policy. Said rules, regulations and procedures shall be effective upon issuance
and shall continue to be in effect until rescinded by the city manager or by
express action of the city council.
      5.   Submit to the city council at least thirty (30) days prior to call
by the county auditor, a single consolidated budget document which shall
include statements relating to projected revenue and proposed sources of
revenue, and all proposed expenditures to be made and obligations to be
incurred by the city in the forthcoming fiscal year.
      6.   Advise the city council on all matters pertaining to or affecting
the operation of the city government and the city proper.
      7.   The city manager shall be responsible for the enforcement of all
laws and ordinances within the city, and whenever necessary shall make
recommendations for changes, amendments or repeal of existing ordinances.
      8.   The city manager shall be directly responsible to the city council
for the faithful and satisfactory performance of the duties of the office;
shall attend all council meetings, but shall not vote; and shall attend such
committee meetings as the city council may direct.
      9.   The city manager shall be the chief purchasing agent of the city and
all city purchases and contracts shall be made or let by the city manager when
the amount involved does not exceed two thousand five hundred dollars
($2,500.00). All other purchases shall be made and all other contracts shall be
let by the city council after the recommendation of the city manager has first
been obtained. All contracts, bonds and instruments of any kind to which the
city is a party shall be signed by the mayor and the city manager on behalf of
the city. (1982 Code § 2.114)
      10.   In addition to the stated powers and duties, the city manager shall
be responsible for the employment and termination of city personnel, other than
otherwise provided for by code or charter. Personnel being involuntarily
terminated shall follow the grievance procedures in the city personnel policy.
(Ord. 195, 6-4-1985)
      11.   Perform such other duties as are required by state law, city
ordinance or as the city council shall from time to time direct. (1982 Code §
2.114)
 
Notes
1 2. See city charter, chapter one, 1.03, sections 3 and 4, and chapter four;
  MSA § 412.641.
1-6-3: CITY CLERK 1 :
A city clerk shall be appointed by the city council, receive such compensation
as the city council may fix, and serve at the pleasure of the city council. The
city clerk shall have such powers and duties as are prescribed by law, by
charter and as the city council may determine. (1982 Code § 2.112)
 
Notes
1 1. See city charter, chapter one, 1.03, section 5, and chapter four; MSA §
  412.151.
1-6-4: CITY TREASURER 1 :
A city treasurer shall be appointed by the city council, receive such
compensation as the city council may fix, and serve at the pleasure of the city
council. The city treasurer shall have such powers and duties as are prescribed
by law, by charter and as the city council may determine. (1982 Code § 2.113)
 
Notes
1 2. MSA § 412.111.
1-6-5: ADDITIONAL OFFICES AND EMPLOYEES:
In addition to the departments, boards, commissions, agencies and other offices
created by charter or in title 2 of this code or other provisions of this code,
the city council may create such additional offices and may designate such
other employees and agents as may be necessary or helpful to the efficient
government of the city and operation and maintenance of the public facilities.
(1982 Code § 2.491)
1-6-6: PERSONNEL POLICY:
The personnel policy for city employees shall be as adopted from time to time
by resolution of the city council. Copies are on file in the office of the city
clerk. (2005 Code)
1-6-7: CRIMINAL HISTORY BACKGROUND CHECKS:
   A.   The Dawson police department is authorized to do a criminal history
background check investigation on applicants for city employment, volunteer
positions and contractors/consultants hired to provide services to the city.
Background investigations of contractors/consultants will only be done if they
have access to sensitive city systems and information such as security
information and private data. Before the investigation is undertaken, the
applicant/individual must authorize the police department in writing to
undertake the investigation and to release the information to the city council,
city manager and other city staff as appropriate. Should the city reject the
applicant/individual due, partially or solely, to the applicant/individual's
prior conviction of a crime, the city manager shall notify the applicant/
individual in writing of the following:
      1.   The grounds and reason for denial;
      2.   The applicable complaint and grievance procedure set forth in
Minnesota statutes section 364.06;
      3.   The earliest date the applicant/individual may reapply for
employment; and
      4.   That all competent evidence of rehabilitation will be considered
upon reapplication. (Ord. 291, 2-15-2011)
CHAPTER 7
HEARINGS
SECTION:
1-7-1: Conduct Of Hearings
1-7-2: Notice
1-7-3: Opportunity To Be Heard
1-7-4: Adoption Of Rules
1-7-5: Record
1-7-1: CONDUCT OF HEARINGS:
Unless otherwise provided in this code, by charter or by law, every public
hearing required to be held on any legislative or administrative matter shall
be conducted in accordance with the provisions of this chapter. (1982 Code §
2.211)
1-7-2: NOTICE:
At least ten (10) days' mailed notice of the time, place and purpose of any
hearing shall be given to all persons entitled to notice. (1982 Code § 2.212)
1-7-3: OPPORTUNITY TO BE HEARD:
At the hearing, each party in interest shall have an opportunity to be heard
and to present evidence relevant to the hearing. (1982 Code § 2.213)
1-7-4: ADOPTION OF RULES:
The city council or other body charged with conduct of any hearing may adopt
rules governing the conduct of hearings, records to be made and such other
matters as it deems necessary for the proper conduct of hearings to be held by
it. (1982 Code § 2.214)
1-7-5: RECORD:
Upon the disposition of any matter after hearing, the body conducting the
hearing shall cause to be prepared a written summary of its findings and
decisions and enter the summary in the official minutes of its meetings. (1982
Code § 2.215)
TITLE 2
BOARDS AND COMMISSIONS
CHAPTER 1
PLANNING COMMISSION 1
SECTION:
2-1-1: Policy
2-1-2: Establishment And Composition
2-1-3: Members Of Commission
2-1-4: Officers
2-1-5: Meetings; Rules; Records
2-1-6: Powers And Duties
2-1-7: Expenditures
 
Notes
1 1. See city charter, chapter two, 2.01, subsections 1) and 2); MSA § 62.354,
  subd. 1.
2-1-1: POLICY:
The city council desires to encourage sound and harmonious growth to the city
and its environment, encourage efficiency and economy in the provision of
facilities and services, ensure maximum return for expenditures of public funds
and avoid error and waste resulting from unplanned and uncoordinated
development. To these ends and for these purposes, the city council finds it
desirable that municipal planning activities be undertaken for guiding the
future development and improvement of the city. (1982 Code § 2.451)
2-1-2: ESTABLISHMENT AND COMPOSITION:
There shall be a planning commission. The planning commission shall be the city
planning agency. The planning commission shall consist of seven (7) members.
Four (4) members shall be appointed by the city council and may be removed by a
five-sixths (5/6) vote of the city council. The city council shall elect one
member of the commission from among its own members. The city manager and the
city attorney shall be ex officio members. (1982 Code §§ 2.452, 2.453)
2-1-3: MEMBERS OF COMMISSION:
   A.   Terms Of Office:
      1.   Appointed Members: Of the members of the commission first appointed,
one shall be appointed for the term of one year, one for the term of two (2)
years, one for the term of three (3) years and one for the term of four years.
Their successors shall be appointed for terms of four (4) years. Both original
and successive appointees shall hold their offices until their successors are
appointed and qualified.
      2.   Ex Officio Members: The terms of the city manager and of the city
attorney shall correspond to their respective official tenures.
      3.   Council Member: The commission member elected by the city council
from its members shall serve at the pleasure of the city council, during the
term of office of the member or such lesser period of time as the city council
may determine in making the election.
      4.   Oath: Every appointed member shall, before entering upon the
discharge of his duties, take an oath that he will faithfully discharge the
duties of his office. (1982 Code § 2.454)
   B.   Vacancies: The chairperson of the commission shall notify the city
council promptly of any vacancy occurring upon the commission. The city council
shall fill any vacancy for the unexpired portion of the original term of the
appointment. (1982 Code § 2.460)
   C.   Compensation: Members of the commission shall receive no salaries or
fees for their services upon the commission. Members shall be allowed necessary
travel and other expenses while on official business for the commission. (1982
Code § 2.462)
   D.   Voting And Other Rights: All members, including the chairperson and the
ex officio members, shall be entitled to vote and shall otherwise have the full
rights and privileges of a member of the commission. (1982 Code § 2.457)
2-1-4: OFFICERS:
The commission shall elect a chairperson and a vice chairperson from among its
appointed members who are not ex officio members and may create such other
offices as it may determine. It shall provide itself with a secretary either by
election from among its members or by appointment of an officer or employee of
the city who is not a member of the commission. (1982 Code § 2.456)
2-1-5: MEETINGS; RULES; RECORDS:
   A.   Meetings: The commission shall hold at least one regular meeting each
month and shall hold any other meetings necessary to the conduct of its
business. (1982 Code § 2.455)
   B.   Rules: The commission shall adopt rules for its governance and for the
transaction of its business. (1982 Code § 2.458)
   C.   Records: The commission shall keep a record of attendance at its
meetings and of its resolutions, transactions, findings and determinations,
showing the vote of each member on each question requiring a vote, including
whether the member was absent or abstained. The records of the commission shall
be a public record. (1982 Code § 2.459)
2-1-6: POWERS AND DUTIES:
In addition to the following, the commission shall be the planning agency. It
shall have the powers and duties given such agencies generally by Minnesota
Statutes Annotated sections 462.351 through 462.364 and other provisions of law
relating to planning agencies. It shall also exercise the duties conferred upon
it by this code. (1982 Code § 2.463)
   A.   Public Hearings On Zoning Ordinances: The commission shall hold a
public hearing upon any proposed zoning ordinance or proposed amendment to a
zoning ordinance, as required by Minnesota Statutes Annotated section 462.357.
(1982 Code § 2.464)
   B.   Approval Of Plats: Any subdivision plat submitted to the city council
for approval shall, prior to final approval, be referred to the commission for
review and recommendation. Any plat so referred shall be returned to the
council by the commission with its recommendations within thirty (30) days. If
the commission fails to act within that time, the city council may then proceed
with its consideration of the plat. (1982 Code § 2.465)
   C.   Annual Report: On or before January 30 of each year the commission
shall submit to the city council a report of its work during the preceding
calendar year. (1982 Code § 2.466)
2-1-7: EXPENDITURES:
Expenditures of the commission shall be within amounts appropriated for the
purpose by the city council. (1982 Code § 2.461)
CHAPTER 2
EMERGENCY MANAGEMENT AGENCY
SECTION:
2-2-1: Agency Created
2-2-2: Director
2-2-3: Organization And Functions
2-2-4: Intergovernmental Arrangements
2-2-5: Emergency Plan
2-2-6: Studies And Reports
2-2-1: AGENCY CREATED:
In accordance with and pursuant to the requirements of Minnesota Statutes
Annotated chapter 12, there shall be an emergency management agency within the
city. (1982 Code § 2.471)
2-2-2: DIRECTOR:
An emergency management director shall be appointed by the mayor for an
indefinite term and may be removed by the mayor at any time. The director shall
receive such compensation as the city council may fix and shall be paid
necessary expenses. The director shall have direct responsibility for the
organization, administration and operation of the emergency services agency,
subject to the direction and control of the city council. (1982 Code § 2.472)
2-2-3: ORGANIZATION AND FUNCTIONS:
The emergency management agency shall be organized into such divisions and
bureaus, consistent with state and local emergency plan, as the director deems
necessary for the efficient performance of local emergency functions during an
emergency. The agency shall perform emergency functions within the city and in
addition shall conduct such functions outside the city as may be required by
law and by this code. (1982 Code § 2.473)
2-2-4: INTERGOVERNMENTAL ARRANGEMENTS:
With the consent of the mayor, the director shall represent the city on any
regional or state organization for emergencies. The director shall develop
proposed mutual aid agreements with other political subdivisions within or
without the state for reciprocal emergency aid and assistance in an emergency
too great to be dealt with unassisted. The director shall present any agreement
to the city council for its action. The agreement shall be consistent with the
emergency plan. During an emergency, the emergency services agency shall render
assistance in accordance with the provisions of the agreement. Any mutual aid
agreement with a political subdivision of another state shall be subject to the
approval of the governor as provided by law. (1982 Code § 2.474)
2-2-5: EMERGENCY PLAN:
The director shall prepare a comprehensive general plan for the emergency
management of the city. The director shall present the plan to the city council
for its approval. The city council shall adopt or reject the plan by
resolution. It may adopt the plan subject to any modifications as it deems fit.
When the city council has adopted the plans, all emergency management services
of the city shall perform the duties and functions assigned by the plan. The
plan may be modified in like manner. The director, as circumstances dictate,
shall from time to time submit proposed modifications of the plan to the city
council for its consideration. (1982 Code § 2.475)
2-2-6: STUDIES AND REPORTS:
The director shall, from time to time, make such studies and surveys relating
to emergency management as the director deems necessary for proper planning of
the continued emergency management of the city. The director shall prepare and
periodically present to the city council a report of activities and
recommendations. (1982 Code § 2.476)
CHAPTER 3
BOARD OF HEALTH
SECTION:
2-3-1: Establishment
2-3-2: Composition
2-3-3: Health Officer
2-3-4: Compensation
2-3-5: Duties Of Board
2-3-6: Right Of Entry
2-3-7: Interference
2-3-1: ESTABLISHMENT:
There shall be a board of health. (1982 Code § 2.431)
2-3-2: COMPOSITION:
The board shall consist of three (3) or more persons. They shall be appointed
by the city council and shall serve at the pleasure of the city council. (1982
Code § 2.432)
2-3-3: HEALTH OFFICER:
At least one member of the board of health shall be a physician, who shall be
the local health officer and executive of the board. The health officer shall
execute the lawful orders of the state and city boards of health and shall have
such powers and duties as are prescribed by law, by regulation of the state
board of health, by charter, by this code and as the city council may
determine. (1982 Code § 2.433)
2-3-4: COMPENSATION:
Members shall receive necessary expenses for their service upon the board as
allowed by the city council. In addition, the physician member shall receive
such compensation as the city council may fix. Members who are not physicians
shall receive no other compensation for their service on the board. (1982 Code
§ 2.434)
2-3-5: DUTIES OF BOARD:
The board of health shall make such investigations and reports and obey such
directions concerning communicable diseases as the state board of health may
require or give. Under the general supervision of the state board of health, it
shall cause all laws and regulations relating to the public health, including
all health regulations included in this code, to be obeyed and enforced. (1982
Code § 2.435)
2-3-6: RIGHT OF ENTRY:
For the purposes of performing their official duties, the health officer and
other members of the board of health shall have the right at any reasonable
hour, and during an emergency at any hour, to enter any building, conveyance or
place where contagion, infection, filth or any other source or cause of
preventable disease exists or is reasonably suspected. (1982 Code § 2.436)
2-3-7: INTERFERENCE:
No person shall obstruct, interfere with, or impede the health officer or board
of health in the performance of official duties or remove any sign posted by
order of the health officer in any area or on any building. (1982 Code § 8.311)
TITLE 3
BUSINESS AND LICENSE REGULATIONS
CHAPTER 1
GENERAL LICENSES AND PERMITS
SECTION:
3-1-1: Application Of Provisions
3-1-2: License Required
3-1-3: License Fees
3-1-4: Bond; Insurance
3-1-5: Issuance
3-1-6: Posting
3-1-7: Term
3-1-8: Duplicate License
3-1-9: Transfer Of License
3-1-10: Renewal
3-1-11: Conditions Of License
3-1-12: Inspection
3-1-13: Misuse Of License
3-1-14: Suspension; Revocation
3-1-1: APPLICATION OF PROVISIONS:
All licenses and permits required by this title shall be governed by the
requirements of this chapter unless otherwise provided by law or in this code.
As used in this title, "license" includes both a license and a permit and
"licensee" includes both a licensee and a permittee. (1982 Code § 7.111)
3-1-2: LICENSE REQUIRED:
   A.   Application:
      1.   Form: Every application shall be made to the city clerk on a form
provided by the city clerk.
      2.   Information: The applicant shall provide all information required by
the application form.
      3.   False Statement: No person shall make a false statement in or
concerning any application. (1982 Code § 7.112)
   B.   Multiple Devices:
      1.   Single License: When multiple tables, machines or other devices of
one kind are licensed at one place of business, the city clerk may issue one
license for all of them and indicate on the license the number of them licensed
under the license.
      2.   Replacement Devices: The licensee may replace any device with
another device without the necessity for transfer of the license.
      3.   Additional Devices: If the license adds to the number of devices
used during the license year, a new license shall be obtained for the
additional devices.
      4.   Separate Licenses: Upon request of the licensee or at the discretion
of the city council or the city clerk, a separate license may instead be issued
for each device. (1982 Code § 7.119)
3-1-3: LICENSE FEES:
   A.   Fee: The application shall be accompanied by payment in full for the
license. Unless a specific fee is provided for, the council shall, by
resolution, establish the fees to be charged for each kind of license. (1982
Code §§ 7.112, 7.116)
   B.   Pro Rata Fees: Unless otherwise specified by law or in this title, if a
portion of the license year has elapsed when an annual license is granted, the
fee shall be one-twelfth (1/12) of the annual fee for each month or fraction of
a month remaining in the license year. No license fee shall be prorated during
the time which a licensee was required to have a license but failed to apply
for one. The council may, by resolution, fix a minimum pro rata fee which is
required for processing the application. (1982 Code § 7.117)
   C.   Refunds:
      1.   Before Issuance: If an application is rejected, the city treasurer
shall refund in full the amount paid, unless the city council, in rejecting the
license, orders that the fee be retained from an applicant making a false
statement in or concerning the application or from an applicant ineligible to
receive a license. (1982 Code § 7.112)
      2.   After Issuance: After issuance, license fees shall not be refunded
in whole or in part unless otherwise specified by law or in this title. (1982
Code § 7.122)
3-1-4: BOND; INSURANCE:
   A.   Surety Bond; Deposit:
      1.   Required: When a bond is required for any license, the applicant
shall file with the city clerk a good and sufficient corporate surety bond, or
in lieu of it, cash in the amount for which the bond is required or United
States government bonds of an equivalent market value.
      2.   Minimum Amount: Except where otherwise provided, the bond or other
security shall be in the sum of at least five thousand dollars ($5,000.00).
      3.   Indemnification: The bond or other security shall be conditioned
that the licensee will comply with all requirements of law and of this code
pertaining to the licensed activity and that the licensee will indemnify the
city and save it harmless from all loss or damage by reason of any act or
omission of the licensee or agents or employees of the licensee. (1982 Code §
7.113)
   B.   Liability Insurance:
      1.   Required: When liability insurance is required for any license, the
licensee shall have on file with the city clerk at all times a currently
effective liability insurance policy issued by a reliable insurance company
authorized to do business in Minnesota.
      2.   Minimum Coverage: Except where otherwise provided, coverage shall be
in the amount of at least one hundred thousand dollars ($100,000.00) for one
person and three hundred thousand dollars ($300,000.00) for more than one
person arising out of a single occurrence.
      3.   Payment: The policy shall specifically provide for the payment by
the insurance company on behalf of the insured of all sums which the insured
shall become obligated to pay by reason of liability imposed upon the insured
for injury or damages to persons other than employees.
      4.   Notice Of Cancellation: The policy shall also provide that no
cancellation of the policy for any cause can be made by either the insured or
the insurance company without first giving ten (10) days' notice to the city in
writing of intention to cancel, addressed to the city clerk.
5. Decreased Coverage: No payment of any claim by the insurance company shall
in any manner decrease the coverage provided for in respect to any other claim
or claims brought against the insured or insurance company thereafter.
6. In Lieu Of Bond: If the insurance policy is made subject to all the
conditions of a bond, it may be filed in lieu of the bond. (1982 Code § 7.114)
C. Approval Of Bond And Insurance:
1. Commencement Of Business: No licensee shall commence business until any
required security, other than cash, and any required insurance policy has been
approved by the city clerk if the license is granted by the city clerk and by
the city council if the license is granted by the city council.
2. Continuance Of Business: No licensee shall continue in business after the
security or insurance is no longer in force.
3. Disapproval: The bond or other security or the insurance policy may be
disapproved upon a finding that the security or policy does not meet
requirements of this code or of law, or that the surety or insurer may become
unable to pay any claim which may arise. (1982 Code § 7.115)
D. Automatic Termination: A license shall automatically terminate upon
termination of any required bond, insurance coverage or other security. (1982
Code § 7.130)
3-1-5: ISSUANCE:
If the license does not require city council approval, the city clerk shall
issue the license upon being satisfied that there is no reason to believe the
public health, safety or welfare would be injured by issuance, and that all
requirements of law and of this code relating to the license have been met. If
the city clerk is not so satisfied, or if council approval is required, the
city clerk shall present the application to the city council for action. The
city clerk shall thereupon issue the license if approval is granted. (1982 Code
§ 7.118)
3-1-6: POSTING:
A. Posting Of License Required: The licensee shall post the license in a
conspicuous place on the premises, in the vehicle or on or near the device to
which the license relates.
B. Multiple Devices: If a license relates to multiple devices at a single
premises, the license shall be posted in a conspicuous place on the premises.
C. Licensed Activity: If the license authorizes the licensee to engage in a
particular line of employment, the license shall be carried on the licensee's
person when the licensee is carrying on the licensed activity, unless the
licensee carries on the activity from a single place of business in the city,
in which case it shall be posted at the place of business.
D. All Other Cases: In all other cases, the license shall be posted at the
licensee's place of business within the city, or such other place in the city
as the city clerk may designate upon the license.
E. Multiple Premises: In addition, if a license relates to multiple premises,
the licensee shall obtain from the city clerk and post a copy of the license in
a conspicuous place on each premises to which the license relates. (1982 Code §
7.126)
F. Copies For Posting: Whenever a licensee is required to post copies of a
license at a place other than where the original license is posted, the city
clerk shall issue a sufficient number of copies for that purpose, marking each
copy with the word "copy" on its face. (1982 Code § 7.120)
3-1-7: TERM:
A. Temporary License: A temporary license shall be issued for a specific
period, which shall be stated on the license, during which a special event is
being held.
B. General Effective Date: Every other license shall become effective when
issued and any required approval of security or insurance is obtained, or such
later date as is requested in the application.
C. Expiration: The license shall expire on December 31 following its
commencement. (1982 Code § 7.123)
3-1-8: DUPLICATE LICENSE:
The city clerk shall issue a duplicate license upon the licensee submitting an
affidavit that the license has been lost, stolen or destroyed. The city clerk
shall make any duplicate with the word "duplicate" on its face. The city
council may, by resolution, establish a fee for issuance of a duplicate
license. (1982 Code § 7.121)
3-1-9: TRANSFER OF LICENSE:
A. Individuals: No license may be transferred to any other person.
B. Premises: When a license relates to specific premises, it may be transferred
to another place only upon request to the city clerk. The city clerk shall
consider the transfer request and approve the transfer or submit it to the city
council in accordance with requirements for issuance of the license.
C. Vehicle; Device: When a license relates to a specific vehicle or device, it
may be transferred to a replacement vehicle or device upon filing with the city
clerk an affidavit of the reasons for the transfer, a description of the
vehicle or device to which it is to be transferred and the disposition of the
vehicle or device from which it is to be transferred.
D. Fee: The city council may, by resolution, impose a transfer fee. (1982 Code
§ 7.125)
3-1-10: RENEWAL:
Applications for renewals of licenses may be made within the three (3) months
prior to expiration. (1982 Code § 7.124)
3-1-11: CONDITIONS OF LICENSE:
Every license shall be subject to the following conditions:
A. The license shall comply with all laws, regulations and provisions of this
code relating to the licensed activity.
B. The act of any employee respecting the licensed activity shall be deemed the
act of the licensee.
C. The licensee shall not permit any gambling upon the licensed premises or by
use of the licensed device or activity.
D. The licensee shall maintain order and shall see to it that the peace is
preserved upon the licensed premises or in the use of any licensed device.
(1982 Code § 7.128)
E. The city of Dawson or the city police department or both shall have the
right to enter, inspect and search the licensed premises without a search and
seizure warrant during the hours in which the licensed premises are open for
the sale of alcoholic beverages.
F. The city of Dawson or the city police department shall conduct at least two
(2) compliance checks each year, and shall issue citations to any licensee
violating the provisions of their license or any relevant provisions of
Minnesota statutes 340A.
G. A violation of a provision of this section is subject to the administrative
penalties set forth in a resolution adopting fees.
H. Any officer of the city police department or any other person employed by
the city, authorized in writing by the city manager, and having authority to
enforce this code, shall, upon determining that there has been a violation,
notify the violator. This notice shall set forth the nature, date and time of
violation, and amount of the scheduled penalty.
I. Once such notice is given, the alleged violator may, within seven (7) days
of the time of issuance of the notice, pay the amount set forth on the schedule
of penalties for the violation, or may request a hearing in writing, as is
provided for hereafter. The penalty may be paid in person or by mail, and
payment shall be deemed to be an admission of the violation.
J. Any person contesting an administrative offense pursuant to this chapter
may, within seven (7) days of the time of issuance of the notice, request a
hearing by a hearing officer who shall forthwith conduct an informal hearing to
determine if a violation has occurred. The hearing officer shall have authority
to dismiss the violation or reduce or waive the penalty. If the violation is
sustained by the hearing officer, the violator shall pay the penalty imposed.
K. In the event a party charged with an administrative offense fails to pay the
penalty, a criminal charge may be brought against the alleged violator in
accordance with applicable statutes. If the penalty is paid or if an individual
is found not to have committed the administrative offense by the hearing
officer, no such charge may be brought by the city for the same violation.
(Ord. 270, 10-21-2008)
3-1-12: INSPECTION:
A. Permitted Entry: The licensee shall permit any law enforcement officer or
health officer or any other duly designated officer or employee of the city
engaged in the performance of official duties with respect to the licensed
activity to enter and inspect the licensed premises and to examine the books
and records of the activity to which the license relates at any time during
which the premises are open for business.
B. Refused Entry: A valid search warrant shall be obtained before conducting
the inspection or examination if the licensee objects to the inspection or
examination. Refusal to permit the inspection or examination is grounds for
suspension or revocation of the license. (1982 Code § 7.127)
3-1-13: MISUSE OF LICENSE:
No person shall lend or give to any other person a license while it is in
effect. No person shall alter, deface or destroy any license while it is in
effect. (1982 Code § 7.129)
3-1-14: SUSPENSION; REVOCATION:
The city council may suspend or revoke any license upon finding that the
licensee has failed to comply with any statute, regulation or provision of this
code relating to the licensed activity, or for any other sufficient cause.
Except when suspension or revocation may be made without hearing, the licensee
shall be granted an opportunity for hearing before decision is made. The notice
of hearing shall state the date, time and place of the hearing and the charges
against the licensee. When the licensee holds more than one license, violation
of any law, regulation or provision respecting any license shall be cause for
suspension or revocation of all other licenses of the same kind issued to the
licensee or upon the premises. A license may be suspended or revoked without
hearing, or with such hearing as conditions warrant, if immediate suspension or
revocation is necessary for protection of the public health, safety or welfare.
In that event, upon demand by the licensee within ten (10) days of the action,
a hearing shall be held as soon as may be done. Licenses may instead be
suspended or revoked in the manner provided by law with respect to any license.
(1982 Code § 7.131)
CHAPTER 2
LIQUOR CONTROL 1
SECTION:
3-2-1: Issuance Of Permits
3-2-2: Permit Fee
3-2-3: Minors
3-2-4: Public Consumption
3-2-5: Restricted Sales
 
Notes
1 1. MSA ch. 340A.
3-2-1: ISSUANCE OF PERMITS:
The city manager and city clerk shall issue the permit when all requirements of
this code and further requirements set by the city council have been complied
with. (Ord. 196, 7-2-1985)
3-2-2: PERMIT FEE:
The city council shall, by motion, establish the fee to be charged. (Ord. 196,
7-2-1985)
3-2-3: MINORS:
No person under the legal age for the purchase of intoxicating beverages shall:
   A.   Misrepresent his or her age for the purpose of obtaining any alcoholic
beverages.
   B.   Purchase or attempt to purchase any alcoholic beverage.
   C.   Induce or attempt to induce another person to purchase any alcoholic
beverage for him.
   D.   Consume any alcoholic beverage unless in the company of his parent or
guardian and unless the consumption is otherwise permitted by law.
   E.   Possess any alcoholic beverage with intent to consume the alcoholic
beverage at a place other than the household of his parent or guardian.
Possession by the person of an alcoholic beverage at a place other than the
household of his parent or guardian shall be prima facie evidence of intent to
consume the alcoholic beverage at a place other than the household of his
parent or guardian. (1982 Code § 6.113)
3-2-4: PUBLIC CONSUMPTION:
No person shall consume or display any alcoholic beverage on any public street,
alley or sidewalk, or in a public park, except the dispensary or other place
where the consumption and display of the alcoholic beverage is lawfully
permitted on the property pursuant to the provisions of this code. (Ord. 196,
7-2-1985)
3-2-5: RESTRICTED SALES:
   A.   Unlicensed Public Places: No person shall display, mix, prepare for
consumption or consume any alcoholic beverage in any place of business, open to
the public for such purposes, which is not licensed for the display,
consumption, sale or furnishing of setups for the alcoholic beverage. (1982
Code § 6.112)
   B.   Softball Fields, Designated Drinking Area: A designated drinking area
is allowed at the Dawson softball fields. Such area shall be marked by
appropriate signs and limited in area by such signs in which the consumption of
alcoholic beverages is lawfully permitted. Such designated drinking area shall
be allowed by motion of the city council. (Ord. 196, 7-2-1985)
      1.   The designated drinking area for the Dawson softball fields listed
in this subsection B may be changed for special events. The change must be made
by permit issued by the city of Dawson and be for the length of the special
event. The permit may be allowed by city staff or by motion of the city
council. Such area shall be marked by appropriate signs and limited in area by
such signs in which the consumption of alcoholic beverages is lawfully
permitted. (Ord. 300, 6-5-2012)
   C.   City Park And Campgrounds:
      1.   City Park: Consumption or display of any alcoholic beverage in the
city park is prohibited except within the shelter house at the city park.
Consumption shall be allowed in the shelter house by permit.
      2.   Campgrounds: Consumption of alcoholic beverages in the campgrounds
at city park is prohibited except if such consumption is by registered campers
and such alcoholic beverage is consumed within the campsite.
   D.   Theodore Christianson Park: Consumption of any alcoholic beverage in
Theodore Christianson Park is prohibited except by permit. (Ord. 196, 7-2-1985)
   E.   Veterans Park: Consumption of any alcoholic beverage in Veterans Park
is prohibited except by permit. (Ord. 279, 7-7-2009)
   F.   Baseball Field, Designated Drinking Area: A designated drinking area is
allowed at the Dawson (Nelson) baseball field in the seating area. Such area
shall be marked by appropriate signs and limited in area by such signs in which
the consumption of alcoholic beverages is lawfully permitted. Sale and
consumption of any alcoholic beverage is also restricted to the times which are
allowed by permit from the city to a lawful vendor. Such designated drinking
area shall be allowed by motion of the city council. (Ord. 294, 12-6-2011)
CHAPTER 2
LIQUOR CONTROL
ARTICLE A. NONINTOXICATING MALT LIQUOR
SECTION:
3-2A-1: Definitions
3-2A-2: State Law Adopted
3-2A-3: License Required
3-2A-4: Types Of Licenses
3-2A-5: Application
3-2A-6: Fees
3-2A-7: Term
3-2A-8: Number Of Licenses
3-2A-9: Eligible Applicants
3-2A-10: Restrictions Upon Premises
3-2A-11: Investigation
3-2A-12: Security
3-2A-13: Hearing
3-2A-14: Issuance
3-2A-15: Hours Of Sale
3-2A-16: Conditions Of License
3-2A-17: Inspection
3-2A-18: Transfer Of License
3-2A-19: Automatic Termination
3-2A-20: Suspension; Revocation
3-2A-1: DEFINITIONS:
In addition to limitations established under state law relating to
nonintoxicating malt liquor, the following terms shall be further limited to
the meaning given to them:
BONA FIDE CLUB: Any nonprofit corporation duly organized under the laws of this
state or by an act of congress for civic, fraternal, social or intellectual
improvement, or any unit of such corporation, which shall for more than one
year have been in existence in the city, and whose affairs and management are
conducted by a board of directors, executive committee or other similar body
chosen by the members at a meeting held for that purpose, none of whose
members, officers, agents or employees are paid directly or indirectly any
compensation by way of profit from the distribution or sale of beverages to the
members of the organization, or to its guests, beyond the amount of such
reasonable salary or wages as may be fixed and voted each year by the directors
or other governing body.
HOTEL: A place of not less than eight (8) sleeping rooms offering to the public
sleeping accommodations for periods of not less than one week, where a
restaurant or dining room is operated in connection therewith offering service
to the public and to those using the hotel accommodations.
RESTAURANT: Any place where preparing and serving lunches or meals to the
public to be consumed on the premises constitutes a major business thereof,
whether called a lunchroom, cafe, restaurant or some other name. (1982 Code §
6.212)
3-2A-2: STATE LAW ADOPTED:
The provisions of this article relating to the retail sale, distribution,
display and consumption of nonintoxicating malt liquor are adopted pursuant to
and supplement Minnesota Statutes Annotated chapter 340A, and establish
additional requirements on the subject as allowed by law. All requirements of
law apply to this article. (1982 Code § 6.211)
3-2A-3: LICENSE REQUIRED:
No person, except a person by law not required to obtain a license from the
city, shall directly or indirectly deal in, sell, offer for sale or keep for
sale any nonintoxicating malt liquor within the city without a license to do so
as provided in this article. (1982 Code § 6.213)
3-2A-4: TYPES OF LICENSES:
Licenses shall be of the following kinds:
   A.   Off Sale Licenses: Off sale licenses shall permit the sale of
nonintoxicating malt liquor at retail in the original package for consumption
off the premises only. (1982 Code § 6.222)
   B.   On Sale Licenses: On sale licenses shall permit sale of nonintoxicating
malt liquor for consumption on the licensed premises only. On sale licenses
shall be granted only to restaurants, hotels, bona fide clubs, and
establishments for the sale of nonintoxicating malt beverages, cigars,
cigarettes, all forms of tobacco, beverages and soft drinks at retail. (1982
Code § 6.223)
   C.   Temporary On Sale Licenses: Temporary on sale licenses shall permit the
temporary sale of nonintoxicating malt liquor to be consumed on the premises
only. Temporary on sale licenses shall be granted only to bona fide clubs and
charitable, religious and nonprofit organizations and shall be subject to such
terms as may be prescribed as a condition of the issuance of the license. (1982
Code § 6.224)
3-2A-5: APPLICATION:
Any person desiring a license shall file with the city clerk a verified written
application in the form prescribed by the city clerk. Every application shall
give such information as the city council or city clerk may require. No person
shall make any false statement in or concerning any application. (1982 Code §
6.233)
3-2A-6: FEES:
   A.   License Fees:
      1.   Established By Resolution: The city council shall, by resolution,
establish the fee to be charged for each kind of license.
      2.   Reduced Fee: The city council may establish a reduced fee for on
sale licenses issued to clubs which sell only to club members and bona fide
guests of club members. (1982 Code § 6.241)
   B.   Pro Rata Fees: If a portion of the license year has elapsed when the
license is granted, the fee shall be one-twelfth (1/12) of the annual fee for
each month or fraction of a month remaining in the license year. The city
council may, by resolution, fix a minimum pro rata fee. (1982 Code § 6.242)
   C.   Payment: Each application for a license shall be accompanied by payment
in full for the license. All license fees shall be paid into the general fund
of the city. If an application is rejected, the city treasurer shall refund in
full the amount paid, unless the city council, in rejecting the license, orders
that the fee, or any part of it, be retained from an applicant making a false
statement in or concerning an application or from an applicant ineligible to
receive a license. (1982 Code § 6.244)
   D.   Refunds:
      1.   Prohibited; Exception: No part of the fee for a license which has
been issued may be refunded, except that the city council may refund any
license fee paid when the licensee ceases business under any of the conditions
for which a refund may by law be allowed.
      2.   Application For Refund: An application for refund must be made to
the city council within thirty (30) days from the happening of the event for
which refund may be made.
      3.   Grant/Denial Of Application: The city council may grant or deny the
refund in its discretion. If the refund is granted, there shall be refunded a
pro rata portion of the fee for the unexpired period of the license, computed
on a monthly basis, excluding the month during which the event occurs from the
computation of the unexpired period of the license.
      4.   Minimum License Fee: In any event, the city shall retain as a
minimum license fee an amount equal to the amount, if any, of any minimum fee
charged for issuance of a prorated license. (1982 Code § 6.245)
3-2A-7: TERM:
A temporary license shall be issued for a specific period, which shall be
stated on the license, during which a special event is being held. Every other
license shall become effective when any required approval of security or
insurance is obtained or such later date as is requested in the application and
shall expire on April 30 following its commencement. (1982 Code § 6.237)
3-2A-8: NUMBER OF LICENSES:
The city council may, by resolution, limit the number of any kind of license
which may be issued. (1982 Code § 6.229)
3-2A-9: ELIGIBLE APPLICANTS:
Applicants for licenses shall meet all requirements of law and of this article
1 . (1982 Code § 6.231)
 
Notes
1 1. MSA § 340A.402.
3-2A-10: RESTRICTIONS UPON PREMISES:
The licensed premises shall meet all requirements of law and of this article.
Licenses shall be granted only for any premises situated and fronting on Sixth
Street between Spruce Street and Walnut Street, or for premises situated and
fronting on Highway 212 or located in block 2, American Legion addition to the
city, or fronting Chestnut Street between Fifth And Sixth Streets in the city,
except that, in the case of bona fide clubs, the city council may, by
resolution, define additional areas of the city where licensed premises may be
situated, and temporary licenses may be issued for any location within the
city. No license shall be granted for any premises on which taxes, assessments
or other financial claims of the city are delinquent. (Ord. 254, 5-20-2003)
3-2A-11: INVESTIGATION:
The city council shall make such investigation of the statements in the
application, the fitness and eligibility of the applicant for a license, the
eligibility and suitability of the premises for a license, whether the public
interest will be served by issuance of the license, and such other matters as
it may deem appropriate. (1982 Code § 6.234)
3-2A-12: SECURITY:
   A.   Bond: Before issuance of a license, the applicant shall file with the
city clerk a good and sufficient corporate surety bond, or, in lieu of it, cash
in the amount for which the bond is required or United States government bonds
of equivalent market value. The bond or security shall be in the sum of at
least three thousand dollars ($3,000,00). The bond or security shall be
conditioned as follows:
      1.   The licensee will pay the city when due all taxes, license fees,
penalties and other charges provided by law.
      2.   The licensee will pay to the principal amount of the bond or
security any damages for death or injury caused by or resulting from the
violation of any provision of law or this article relating to nonintoxicating
malt liquor. (1982 Code § 6.251)
   B.   Liability Insurance:
      1.   Required: In addition to the bond required, the licensee shall have
on file with the city clerk, at all times, a currently effective liability
insurance policy issued by a reliable insurance company authorized to do
business in Minnesota.
      2.   Minimum Coverage: Coverage shall be in the amount of at least one
hundred thousand dollars ($100,000.00) for one person and three hundred
thousand dollars ($300,000.00) for more than one person arising out of a single
occurrence.
      3.   Payments: The policy shall specifically provide for the payment by
the insurance company on behalf of the insured of all sums which the insured
shall become obligated to pay by reason of liability imposed upon the insured
for injury or damages to persons, other than employees.
      4.   Cancellation: The policy shall also provide that no cancellation of
the policy for any cause can be made by either the insured or the insurance
company without first giving ten (10) days' notice to the city in writing of
intention to cancel, addressed to the city clerk.
      5.   Decreased Coverage: No payment of any claim by the insurance company
shall in any manner decrease the coverage provided for in respect to any other
claim or claims brought against the insured or insurance company thereafter.
      6.   In Lieu Of Bond: If the insurance policy is made subject to all the
conditions of a bond under subsection A of this section, it may be filed in
lieu of the bond. (Ord. 201, 4-7-1987)
   C.   Approval Of Bond And Insurance: No licensee shall commence business
until any required security, other than cash, and any required insurance
policy, has been approved by the city council or by such state official as by
law must grant approval. No licensee shall continue in business after the
security or insurance is no longer in force. The bond or other security, or the
insurance policy, may be disapproved upon a finding that the security or policy
does not meet requirements of this code or of law, or that the surety or
insurer may become unable to pay any claims which may arise. (1982 Code §
6.253)
3-2A-13: HEARING 1 :
Opportunity shall be given to any person to be heard for or against the
granting of the license. (1982 Code § 6.235)
 
Notes
1 1. See title 1, chapter 7 of this code.
3-2A-14: ISSUANCE:
After investigation and hearing, the city council shall grant or deny the
application in its discretion. If the application is approved, the city clerk
shall issue the license to the applicant upon the applicant complying with all
requirements of law and of this code relating to issuance of the license. (1982
Code § 6.236)
3-2A-15: HOURS OF SALE:
   A.   Prohibited Sales: No sale of nonintoxicating malt liquor shall be made
at any time that sale is prohibited by law 1 . (1982 Code § 6.262)
   B.   Display And Consumption During Prohibited Hours:
      1.   Display: No licensee shall display nonintoxicating malt liquor to
the public during hours that sale is prohibited.
