      2.   Consumption: Consumption must cease and the premises closed to the
public within one-half (1/2) hour of sales being prohibited.
      3.   Additional Rooms: If the licensee maintains dining rooms, meeting
rooms, or any other rooms on the licensed premises for public use at a time
when sale is prohibited, the part of the premises where the nonintoxicating
malt liquor is kept shall be locked against access to it from the other room or
rooms during the hours that sales are prohibited. (Ord. 196, 7-2-1985)
 
Notes
1 2. MSA § 340A.504.
3-2A-16: CONDITIONS OF LICENSE:
Every license shall be subject to the following conditions:
   A.   All requirements of this article relating to nonintoxicating malt
liquor and all other applicable provisions of this code.
   B.   All requirements imposed by law or other regulation.
   C.   The license shall be posted in a conspicuous place on the premises at
all times.
   D.   No sale may be made to any intoxicated person, to any disorderly
person, or to any person to whom sale is prohibited by law.
   E.   The licensee shall be responsible for the conduct of the licensed
business, and for conditions of sobriety and order in it.
   F.   The act of any employee on the licensed premises shall be deemed the
act of the licensee.
   G.   No licensee not also holding a license or permit to do so shall sell or
permit the display or consumption of any intoxicating liquor on the licensed
premises or serve any liquid for the purpose of mixing with intoxicating liquor
upon the premises. (1982 Code § 6.265)
   H.   No licensee shall sell or serve nonintoxicating malt liquor, or any
other alcoholic beverage, to any person under twenty one (21) years of age, or
permit a person under age twenty one (21) to consume such beverages on the
licensed premises. (Ord. 254, 5-20-2003)
3-2A-17: INSPECTION:
The licensee shall permit any law enforcement officer or health officer or
other duly designated officer or employee of the city to enter and inspect the
premises at any time during which the premises are open for business. (1982
Code § 6.264)
3-2A-18: TRANSFER OF LICENSE:
Each license shall be issued to the applicant only and shall not be
transferable to any other holder. Each license shall be issued for the premises
described in the application and may be transferred to another place only with
the approval of the city council. Any transfer of shares of a corporate
licensee or other than of a publicly held corporation without prior city
council approval is cause for revocation of the license. (1982 Code § 6.261)
3-2A-19: AUTOMATIC TERMINATION:
A license shall automatically terminate upon termination of any required bond,
insurance coverage or other required security. (1982 Code § 6.266)
3-2A-20: SUSPENSION; REVOCATION:
The city council may suspend or revoke any license upon a finding that the
licensee has failed to comply with any statute, regulation or provision of this
code relating to nonintoxicating malt liquor, or for any other sufficient
cause. Except when by law no hearing is required, the licensee shall be granted
an opportunity for hearing before decision is made. The notice of hearing shall
state the date, time and place of the hearing and the charges against the
licensee. (1982 Code § 6.267)
ARTICLE B. INTOXICATING LIQUOR
SECTION:
3-2B-1: State Law Adopted
3-2B-2: License Required
3-2B-3: Types Of Licenses
3-2B-4: Application
3-2B-5: Fees
3-2B-6: Submission Of Information
3-2B-7: Term
3-2B-8: Number Of Licenses
3-2B-9: Eligible Applicants
3-2B-10: Eligible Premises
3-2B-11: Investigation
3-2B-12: Security
3-2B-13: Hearing
3-2B-14: Issuance
3-2B-15: Hours Of Sale
3-2B-16: Conditions Of License
3-2B-17: Inspection
3-2B-18: Transfer Of License
3-2B-19: Automatic Termination
3-2B-20: Suspension; Revocation
3-2B-1: STATE LAW ADOPTED:
The provisions of this article relating to the retail sale, distribution,
display and consumption of intoxicating liquor are adopted pursuant to and
supplement Minnesota Statutes Annotated chapter 340A, and establish additional
requirements on the subject as allowed by law. All requirements of law apply to
this article. (1982 Code § 6.311)
3-2B-2: LICENSE REQUIRED:
No persons except a person by law not required to obtain a license from the
city, shall directly or indirectly deal in, sell, offer for sale or keep for
sale any intoxicating liquor within the city without a license to do so as
provided in this article. (1982 Code § 6.313)
3-2B-3: TYPES OF LICENSES:
Licenses shall be of the following kinds:
   A.   Club On-Sale Licenses: Club on-sale licenses shall permit sale of
intoxicating liquor to club members and bona fide guests of club members only,
for consumption on the licensed premises only. Club on-sale licenses may be
granted only to incorporated congressionally chartered veterans organizations
which have been in existence for at least ten (10) years. (1982 Code §§ 6.321,
6.326)
   B.   On-Sale Liquor Licenses: On-sale liquor licenses shall be issued only
to hotels, restaurants and bowling alleys and shall permit on-sale of liquor
only. "Restaurant" means an eating facility, other than a hotel, under the
control of a single proprietor or manager, where meals are regularly prepared
on the premises and served at tables to the general public. To be a
"restaurant" as defined by this section, an establishment shall have a license
from the state as required by Minnesota statutes section 157.16, as it may be
amended from time to time, and meet the definition of either a "small
establishment", "medium establishment" or "large establishment" as defined in
Minnesota statutes section 157.16 subdivision 3(d), as it may be amended from
time to time. An establishment which serves prepackaged food that receives heat
treatment and is served in the package or frozen pizza that is heated and
served, shall not be considered to be a restaurant for purposes of this chapter
unless it meets the definition of "small establishment", "medium establishment"
or "large establishment" and is licensed as such.
   C.   Off-sale intoxicating liquor licenses, which may be issued only to the
exclusive liquor store. Off-sale intoxicating liquor licenses may be granted
for the sale of liquor in original packages in retail stores for consumption
off or away from the premises where sold. No “off-sale” license shall be issued
to a place where 3.2 percent malt liquor is sold for consumption on the
premises. The city shall be limited to the issuance of once (1) off-sale
license.
(Ord. 271, 11-5-2008; amd. Ord. 326, 5-7-2024)
3-2B-4: APPLICATION:
Any person desiring a license shall file with the city clerk a verified written
application in the form prescribed by the commissioner of public safety. Every
application shall include such additional information as the city council or
city clerk may require. No person shall make any false statement in or
concerning any application. (1982 Code § 6.333)
3-2B-5: FEES:
   A.   License Fees: The city council shall, by resolution, establish the fee
to be charged for each kind of license within the limits of law. (1982 Code §
6.341)
   B.   Pro Rata Fees: If a portion of the license year has elapsed when the
license is granted, the fee shall be one-twelfth (1/12) of the annual fee for
each month or fraction of a month remaining in the license year. The city
council may, by resolution, fix a minimum pro rata fee. (1982 Code § 6.342)
   C.   Payment: Each application for a license shall be accompanied by payment
in full for the license. All license fees shall be paid into the general fund
of the city. If an application is rejected, the city treasurer shall refund in
full the amount paid, unless the city council, in rejecting the license, orders
that the fee, or any part of it, be retained from an applicant making a false
statement in or concerning an application or from an applicant ineligible to
receive a license. (1982 Code § 6.344)
   D.   Refunds:
      1.   Prohibited; Exception: No part of the fee for a license which has
been issued may be refunded, except that the city council may refund any
license fee paid when the licensee ceases business under any of the conditions
for which a refund may by law be allowed.
      2.   Application For Refund: An application for refund must be made to
the city council within thirty (30) days from the happening of the event for
which refund may be made.
      3.   Grant/Denial Of Application: The city council may grant or deny the
refund in its discretion. If the refund is granted, there shall be refunded a
pro rata portion of the fee for the unexpired period of the license, computed
on a monthly basis, excluding the month during which the event occurs from the
computation of the unexpired period of the license.
      4.   Minimum License Fee: In any event, the city shall retain as a
minimum license fee an amount equal to the amount, if any, of any minimum fee
charged for issuance of a prorated license. (1982 Code § 6.345)
3-2B-6: SUBMISSION OF INFORMATION:
The city clerk shall, within the time required by law, submit to the
commissioner of public safety, or such other official as may be required, any
license, license application or any information concerning any license required
by law to be submitted to that official. (1982 Code § 6.314)
3-2B-7: TERM:
Every license shall become effective when any required approval of security or
insurance is obtained or such later date as is requested in the application.
The license shall expire on April 30 following its commencement. (1982 Code §
6.337)
3-2B-8: NUMBER OF LICENSES:
Within any limits established by law, the city council may, by resolution,
limit the number of any kind of license which may be issued. (1982 Code §
6.329)
3-2B-9: ELIGIBLE APPLICANTS:
Applicants for licenses shall meet all requirements of law and of this article.
(1982 Code § 6.331)
3-2B-10: ELIGIBLE PREMISES:
The licensed premises shall meet all requirements of law and of this article.
No license shall be granted for any premises on which taxes, assessments or
other financial claims of the city are delinquent. (1982 Code § 6.332)
3-2B-11: INVESTIGATION:
The city council shall make such investigation of the statements in the
application, the fitness and eligibility of the applicant for a license, the
eligibility and suitability of the premises for a license, whether the public
interest will be served by issuance of the license, and such other matters as
it may deem appropriate or as may be provided for by law. (1982 Code § 6.334)
3-2B-12: SECURITY:
   A.   Bond: Before issuance of a license, the applicant shall file with the
city clerk a good and sufficient corporate surety bond, or, in lieu of it, cash
in the amount for which the bond is required or United States government bonds
of equivalent market value. The bond or security shall be in the sum of at
least three thousand dollars ($3,000.00). It shall be conditioned as is
provided by law and shall meet all requirements of law. (1982 Code § 6.351)
   B.   Liability Insurance:
      1.   Required: In addition to the bond required, the licensee shall have
on file with the city clerk at all times a currently effective liability
insurance policy issued by a reliable insurance company licensed to do business
in Minnesota.
      2.   Minimum Coverage: Coverage shall be in the amount of at least one
hundred thousand dollars ($100,000.00) for one person and three hundred
thousand dollars ($300,000.00) for more than one person arising out of a single
occurrence.
      3.   Compliance: The policy shall include all of the provisions and be
subject to all of the requirements of Minnesota Statutes Annotated section
340.412 relating to such policies.
      4.   In Lieu Of Bond: If the insurance policy is made subject to all of
the conditions of a bond under state law, the policy may be filed in lieu of
the bond required under subsection A of this section. (1982 Code § 6.352)
   C.   Approval Of Bond And Insurance: No licensee shall commence business
until any required security, other than cash, and any required insurance
policy, has been approved by the city council or by such state official as by
law must grant approval. No licensee shall continue in business after the
security or insurance is no longer in force. The bond or other security, or the
insurance policy, may be disapproved upon a finding that the security or policy
does not meet requirements of this code or of law, or that the surety or
insurer may become unable to pay any claims which may arise. (1982 Code §
6.353)
3-2B-13: HEARING 1 :
Opportunity shall be given for any person to be heard for or against the
granting of the license. (1982 Code § 6.335)
 
Notes
1 1. See title 1, chapter 7 of this code.
3-2B-14: ISSUANCE:
After investigation and hearing, the city council shall grant or deny the
application in its discretion. If the application is approved, the city clerk
shall issue the license to the applicant upon the applicant complying with all
requirements of law and of this chapter relating to issuance of the license. If
any license, or the security or insurance for any license, is required by law
to be approved by the commissioner of public safety or any other official, the
license shall not become effective until approval is granted. (1982 Code §
6.336)
3-2B-15: HOURS OF SALE:
   A.   Prohibited Sales: No sale of intoxicating liquor shall be made at any
time that sale is prohibited by law. (1982 Code § 6.362)
   B.   Display And Consumption During Prohibited Hours:
      1.   Display: No licensee shall display intoxicating liquor to the public
during hours that sale is prohibited.
      2.   Consumption: Consumption must cease and the premises closed to the
public within one-half (1/2) hour of sales being prohibited.
      3.   Additional Rooms: If the licensee maintains dining rooms, meeting
rooms, or any other rooms on the licensed premises for public use at a time
when sale is prohibited, the part of the premises where the intoxicating liquor
is kept shall be locked against access to it from the other room or rooms
during the hours that sales are prohibited. (Ord. 196, 7-2-1985)
3-2B-16: CONDITIONS OF LICENSE:
Every license shall be subject to the following conditions:
   A.   All requirements of this article relating to intoxicating liquor, and
all other applicable provisions of this code.
   B.   All requirements imposed by law or regulation.
   C.   The license shall be posted in a conspicuous place on the premises at
all times.
   D.   No sale may be made to any intoxicated persons to any disorderly
person, or to any person to whom sale is prohibited by law.
   E.   The licensee shall be responsible for the conduct of the licensed
business and for conditions of sobriety and order in it.
   F.   The act of any employee on the licensed premises shall be deemed the
act of the licensee.
   G.   No licensee not also holding a license or permit to do so shall sell or
permit the display or consumption of any nonintoxicating malt liquor on the
licensed premises or serve any liquid for the purpose of mixing with
intoxicating liquor upon the premises. (1982 Code § 6.365)
   H.   No licensee shall sell or serve intoxicating liquor, or any other
alcoholic beverage, to any person under twenty one (21) years of age, or permit
a person under age twenty one (21) to consume such beverages on the licensed
premises. (1982 Code § 6.365; amd. 2005 Code)
3-2B-17: INSPECTION:
The licensee shall permit any law enforcement officer or health officer or
other duly designated officer or employee of the city to enter and inspect the
premises at any time during which the premises are open for business. (1982
Code § 6.364)
3-2B-18: TRANSFER OF LICENSE:
Each license shall be issued to the applicant only and shall not be
transferable to any other holder. Each license shall be issued for the premises
described in the application and may be transferred to another place only with
the approval of the city council. Any transfer of shares of a corporate
licensee, other than of a publicly held corporation, shall be deemed a transfer
of the license. A transfer of shares, other than of a publicly held
corporation, without prior council approval is cause for revocation of the
license. (1982 Code § 6.361)
3-2B-19: AUTOMATIC TERMINATION:
A license shall automatically terminate upon termination of any required bond,
insurance coverage or other required security. (1982 Code § 6.366)
3-2B-20: SUSPENSION; REVOCATION:
The city council may suspend or revoke any license upon finding that the
licensee has failed to comply with any statute, regulation or provision of this
code relating to intoxicating liquor, or for any other sufficient cause. Except
when by law no hearing is required, the licensee shall be granted an
opportunity for hearing before decision in made. The notice of hearing shall
state the date, time and place of the hearing and the charges against the
licensee. (1982 Code § 6.367)
ARTICLE C. WINE 1
SECTION:
3-2C-1: State Law Adopted
3-2C-2: License Required
3-2C-3: On-Sale Wine Licenses
3-2C-4: Application
3-2C-5: Fees
3-2C-6: Eligible Applicants
3-2C-7: Restrictions On Premises
3-2C-8: Security
3-2C-9: Investigation; Hearing; Issuance
3-2C-10: Display During Prohibited Hours
3-2C-11: Conditions Of License
3-2C-12: Inspection
3-2C-13: Transfer Of License
3-2C-14: Suspension; Revocation
3-2C-15: Penalty
 
Notes
1 1. MSA § 340A.404, subd. 5.
3-2C-1: STATE LAW ADOPTED:
Provisions of Minnesota Statutes Annotated chapter 340A, relating to the
definition of terms, licensing, consumption, sales, conditions of bonds, of
licenses, hours of sale, and all other matters pertaining to the retail sale,
distribution, and consumption of intoxicating liquor insofar as they are
applicable to wine licenses authorizing the sale of wine not exceeding fourteen
percent (14%) alcohol by volume for consumption on the licensed premises only
in conjunction with the sale of food, are adopted and made a part of this
article as if set out in full. (Ord. 200, 3-3-1987)
3-2C-2: LICENSE REQUIRED:
   A.   On-Sale License: No person, except a wholesaler or manufacturer to the
extent authorized under state license, and the municipal liquor dispensary,
shall directly or indirectly deal in, sell, or keep for sale in the city any
wine not exceeding fourteen percent (14%) alcohol by volume without an on-sale
license. (Ord. 200, 3-3-1987)
   B.   Intoxicating Malt Liquor Sales: Pursuant to Minnesota Statutes
Annotated 340A.404, subdivision 5, the city authorizes a holder of an on-sale
wine license issued pursuant to subsection A of this section, who is also
licensed to sell 3.2 percent malt liquors at on-sale pursuant to Minnesota
Statutes Annotated section 340A.411, and whose gross receipts are at least
sixty percent (60%) attributable to the sale of food, may sell intoxicating
malt liquors at on-sale without an additional license. (Ord. 242, 4-17-2001)
3-2C-3: ON-SALE WINE LICENSES:
On-sale wine licenses shall be issued only to hotels, restaurants and bowling
alleys and shall permit on-sale of wine only. "Restaurant" means an eating
facility, other than a hotel, under the control of a single proprietor or
manager, where meals are regularly prepared on the premises and served at
tables to the general public. To be a "restaurant" as defined by this section,
an establishment shall have a license from the state as required by Minnesota
statutes section 157.16, as it may be amended from time to time, and meet the
definition of either a "small establishment", "medium establishment" or "large
establishment" as defined in Minnesota statutes section 157.16 subdivision 3
(d), as it may be amended from time to time. An establishment which serves
prepackaged food that receives heat treatment and is served in the package or
frozen pizza that is heated and served, shall not be considered to be a
restaurant for purposes of this chapter unless it meets the definition of
"small establishment", "medium establishment" or "large establishment" and is
licensed as such. (Ord. 280, 12-15-2009)
3-2C-4: APPLICATION:
   A.   Required Information: Every applicant for an on sale wine license shall
state:
      1.   The name of the applicant;
      2.   His age;
      3.   Representations as to his character, with such references as the
city council may require;
      4.   His citizenship;
      5.   The restaurant in connection with which the proposed license will
operate and its location;
      6.   Whether the applicant is owner and operator of the restaurant;
      7.   How long he has been in the restaurant business at that place; and
      8.   Such other information as the city council may require from time to
time.
   B.   Form: In addition to containing such information, the application shall
be in the form prescribed by the commissioner of public safety and shall be
verified and filed with the city clerk.
   C.   False Statement: No person shall make a false statement in an
application. (Ord. 200, 3-3-1987)
3-2C-5: FEES:
   A.   License Fees: The annual fee for a wine license is sixty dollars
($60.00).
   B.   Term; Pro Rata Fees: Each license shall be issued for a period of one
year, except that if the application is made during the license year, a license
may be issued for the remainder of the year for a pro rata fee, with an
unexpired fraction of a month being counted as one month. Every license shall
expire on April 30 following its commencement.
   C.   Payment; Application Fee Refund: Each application for a wine license
shall be accompanied by payment in full for the license. All license fees shall
be paid into the general fund of the city. If an application is rejected, the
treasurer shall refund in full the amount paid, unless the city council, in
rejecting the license, orders that the fee, or any part of it, be retained from
an applicant making a false statement in or concerning an application or from
an applicant ineligible to receive a license.
   D.   Refunds After License Issued:
      1.   Prohibited; Exception: No part of the fee for a license which has
been issued may be refunded, except that the city council may refund any
license fee paid when the licensee ceases business under any of the conditions
for which a refund may by law be allowed.
      2.   Application For Refund: An application for refund must be made to
the city council within thirty (30) days from the happening of the event for
which refund may be made.
      3.   Grant/Denial Of Application: The city council may grant or deny the
refund in its discretion. If the refund is granted, there shall be refunded a
pro rata portion of the fee for the unexpired period of the license, computed
on a monthly basis, excluding the month during which the event occurs from the
computation of the unexpired period of the license.
      4.   Minimum License Fee: In any event, the city shall retain as a
minimum license fee an amount equal to the amount, if any, of any minimum fee
charged for issuance of a prorated license. (Ord. 200, 3-3-1987)
3-2C-6: ELIGIBLE APPLICANTS:
No wine license shall be granted to any person made ineligible for such license
by state law. (Ord. 200, 3-3-1987)
3-2C-7: RESTRICTIONS ON PREMISES:
No wine license shall be issued for any restaurant ineligible for such a
license under state law. No license shall be granted for any premises which is
not situated and fronting on Sixth Street between Spruce Street and Walnut
Street or for premises situated and fronting on Highway 212 or located in block
2, American Legion addition to the city or fronting Chestnut Street between
Fifth And Sixth Streets in the city, except that in the case of bona fide
clubs, the city council may, by resolution, define additional areas of the city
where licensed premises may be situated and temporary licenses may be issued
for any location within the city. No license shall be granted for any premises
on which taxes, assessments or other financial claims of the city are
delinquent. (Ord. 254, 5-20-2003)
   A.   Distance From School Or Church: No license shall be granted for a
building within three hundred feet (300') of any school or within three hundred
feet (300') of any church.
   B.   Delinquent Taxes And Charges: No license shall be granted for operation
on any premises on which taxes, assessments, or other financial claims of the
city are delinquent and unpaid. (Ord. 200, 3-3-1987)
3-2C-8: SECURITY:
   A.   Bond: Each application for a license shall be accompanied by a surety
bond or, in lieu thereof, cash or United States government bonds of equivalent
market value as provided in Minnesota Statutes Annotated section 340A.409. Such
surety bond or other security shall be in the sum of three thousand dollars
($3,000.00) for an application for an on sale wine license.
   B.   Liability Insurance:
      1.   Required; Minimum Coverage: Prior to the issuance of a wine license,
the applicant shall file with the city clerk a liability insurance policy in
the amount of one hundred thousand dollars ($100,000.00) coverage for one
person and three hundred thousand dollars ($300,000.00) coverage for more than
one person and shall comply with the provisions of Minnesota Statutes Annotated
section 340A.409 relating to liability insurance policies.
      2.   In Lieu Of Bond: If a liability insurance policy is made subject to
all the conditions of a bond under that statute, the policy may be accepted by
the city council in lieu of the bond required under subsection A of this
section.
   C.   Approval Of Bond And Insurance: The security offered under this section
shall be approved by the city council and the commissioner of public safety.
Surety bonds and liability insurance policies shall be approved as to form by
the city attorney. Operation of a licensed business without having on file with
the city at all times effective security as required in subsections A and B of
this section is a cause for revocation of the license. (Ord. 200, 3-3-1987)
3-2C-9: INVESTIGATION; HEARING; ISSUANCE:
The city council shall investigate all facts set out in the application.
Opportunity shall be given to any person to be heard for or against the
granting of the license. After the investigation and hearing, the city council
shall, in its discretion, grant or refuse the application. No wine license
shall become effective until it, together with the security furnished by the
applicant, has been approved by the commissioner of public safety. (Ord. 200,
3-3-1987)
3-2C-10: DISPLAY DURING PROHIBITED HOURS:
No licensee shall display wine to the public during hours when the sale of wine
is prohibited. (Ord. 200, 3-3-1987)
3-2C-11: CONDITIONS OF LICENSE:
Every license is subject to the conditions in the following subsections and all
other provisions of this article and of any other applicable ordinance, state
law or regulation:
   A.   Every licensee is responsible for the conduct of his place of business
and the conditions of sobriety and order in it.
   B.   The act of any employee on the licensed premised authorized to sell
intoxicating liquor there is deemed the act of the licensee as well, and the
licensee shall be liable to all penalties provided by this article and the law
equally with the employee. (Ord. 200, 3-3-1987)
3-2C-12: INSPECTION:
Every licensee shall allow any peace officer, health officer, or properly
designated officer or employee of the city to enter, inspect, and search the
premises of the licensee during business hours without a warrant. (Ord. 200, 3-
3-1987)
3-2C-13: TRANSFER OF LICENSE:
Each license shall be issued only to the applicant and for the premises
described in the application. No license may be transferred to another person
or place without city council approval. Any transfer of stock of a corporate
licensee is deemed a transfer of the license and a transfer of stock without
prior city council approval is a ground for revocation of the license. (Ord.
200, 3-3-1987)
3-2C-14: SUSPENSION; REVOCATION:
The city council may either suspend for not to exceed sixty (60) days or revoke
any on sale wine license upon a finding that the licensee has failed to comply
with any applicable statute, regulation or ordinance relating to intoxicating
liquor. No suspension or revocation shall take effect until the licensee has
been afforded an opportunity for a hearing pursuant to Minnesota statutes.
(Ord. 200, 3-3-1987)
3-2C-15: PENALTY:
Any person violating any provision of this article is guilty of a misdemeanor
and, upon conviction, shall be punished as provided in the general penalty in
subsection 1-4-1B of this code, plus the cost of prosecution in any case. (Ord.
200, 3-3-1987; amd. 2005 Code)
ARTICLE D. MUNICIPAL LIQUOR DISPENSARY
SECTION:
3-2D-1: Dispensary Continued
3-2D-2: Location
3-2D-3: Manager
3-2D-4: Additional Employees
3-2D-5: Revenues
3-2D-6: Hours
3-2D-7: Restrictions
3-2D-1: DISPENSARY CONTINUED:
The municipal liquor dispensary heretofore established is hereby continued for
the off sale of intoxicating liquor. No person other than a duly acting
employee of the dispensary shall sell intoxicating liquor at off sale in the
city unless allowed to do so by law or pursuant to other provisions of this
code. (1982 Code § 6.411)
3-2D-2: LOCATION:
The dispensary shall be located at such suitable place in the city as the city
council determines. No premises upon which taxes, assessments or other
financial claims of the city are delinquent shall be leased for dispensary
purposes. (1982 Code § 6.412)
3-2D-3: MANAGER:
   A.   Selection: The dispensary shall be in the immediate charge of a liquor
store manager elected by the city council.
   B.   Compensation: The manager shall be paid such compensation as is fixed
by the city council, and shall serve at the pleasure of the city council. (1982
Code § 6.413)
   C.   Duties: The manager shall operate the dispensary under the direction of
the city manager. The manager shall perform such duties in connection with the
dispensary as may be required by the city council or the city manager. The
manager shall conduct the dispensary in full compliance with this code and with
all laws relating to the sale and consumption of intoxicating liquor. (1982
Code § 6.414)
   D.   Bond: The manager shall furnish a surety bond to the city, conditioned
upon the faithful discharge of the duties of the manager, in such sum as the
city council may require. The bond premium shall be paid by the city. (1982
Code § 6.416)
3-2D-4: ADDITIONAL EMPLOYEES:
   A.   Employment: The city council may also employ such additional employees
as may be required for the dispensary.
   B.   Compensation: All such employees shall be paid such compensation as is
fixed by the city council and shall serve at the pleasure of the city council.
   C.   Age Requirement: No person under nineteen (19) years of age shall be
employed in the dispensary. (1982 Code § 6.415)
   D.   Bond: The council, at its discretion, may require other employees to
furnish bond. The bond premium shall be paid by the city. (1982 Code § 6.416)
3-2D-5: REVENUES:
   A.   Dispensary Fund: The municipal liquor dispensary fund is hereby
continued.
      1.   Receipts; Disbursements: All revenues received from operation of the
dispensary shall be deposited into such fund and all ordinary operating
expenses shall be paid from it.
      2.   Borrowing From General Fund: Any amount which it may be necessary to
borrow from the general fund of the city in connection with the dispensary
shall be reimbursed to the general fund out of the first available monies
coming into the dispensary fund thereafter.
      3.   Surplus Funds: Surpluses in the dispensary fund may be transferred
to the general fund or to any other appropriate fund by the city by resolution
of the council and expended for any municipal purpose, or may be expended for
hospital purposes as allowed by charter 1 . (1982 Code § 6.417)
   B.   Handling Of Monies: Handling of dispensary receipts and disbursements
shall comply with the procedures prescribed by law or by charter for receipt
and disbursement of city funds generally. (1982 Code § 6.418)
   C.   Audit: The city council shall provide as soon as possible following the
close of each fiscal year for an audit of the accounts of the municipal liquor
dispensary for that fiscal year. (1982 Code § 6.419)
 
Notes
1 1. See city charter, chapter seven, section 7.13.
3-2D-6: HOURS:
No sale shall be made at any time that sale of intoxicating liquor is
prohibited by law. The dispensary shall not be open for business during any
time that such sales are prohibited. (1982 Code § 6.420)
3-2D-7: RESTRICTIONS:
The following restrictions apply to the dispensary:
   A.   Employees shall comply with all requirements of law and of this code.
   B.   No sale shall be made on credit. (1982 Code § 6.421)
   C.   No sale shall be made to a person under age twenty one (21), an
intoxicated person, or any other person to whom sale is prohibited.
   D.   No person who is under age twenty one (21), intoxicated or disorderly
shall be permitted to remain in the dispensary, nor shall any person be
permitted to loiter in the dispensary.
   E.   No person shall be permitted to gamble in the dispensary. (1982 Code §
6.421; amd. 2005 Code)
CHAPTER 3
AMUSEMENT PLACES AND DEVICES
SECTION:
3-3-1: Amusement Devices
3-3-2: Pool Halls
3-3-3: Bowling Alleys
3-3-4: Traveling Exhibitions
3-3-5: Motion Picture Theaters
3-3-6: Roller Skating Rinks
3-3-7: Public Dances And Dancing Places
3-3-1: AMUSEMENT DEVICES 1 :
   A.   Definition: As used in this section, "coin operated amusement device"
includes any machine, screen or other device which, upon the insertion of a
coin, token or slug, or upon payment of a price, directly or indirectly, for
the privilege, may be operated by one or more players for amusement by
manipulating special equipment on or in the device, the object of which is to
secure a special number or score, or a high or low total score. It does not
include any device required to be licensed under any other provision of this
title.
   B.   Licensed Required: No person shall keep within the city for public use
for which any money is charged, directly or indirectly, any coin operated
amusement device without having first obtained a license to do so. (1982 Code §
7.211)
 
Notes
1 1. See chapter 9 of this title and title 11, chapter 2 of this code for
  provisions regarding sexually oriented businesses.
3-3-2: POOL HALLS:
No person shall keep within the city for public use for which any money is
charged, directly or indirectly any billiard table, pool table or similar
device without having first obtained a license to do so. (1982 Code § 7.221)
3-3-3: BOWLING ALLEYS:
No person shall keep within the city for public use for which any money is
charged, directly or indirectly, any bowling alley without having first
obtained a license to do so. (1982 Code § 7.231)
3-3-4: TRAVELING EXHIBITIONS:
   A.   License Required: No person except a bona fide club or a nonprofit
organization shall make or exhibit any traveling show, caravan, circus, play,
game, concert, performance or other exhibition whatsoever within the city for
which, directly or indirectly, money is received or charged, including money
received through donations, without having first obtained a license to do so.
(1982 Code § 7.241)
   B.   Application: Each application shall state the full name and address of
the person making the application, the full name and address of the owner or
sponsor of the traveling exhibition, the place at which the traveling
exhibition is to be conducted, the name and address of the person responsible
for the conduct of the traveling exhibition, and such other information as may
be required on the application form. (1982 Code § 7.242)
   C.   Issuance: The city council shall approve issuance of the license upon
being satisfied that all requirements of law and of this code have been met and
that the public health, safety and welfare will not be adversely affected if
the license is granted. (1982 Code § 7.243)
   D.   Conditions Of License: The licensee shall see to it that the exhibition
is conducted in an orderly manner at all times. The license shall be subject to
such additional conditions as the city council may impose for the protection of
public health, safety and welfare. (1982 Code § 7.244)
3-3-5: MOTION PICTURE THEATERS:
No person shall, within the city, operate any motion picture theater which is
open to the public for which an admission fee is charged, directly or
indirectly, without having first obtained a license to do so. (1982 Code §
7.251)
3-3-6: ROLLER SKATING RINKS:
No person shall keep, maintain or operate for hire within the city any roller
skating rink, whether indoors or outdoors, which is open to the public for
which an admission fee is charged, directly or indirectly, without having first
obtained a license to do so. (1982 Code § 7.261)
3-3-7: PUBLIC DANCES AND DANCING PLACES:
   A.   Permit Required: No person shall give, hold or conduct a public dance
or operate a public dancing place within the city unless the owner or
proprietor of the public dancing place, or the person giving the dance and in
charge of it, has first obtained a permit to do so. (1982 Code § 7.271; amd.
2005 Code)
   B.   Application: Application shall be made to the city clerk as provided by
law. The applicant shall give such information in the application as is
required by law or as the city council or the city clerk may otherwise require.
Applicant, and the premises to which the permit relates, shall meet all
requirements of law. (1982 Code § 7.272)
   C.   Fees:
      1.   Established By Resolution: The city council shall, by resolution,
establish fees to be charged for permits for public dances and public dancing
places.
      2.   Reduced Fees: In doing so, it may provide for a reduced fee, or no
fee, if the dance or dancing place is not for profit, or if the dance is given
for the benefit of a nonprofit organization or charity.
      3.   Increased Fee: The council may also provide for an increased fee for
any application not submitted in time to be considered at a regular meeting of
council or not submitted such other period of time in advance as the city
council may determine.
      4.   Additional Costs: In addition, the applicant shall pay the expense
of any investigation conducted by the city respecting the application and the
fees and expenses of any officer of the law required to attend at the dance.
All fees shall be paid prior to issuance of the permit. (1982 Code § 7.273)
   D.   Issuance: Permits shall be considered as provided by law, and, if
issued, shall be subject to such conditions as may be provided by law and as
the city council may otherwise impose for the protection of public health,
safety and welfare. (1982 Code § 7.274)
   E.   Term: A dance permit may be issued for one or more public dances and
shall be valid for such days and times as may be specified in the permit. A
permit for a public dancing place shall expire on December 31 following its
issuance. (1982 Code § 7.275)
CHAPTER 4
REFUSE COLLECTORS
SECTION:
3-4-1: License Required
3-4-2: Application
3-4-3: Fees
3-4-4: Bond; Insurance
3-4-5: Approval; Issuance
3-4-6: Term
3-4-7: Additional Rules
3-4-1: LICENSE REQUIRED:
No person, other than employees of the municipal refuse collection system, in
the course of their work, whether or not for hire, shall collect or remove any
refuse from the premises of another, or transport the same over any street,
alley, or other public way, within the city, without first having obtained a
license to do so. (1982 Code § 8.471)
3-4-2: APPLICATION:
Any person desiring a license shall file an application with the city clerk in
the form prescribed by the city clerk. The application shall state the name,
address and age of the applicant, the type of equipment to be used, a schedule
of rates to be charged for the services provided, the place to which the refuse
is to be hauled and such other information as the city council may require. No
person shall make a false statement on any application. (1982 Code § 8.472)
3-4-3: FEES:
The city council shall, by resolution, establish the license fees to be
charged. (1982 Code § 8.473)
3-4-4: BOND; INSURANCE:
   A.   Bond: When the city council deems it reasonably necessary in view of
the applicant's proposed services, equipment, experience and training, the city
council may require as a condition of the issuance of a license that the
applicant furnish bond in an amount determined by the city council for the
performance of the licensed activity in accordance with all provisions of law
and administrative regulation and of this code.
   B.   Insurance: The council may, in addition to or in lieu of bond, require
that a licensee file with the city clerk a policy of insurance in such kinds
and amounts as the city council may determine. (1982 Code § 8.474)
3-4-5: APPROVAL; ISSUANCE:
   A.   Investigation: The city council may make such investigation of the
fitness of any applicant for a license as it deems appropriate.
   B.   Denial Of Application: The city council may deny a license to any
applicant when it finds that the applicant lacks sufficient training
experience, equipment or employees to provide the services proposed at the
rates proposed in a safe, sanitary or efficient manner, or if it finds that no
need exists for the service proposed.
   C.   Approval Of Application; Issuance: If the city council approves
issuance of a license, the city clerk shall issue the license upon the
applicant paying the necessary fees and filing with the city clerk any required
bond or policy of insurance. (1982 Code § 8.475)
3-4-6: TERM:
Licenses shall be issued for one year. (1982 Code § 8.476)
3-4-7: ADDITIONAL RULES:
The city council may, by resolution, provide such additional rules and
regulations as may be proper to carry out and enforce the provisions of this
chapter. (1982 Code § 8.477)
CHAPTER 5
PEDDLERS, HAWKERS AND TRANSIENT MERCHANTS
SECTION:
3-5-1: Peddlers And Hawkers
3-5-2: Transient Merchants
3-5-1: PEDDLERS AND HAWKERS:
   A.   License Required: No person shall go in or upon any private residence
or other private property within the city for the purpose of selling or
soliciting orders for the sale of any goods, wares or merchandise without
having first obtained a license to do so. Pursuant to Minnesota constitution,
article 13, section 7, no person shall be required to obtain a license to sell
or peddle the products of the farm or garden occupied and cultivated by him or
her. (1982 Code § 7.321)
   B.   Posted Premises: No person shall sell or solicit orders for the sale of
any goods, wares or merchandise at any private premises conspicuously posted
near the entrance with a sign stating "No Peddlers" or any other message
indicating that the occupants do not want to have any peddler or solicitor call
upon them, or to otherwise have their privacy disturbed. (1982 Code § 7.322)
3-5-2: TRANSIENT MERCHANTS:
No transient merchant shall operate in the city without having first obtained a
license to do so. No license shall be required of any transient merchant
excepted by law from having to obtain any transient merchant's license also
required by law. (1982 Code § 7.331)
CHAPTER 6
CIGARETTE SALES
SECTION:
3-6-1: License Required
3-6-2: Restrictions
3-6-3: Conditions Of License
3-6-4: Blind Persons
3-6-1: LICENSE REQUIRED:
No person shall, directly or indirectly, or by means of any device, keep for
retail sales sell at retail or otherwise furnish to another for any
consideration, whether directly or indirectly, any cigarette, cigarette paper,
or cigarette wrapper within the city without having first obtained a license to
do so. (1982 Code § 7.311)
3-6-2: RESTRICTIONS:
The following restrictions shall apply to the issuance of a license:
   A.   Moral Character Of Applicant: No license shall be issued except to a
person of good moral character.
   B.   Place Of Business; Temporary License: No license shall be issued to an
applicant for sale of cigarettes at any place other than the applicant's
established place of business, nor shall a license be issued for the sale of
cigarettes at a movable place of business. However, a temporary license may be
issued at a temporary place of business for the duration of a special event
only.
   C.   Individual Premises: Each license shall be issued for the sale of
cigarettes at only one place of business.
   D.   Proximity To Church Or School: No license, other than a temporary
license, shall be issued for any business within fifty feet (50') of any public
school or within fifty feet (50') of any church, as measured by the shortest
distance between the nearest points of the business and the school or church
building. (1982 Code § 7.312)
3-6-3: CONDITIONS OF LICENSE:
In addition to conditions established elsewhere in this code, every license
shall be subject to the following conditions:
   A.   Harmful Substances: No licensee shall keep for sale, sell or give away
any cigarette containing opium, morphine, Jimson weed, belladonna, strychnia,
cocaine, marijuana or any other deleterious or poisonous drug except nicotine.
   B.   Sale To Children 1 : No licensee shall sell, give away, or permit any
vending machine to be used to sell any cigarette, cigarette paper or cigarette
wrapper to any person below eighteen (18) years of age. (1982 Code § 7.314)
 
Notes
1 1. MSA § 609.685.
3-6-4: BLIND PERSONS:
Pursuant to the requirements of Minnesota Statutes Annotated section 461.15, no
blind person shall be required to pay the license fee. (1982 Code § 7.313)
CHAPTER 7
GAMBLING 1
SECTION:
3-7-1: Purpose
3-7-2: State Law Adopted
3-7-3: License Required
3-7-4: Application
3-7-5: License Fee
3-7-6: Eligibility For License
3-7-7: Eligible Premises
3-7-8: Permit Required, Certain Lawful Gambling Activities
3-7-9: Gambling Manager
3-7-10: Reporting Requirements
3-7-11: Profits
3-7-12: Suspension; Revocation
3-7-13: Penalty
 
Notes
1 1. MSA § 412.221, subd. 25.
3-7-1: PURPOSE:
The purpose of this chapter is to closely regulate and control the conduct of
gambling. (Ord. 226, 9-19-1996)
3-7-2: STATE LAW ADOPTED:
The provisions of Minnesota Statutes Annotated chapter 349, section 609.75,
subdivision 3, and section 609.761 relating to the definition of terms,
licensing, and restrictions of gambling are adopted and made a part of this
chapter as if set out in full. (Ord. 226, 9-19-1996; amd. 2005 Code)
3-7-3: LICENSE REQUIRED:
No person shall directly or indirectly operate a gambling device or conduct a
raffle without a license to do so as provided in this chapter. (Ord. 226, 9-19-
1996)
3-7-4: APPLICATION:
   A.   Form: Application for a license shall be made upon a form prescribed by
the city council.
   B.   False Statement: No person shall make a false representation in an
application.
   C.   City Council Action: The city council shall act upon said application
within one hundred eighty (180) days from the date of application. The city
council shall review each application as an initial application. (Ord. 226, 9-
19-1996)
3-7-5: LICENSE FEE:
There shall be an investigation fee of one hundred dollars ($100.00) payable
every two (2) years to conduct lawful gambling within the city. (Ord. 285, 7-6-
2010)
3-7-6: ELIGIBILITY FOR LICENSE:
A license shall be issued only to fraternal, religious, and veterans'
organizations, or any corporation, trust, or association organized for
exclusively scientific, literary, charitable, educational, or artistic
purposes, or any club which is organized and operated exclusively for pleasure
or recreation. Such organization must have been in existence for at least three
(3) years and shall have at least thirty (30) active members. (Ord. 226, 9-19-
1996)
3-7-7: ELIGIBLE PREMISES:
Gambling shall be conducted by a licensed organization only upon premises which
it owns or leases. Leases shall be in writing and shall be for a term of at
least twelve (12) months. No lease shall provide that rental payments be based
on a percentage of receipts. A copy of the lease shall be filed with the city
clerk. (Ord. 226, 9-19-1996)
3-7-8: PERMIT REQUIRED, CERTAIN LAWFUL GAMBLING ACTIVITIES:
   A.   Permit Required: No person or organization shall conduct the following
gambling activities exempt from licensure requirements of Minnesota Statutes
Annotated section 349.16, without first obtaining a permit from the city:
      1.   Bingo conducted in connection with a civic celebration if it is not
conducted for more than twelve (12) consecutive days in a calendar year.
      2.   Bingo conducted by an organization which conducts four (4) or fewer
bingo occasions in a calendar year.
      3.   Raffles conducted by an organization wherein the value of all raffle
prizes awarded by the organization in a calendar year does not exceed seven
hundred fifty dollars ($750.00) with prizes valued at fair market value.
      4.   Raffles conducted by an organization which directly or under
contract to the state or political subdivision delivers health or social
services and is exempt from taxation under internal revenue code 501(c)(3), if
prizes awarded in the raffles are real or personal property donated by an
individual, firm or other organization.
   B.   Application: To obtain a permit, the applicant shall first file an
application in a form furnished for such purpose. The application shall contain
the following:
      1.   Name and address of organization requesting permit.
      2.   Address of officers and person accounting for receipts, expenses and
profits for the event.
      3.   Dates of bingo occasion or raffle for which permit is requested.
      4.   Premises on which event will occur.
      5.   Copy of any rental or leasing arrangement connected with the event
including rental to be charged to the organization.
      6.   Estimated value of prizes to be awarded.
   C.   Permit Fee: No fee shall be required for a permit issued.
   D.   Use Of Profits: Profits from the conduct of a bingo occasion or raffle
shall be used for "lawful purposes" 1 . (Ord. 226, 9-19-1996)
 
Notes
1 1. MSA § 349.12, subd. 25.
3-7-9: GAMBLING MANAGER:
   A.   Designation: All lawful gambling operations shall be under the
supervision of a single gambling manager to be designated by the organization.
   B.   Qualifications: The gambling manager shall be an active member of the
organization and shall qualify under state law.
   C.   Bond: The gambling manager shall provide a fidelity bond in the sum of
ten thousand dollars ($10,000.00) in favor of the organization conditioned on
the faithful performance of his duties.
   D.   Responsibilities: The gambling manager shall be responsible for gross
receipts and profits from lawful gambling and for their operation. The gambling
manager shall be responsible for using profits for a proper purpose. (Ord. 226,
9-19-1996)
3-7-10: REPORTING REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Gross Receipts: Each organization licensed to operate lawful gambling
shall keep records of its gross receipts, expenses and profits for each single
gathering or occasion at which lawful gambling is used. All deductions from
gross receipts for each single gathering or occasion shall be documented with
receipts or other records indicating the amount, a description of the service
or other reason for the deduction, and the recipient. The distribution of
profits shall be itemized as to payee, purpose, amount and date of payment.
   B.   Separation Of Funds: Gross receipts from the operation of lawful
gambling shall be segregated from other revenues of the organization and placed
in a separate account. The person who accounts for gross receipts, expenses and
profits from the lawful gambling shall not be the same person who accounts for
other revenues of the organization.
   C.   Monthly Reports: Each organization licensed to operate lawful gambling
shall report monthly to its membership and to the city clerk, its gross
receipts, expenses and profits from gambling devices or raffles, and the
distribution of profits. The organization will provide the city clerk with an
annual audit at the end of the license year. The licensee shall preserve such
records for three (3) years. (Ord. 226, 9-19-1996)
3-7-11: PROFITS:
Profits from the operation of lawful gambling shall be used for "lawful
purposes" as contained in Minnesota Statutes Annotated 349.12, subdivision 25.
Each organization conducting lawful gambling within the city shall contribute
at least sixty five percent (65%) of its lawful purpose expenditures in the
trade area. The city's trade area shall be the city limits of the city. (Ord.
226, 9-19-1996)
3-7-12: SUSPENSION; REVOCATION:
   A.   Suspension: Any license may be suspended or revoked for any violation
of this chapter. A license shall not be suspended or revoked until the
procedural requirements of subsection B of this section have been complied
with; provided, that in cases where probable cause exists as to a violation,
the city may temporarily suspend upon service of notice of the hearing provided
for in subsection B of this section. Such temporary suspension shall not extend
for more than two (2) weeks.
   B.   Revocation: A license shall not be revoked under subsection A of this
section until notice and a opportunity for a hearing have first been given to
the licensee. The notice shall be personally served and shall state the
provision reasonably believed to be violated. The notice shall also state that
the licensee may demand a hearing on the matter, in which case the license will
not be suspended until after the hearing is held. If the licensee requests a
hearing, one shall be held on the matter by the council at least one week after
the date on which the request is made. If, as a result of the hearing, the
council finds that a violation exists, then the city council may suspend or
terminate the license. (Ord. 226, 9-19-1996)
3-7-13: PENALTY:
Violation of any provision of this chapter shall be a misdemeanor. A person
convicted of violating any provision of this chapter shall be subject to a fine
as provided in the general penalty in subsection 1-4-1B of this code, plus in
either case the costs of prosecution. (Ord. 226, 9-19-1996; amd. 2005 Code)
CHAPTER 8
KENNELS
SECTION:
3-8-1: Definition
3-8-2: License Required
3-8-3: Application
3-8-4: Fee
3-8-5: Issuance
3-8-6: Term
3-8-7: Tags
3-8-8: Conditions And Restrictions
3-8-1: DEFINITION:
"Kennel" means any establishment where dogs are boarded for profit or are kept
for the purpose of breeding or sale, and any other place where three (3) or
more dogs over the age of six (6) months are kept. (Ord. 283, 6-1-2010)
3-8-2: LICENSE REQUIRED:
No person shall operate any kennel within the city without first having
obtained a license to do so. (1982 Code § 8.592)
3-8-3: APPLICATION:
Application for a kennel license shall be made to the city clerk. (1982 Code §
8.593)
3-8-4: FEE:
The city council shall, by resolution, establish the fee for a kennel license.
(1982 Code § 8.594)
3-8-5: ISSUANCE:
A license shall be issued by the city clerk upon proper application accompanied
by payment of the required fee. (1982 Code § 8.595)
3-8-6: TERM:
Each license issued shall become effective when issued and shall expire on the
last day of the same month in the next calendar year that it was issued. (1982
Code § 8.596)
3-8-7: TAGS:
   A.   Issuance: The city clerk shall issue with the license a number of metal
tags equal to the number of dogs for which the kennel is licensed.
   B.   Form: The tags shall be made in a form so that they may be readily
distinguishable from the individual license tags for the same year.
   C.   Collar: The licensee shall at all times keep a tag attached to the
collar of each dog over six (6) months old kept in the kennel under a kennel
license.
   D.   Transfer Of Tags: The tags may be transferred from one dog to another
within the kennel. (1982 Code § 8.597)
3-8-8: CONDITIONS AND RESTRICTIONS:
   A.   Condition Of Premises: The licensee shall keep the premises in a clean,
quiet, orderly and sanitary condition. (1982 Code § 8.598)
   B.   Location: No kennel may be located except in a commercial district
under subsection 11-1-2C2 of this code, or in an industrial district under
subsection 11-1-2D of this code. (Ord. 284, 6-1-2010)
   C.   Compliance Required: The licensee shall obey all requirements imposed
by law, regulation and this code.
   D.   Other Licenses Or Permits: The issuance of a kennel license shall not
relieve any licensee of obtaining any other license or permit which may be
required by law or by any other part of this code. (1982 Code § 8.598)
   E.   Rental Property: If the kennel is located on rented property, the
applicant shall obtain written consent from the recorded owners of the
property. (Ord. 286, 7-6-2010)
CHAPTER 9
SEXUALLY ORIENTED BUSINESSES 1
SECTION:
3-9-1: Purpose
3-9-2: License Required
3-9-3: Application
3-9-4: License Fees
3-9-5: Granting Of License
3-9-6: Persons Ineligible For License
3-9-7: Premises Ineligible For License
3-9-8: Building Standards
3-9-9: Conditions Of License
3-9-10: Hours Of Operation
3-9-11: Existing Licensee Compliance
3-9-12: Principal Use License Fees
 
Notes
1 1. See also title 11, chapter 2 of this code.
3-9-1: PURPOSE:
The purpose of this chapter is to establish regulations governing the licensing
of sexually oriented businesses classified as adult use-principal in the city
and to prevent the spread of sexually transmitted diseases. (Ord. 227, 5-6-
1997)
3-9-2: LICENSE REQUIRED:
No person shall operate a sexually oriented business classified as "adult use-
principal" defined in section
11-2-4 of this code and "adult uses-accessory" defined in section
11-2-5 of this code without having first secured a license as hereinafter
provided. (Ord. 227, 5-6-1997)
3-9-3: APPLICATION:
In addition to such applicable information as the city may require, an
application for the license required by this chapter shall include the
following information:
   A.   Applicant: The name, residence, phone number and birth date of the
applicant, if an individual; and if a corporation, the names, residences, phone
numbers and birth dates of those owners holding more than five percent (5%) of
the outstanding stock of the corporation.
   B.   Manager: The name, address, phone number and birth date of the manager
of such operation, if different from the owners.
   C.   Premises: The premises where in the adult use is to be located.
   D.   Prior Offenses: A statement detailing each gross misdemeanor or felony
relating to a sex offense and/or the operation of adult uses and related
activities of which the applicant or, in the case of a corporation, the owners
of more than five percent (5%) of the outstanding stock of the corporation,
having been convicted, and whether or not the applicant has ever applied for or
held a license to operate a similar type of business in other communities.
   E.   Type Of Business: The activities and types of business to be conducted.
   F.   Hours: The hours of operation.
   G.   Minors: The provisions made to restrict access by minors.
   H.   Building Plan: A building plan of the premises detailing all internal
operations and activities. (Ord. 227, 5-6-1997)
3-9-4: LICENSE FEES:
   A.   Payment Required; Refund: Each application for a license shall be
accompanied by a receipt from the city for payment in full of the required fee
for the license. All fees shall be paid into the general fund of the
municipality. Upon rejection of any applications for a license, the city may
refund the license fee paid, minus the amount of costs necessary for
application, investigation and review, including, but not limited to, costs
relating to administration, planning, legal, inspection and police
investigation.
   B.   Term; Proration: All licenses shall expire on December 31 of each
calendar year. Each license shall be issued for a period of one year, except
that if a portion of the license year has elapsed when the application is made,
a license may be issued for the remainder of the year, any unexpired fraction
of a month shall be counted as one month.
   C.   Annual Fee: The annual fee for an adult use-principal license shall be
as set forth in section
3-9-12 of this chapter.
   D.   Criteria For Refund: No part of the fee paid by any licensee shall be
refunded except in the following instances upon application to the city manager
within thirty (30) days from the happening of any of the following events.
There shall be refunded a pro rata portion of the fee for the unexpired period
of the license, computed on a monthly basis, when operation of the licensed
business ceases not less than one month before expiration of the license
because of:
      1.   Destruction or damage of the licensed premises by fire or other
catastrophe;
      2.   The licensee's disabling illness;
      3.   The licensee's death. (Ord. 227, 5-6-1997)
3-9-5: GRANTING OF LICENSE:
   A.   Investigation; Hearing: The city manager or his or her designated
representatives shall investigate all facts set out in the application. A
public hearing shall be held before the city council prior to any action taken
on the license application.
   B.   City Council Action; Criteria For Evaluation: After such investigation
and hearing, the city council shall grant or refuse the application. Criteria
for evaluating a license shall include the following:
      1.   Application shall be completed in full.
      2.   Applicant shall be eligible for license.
      3.   Location shall be eligible for license.
      4.   Applicant shall provide description of merchandise, services or
entertainment for sale in premises.
      5.   Applicant shall identify means of restricting access by minors and
shall not employ any minors.
      6.   Applicant shall provide property owner's name and address and
business owner's name and address.
      7.   The adult use shall be in compliance with all applicable city code
regulations
   C.   Transferability: Each license shall be issued to the applicant only and
shall not be transferable to another holder. Each license shall be issued only
for the premises described in the application. No license shall be transferred
to another place without the approval of the city council. (Ord. 227, 5-6-1997)
3-9-6: PERSONS INELIGIBLE FOR LICENSE:
No license shall be granted to or held by any person:
   A.   Age: Under twenty one (21) years of age;
   B.   Felony Conviction: Who has been convicted of a felony or of violating
any law of this state or local ordinance relating to sex offenses and/or adult
uses;
   C.   Proprietor: Who is not the proprietor of the establishment for which
the license is issued. (Ord. 227, 5-6-1997)
3-9-7: PREMISES INELIGIBLE FOR LICENSE:
   A.   Prior Violations: No license shall be granted for adult uses on any
premises where a licensee has been convicted of a violation of this chapter, or
where any license hereunder has been revoked for cause, until one year has
elapsed after such conviction or revocation.
   B.   Compliance With Zoning: Except for uses lawfully existing at the time
of the adoption of this chapter, no license shall be granted for any adult use
which is not in compliance with the city's zoning regulations. (Ord. 227, 5-6-
1997)
3-9-8: BUILDING STANDARDS:
   A.   Prohibited Activities: No commercial building, structure, premises, or
part thereof, or facilities therein used by a sexually oriented business
classified as an adult use-principal shall be so constructed, used, designed or
operated for the purpose of engaging in, or permitting persons to engage in
"sexual activities" as defined in section
11-2-2 of this code.
   B.   Prohibited Partitions, Booths, Stalls, Etc.: No person shall own,
operate, manage, rent, lease, or exercise control of any commercial building,
structure, premises, or portion or part thereof, which contains:
      1.   Partitions between subdivisions of a room, portion or part of a
building, structure or premises having an aperture which is designed or
constructed to facilitate sexual activity between persons on either side of the
partition.
      2.   Booths, stalls, or partitioned portions of a room, or individual
rooms, used for adult uses, having doors, curtains or portal partitions, unless
such booths, stalls, partitioned portions of a room, or individual rooms so
used shall have at least one side open to an adjacent public room so that the
area inside is visible to persons in the adjacent public room. Such areas shall
be lighted in a manner that the persons in the area used for adult uses are
visible from the adjacent public rooms, but such lighting shall not be of such
intensity as to prevent the viewing of motion pictures or other offered adult
uses.
   C.   Viewing Areas Or Booths:
      1.   Accessibility: All viewing areas or booths in movie arcades shall be
accessible from a continuous main aisle.
      2.   Location: All viewing areas or booths shall be located together
along a continuous main aisle to eliminate the possibility of secluded booths
elsewhere on the premises.
      3.   Number Of Persons Allowed: No more than one person shall be
permitted to enter or remain in a viewing area or booth at any time.
      4.   Maintenance: The viewing areas or booth shall be maintained at all
times in a clean and sanitary manner.
   D.   Entrances: All entrances to the business, with the exception of
emergency fire exits not usable to enter the business, shall be visible from a
public right of way. (Ord. 227, 5-6-1997)
3-9-9: CONDITIONS OF LICENSE:
   A.   Subject To Code And Applicable Law: Every license shall be granted
subject to all of the conditions of this code, and of any other applicable
county, state or federal law.
   B.   Posting Of License: All licensed premises shall have the license posted
in a conspicuous place at all times.
   C.   Minors: No minor shall be permitted on the licensed premises.
   D.   Right Of Entry: Any designated inspection officer of the city shall
have the unqualified right to enter and inspect all public areas of the
premises of a licensee during regular business hours.
   E.   Responsibility For Conduct: Every licensee shall be responsible for the
conduct of his place of business and shall maintain conditions of order. (Ord.
227, 5-6-1997)
3-9-10: HOURS OF OPERATION:
Sexually oriented businesses adult use-principal operations shall be restricted
from operating between the hours of one minute after twelve o'clock (12:01)
A.M. and six o'clock (6:00) A.M. (Ord. 227, 5-6-1997)
3-9-11: EXISTING LICENSEE COMPLIANCE:
All existing businesses shall be required to conform with this chapter on or
before August 1, 1997. Failure to comply will result in the license being
revoked effective twelve o'clock (12:00) midnight August 1, 1997. (Ord. 227, 5-
6-1997)
3-9-12: PRINCIPAL USE LICENSE FEES:
   A.   Investigation Fee: Nonrefundable investigation fee shall be as set by
resolution of the city council.
   B.   Annual License Fee: Annual license fee for adult use-principal license
shall be as set by resolution of the city council. (Ord. 227, 5-6-1997)
TITLE 4
PUBLIC HEALTH AND SAFETY
CHAPTER 1
FIRE DEPARTMENT
SECTION:
4-1-1: Department Continued
4-1-2: Duties
4-1-1: DEPARTMENT CONTINUED:
A nonprofit volunteer fire department duly incorporated under the laws of the
state of Minnesota is hereby continued. (1982 Code § 2.421)
4-1-2: DUTIES:
Members of the fire department shall perform such duties relating to the
extinguishment and prevention of fires, protection of life and property from
fires, and have such other powers and duties relating to firefighting and fire
prevention as are prescribed by law, by charter, by this code and as the city
council may determine. (1982 Code § 2.422)
CHAPTER 1A
EMERGENCY PROTECTION FIRE SERVICES
SECTION:
4-1A-1: Purpose And Intent
4-1A-2: Definitions
4-1A-3: Parties Affected
4-1A-4: Rates
4-1A-5: Billing And Collection
4-1A-6: Mutual Aid Agreement
4-1A-7: Application Of Collections To Budget
4-1A-1: PURPOSE AND INTENT:
This chapter is adopted for the purpose of authorizing the city of Dawson to
charge for fire service as authorized by Minnesota statutes sections 366.011,
366.012, and 415.01. (Ord. 296, 1-3-2012)
4-1A-2: DEFINITIONS:
FIRE PROTECTION CONTRACT: A contract between the city and a town or other city
for the city to provide fire service.
FIRE SERVICE: Any deployment of firefighting personnel and/or equipment to
extinguish a fire or perform any preventative measure in an effort to protect
equipment, life, or property in an area threatened by fire. It also includes
the deployment of firefighting personnel and/or equipment to provide fire
suppression, rescue, extrication, and any other services related to fire and
rescue as may occasionally occur.
FIRE SERVICE CHARGE: The charge imposed by the city for receiving fire service.
JOINT POWERS AGREEMENT: An agreement between the city and townships or other
cities for the city's fire department to provide fire service to that township
or city.
MOTOR VEHICLE: Any self-propelled vehicle designed and originally manufactured
to operate primarily upon public roads and highways, and not operated
exclusively upon railroad tracks. It includes semitrailers. It does not include
snowmobiles, manufactured homes, all-terrain vehicles, or park trailers.
MUTUAL AID AGREEMENT: An agreement between the city and a town or other city
for the city's fire department to provide assistance to the fire department of
a town or other city. (Ord. 296, 1-3-2012)
4-1A-3: PARTIES AFFECTED:
   A.   Owners of property within the city who receive fire service.
   B.   Anyone who receives fire service as a result of a motor vehicle
accident or fire within the city.
   C.   Owners of property in towns or cities to which the city provides fire
service pursuant to a fire protection contract or a joint powers agreement.
(Ord. 296, 1-3-2012)
4-1A-4: RATES:
The rate charged to the parties affected in section
4-1A-3 of this chapter shall be one thousand dollars ($1,000.00) for each fire
service. The fire service charge for each fire service will be charged to the
parties affected under section
4-1A-3 of this chapter. (Ord. 296, 1-3-2012)
4-1A-5: BILLING AND COLLECTION:
   A.   Parties requesting and receiving fire services may be billed directly
by the city. Additionally, if the party receiving fire services did not request
services but a fire or other situation exists which, at the discretion of the
fire department personnel in charge requires fire service, the party will be
charged and billed. All parties will be billed whether or not the fire service
is covered by insurance. Any billable amount of the fire charge not covered by
a party's insurance remains a debt of the party receiving the fire service.
   B.   Parties billed for fire service will have thirty (30) days to pay. If
the fire service charge is not paid by that time, it will be considered
delinquent and the city will send a notice of delinquency.
   C.   If the fire service charge remains unpaid for thirty (30) days after
this notice of delinquency is sent, the city will use all practical and
reasonable legal means to collect the fire service charge. The party receiving
fire service shall be liable for all collection costs incurred by the city
including, but not limited to, reasonable attorney fees and court costs.
   D.   If the fire service charge remains unpaid for thirty (30) days after
the notice of delinquency is sent, the city council may also, on or before
October 15 of each year, certify the unpaid fire service charge to the county
auditor in which the recipient of the services owns real property for
collection with property taxes. The county auditor is responsible for remitting
to the city all charges collected on behalf of the city. The city must give the
property owner notice of its intent to certify the unpaid fire service charge
by September 15.
   E.   The first three (3) false alarms will not be billed as a fire call. If
a fourth false alarm occurs, a fire service charge will be billed as set out in
section
4-1A-4 of this chapter. (Ord. 296, 1-3-2012)
4-1A-6: MUTUAL AID AGREEMENT:
When the city fire department provides fire service to another fire department
pursuant to a mutual aid agreement, the billing will be determined by the
mutual aid agreement. (Ord. 296, 1-3-2012)
4-1A-7: APPLICATION OF COLLECTIONS TO BUDGET:
All collected fire charges will be city funds and used to offset the expenses
of the city fire department in providing fire services. (Ord. 296, 1-3-2012)
CHAPTER 2
FIRE SAFETY
SECTION:
4-2-1: False Alarms
4-2-2: Interference Prohibited
4-2-3: Driving Over Fire Hose
4-2-4: Injury To Apparatus Or Equipment
4-2-1: FALSE ALARMS 1 :
No person shall give or make or cause to be given or made a fire alarm without
probable cause. (1982 Code § 8.211)
 
Notes
1 1. MSA § 609.686.
4-2-2: INTERFERENCE PROHIBITED 1 :
No person shall neglect or refuse to obey any reasonable order of any
firefighter at a fire, or interfere with the fire department in the discharge
of its duties. (1982 Code § 8.212)
 
Notes
1 2. MSA § 609.50.
4-2-3: DRIVING OVER FIRE HOSE 1 :
No person without permission of a firefighter at the scene shall drive any
vehicle over any fire hose. (1982 Code § 8.212)
 
Notes
1 3. MSA § 169.41.
4-2-4: INJURY TO APPARATUS OR EQUIPMENT:
No person shall intentionally injure any fire hose or any other fire apparatus
or equipment. (1982 Code § 8.212)
CHAPTER 3
NUISANCES 1
SECTION:
4-3-1: Public Nuisances Prohibited
4-3-2: Unwholesome Meat And Food
4-3-3: Unsanitary Uses
4-3-4: Abatement
 
Notes
1 1. MSA § 412.221, subd. 23.
4-3-1: PUBLIC NUISANCES PROHIBITED:
No person shall, by any act or by any failure to perform a legal duty,
intentionally do any of the following:
   A.   Maintain or permit a condition which unreasonably annoys, injures or
endangers the safety, health, morals, comfort or repose of any considerable
number or numbers of the public.
   B.   Interfere with, obstruct or render dangerous for passage any public
highway, right of way or waters used by the public.
   C.   Engage in any other act or omission declared by law or by this code to
be a public nuisance. (1982 Code § 8.111)
4-3-2: UNWHOLESOME MEAT AND FOOD:
No person shall sell, expose for sale or in any manner dispose of to the public
any emaciated, tainted or putrid meat or any unwholesome food of any kind.
(1982 Code § 8.312)
4-3-3: UNSANITARY USES:
No person shall place, deposit or permit to be deposited in any unsanitary
manner upon public or private property within the city, or in any area under
the jurisdiction of the city, any dead animal or offal, any human or animal
excrement, or any garbage, rubbish, litter or any other objectionable wastes.
Any such deposit or accumulation is a public nuisance. (1982 Code § 8.313)
4-3-4: ABATEMENT:
   A.   Notice:
      1.   Notice To Abate: Whenever any public nuisance exists, the city
council may, by resolution, direct the city clerk to give notice to the person
responsible for creating, maintaining or permitting the nuisance or to the
owner of the property, or to any or all of them, to abate the nuisance.
      2.   Contents Of Notice: The notice shall describe each nuisance, and
shall specify the time, considering the nature of each nuisance and the
difficulty of correcting it, within which each nuisance or all of them must be
abated.
   B.   Failure To Abate: Any person who fails to abate any public nuisance
when required to do so shall, upon conviction, be guilty of a misdemeanor.
(1982 Code § 8.112)
   C.   Abatement By City: If each nuisance is not corrected within the time
specified, the city council may, by resolution, order the nuisance abated at
the expense of the person notified. If the owner of real property was notified,
the cost of abatement shall also be a lien against the property and may be
collected as a special assessment if not promptly paid. (1982 Code § 8.113)
   D.   Abatement Procedures In Special Cases: Abatement of hazardous buildings
shall be made pursuant to the requirements of Minnesota Statutes Annotated
sections 463.15 through 463.26. Abatement of any other nuisances for which
special requirements are provided by law shall be in the manner provided by
law. (1982 Code § 8.114)
CHAPTER 4
GARBAGE AND REFUSE
ARTICLE A. GENERAL REGULATIONS 1
SECTION:
4-4A-1: Definitions
4-4A-2: Use Of Municipal Or Licensed Collector Required
4-4A-3: Open Burning Prohibited
4-4A-4: Improper Deposit Of Refuse
4-4A-5: Scattering Refuse
4-4A-6: Removal Of Refuse
4-4A-7: Burying And Composting
4-4A-8: Recyclables
4-4A-9: Junked Vehicles And Machinery
 
Notes
1 1. MSA § 412.221, subd. 22.
4-4A-1: DEFINITIONS:
As used in this article, the following terms shall have the meaning given to
them:
GARBAGE: Organic waste attending the preparation and consumption of food,
decayed, spoiled or discarded food, offal and other putrescible solid waste and
all other similar wastes from the sale, preparation, consumption and discarding
of food.
RECYCLABLES: Any paper, plastic, metal, aluminum, oil, glass and other items
capable of being recycled, but only when such items are being properly stored
for recycling and are at appropriate intervals taken from the premises to a
place where they are collected to be recycled.
REFUSE: Garbage and rubbish plus all other solid wastes. It does not include
recyclables actually and reasonably being stored for recycling.
RUBBISH: Paper boxes, cartons, cans, bottles, metals, tires and tubes, plastic,
glass and other similar articles of debris which are unsightly or may endanger
health or safety if allowed to accumulate or scatter. (1982 Code § 8.411)
4-4A-2: USE OF MUNICIPAL OR LICENSED COLLECTOR REQUIRED:
No householder, occupant or owner of any residence shall cause or allow any
refuse to be taken from the property except by the municipal refuse collection
system or a refuse collector licensed by the city. A householder, occupant or
owner of any residence, who also has ownership in a business which receives
refuse collection may take refuse from his residence to the business for
collection by the municipal refuse collection system or a refuse collector
licensed by the city. (Ord. 264, 2-20-2007)
4-4A-3: OPEN BURNING PROHIBITED:
No person shall dispose of any garbage, rubbish or other refuse by open
burning, nor shall any person owning or having control of any premises cause or
permit the same, in the city, except upon application to and approval by the
appropriate state agency and in the manner and under the conditions and
restrictions established by law and administrative regulation. (1982 Code §
8.412)
4-4A-4: IMPROPER DEPOSIT OF REFUSE:
No person shall deposit or cause to be deposited any refuse:
   A.   In any stream or other body of water;
   B.   Upon any street, alley or other public property, except that refuse
from picnicking or other use at a park, from pedestrians using a sidewalk and
from other similar uses may be deposited in proper containers provided for that
purpose;
   C.   Upon the property of another without permission to do so or in
violation of any requirement of law, regulations or this code; or
   D.   Upon property owned by, occupied by or otherwise in control of the
person doing so unless in proper containers for storage of the refuse until
collected or otherwise disposed of properly. (1982 Code § 8.413)
4-4A-5: SCATTERING REFUSE:
No person shall keep or haul, or allow to be kept on or hauled to or from
premises owned by, occupied by, or in control of that person, any refuse in a
manner that the wind, water or any other cause will or is likely to scatter the
refuse from the place of keeping or transport. (1982 Code § 8.414)
4-4A-6: REMOVAL OF REFUSE:
Refuse which accumulates between collections shall be set out for removal with
