each collection from premises regularly served by a refuse collection service.
Refuse from other premises shall be removed and disposed of properly at such
intervals as will prevent it from becoming rotten and offensive to smell and as
will prevent a greater accumulation than can be held by the containers used. No
person shall cause or allow any unsanitary or unsightly accumulation of refuse
upon any property owned by, occupied by or in the control of that person. Any
such accumulation is a public nuisance. (1982 Code § 8.415)
4-4A-7: BURYING AND COMPOSTING:
No person shall bury any refuse in the city except in an approved sanitary
landfill, except that leaves, lawn clippings and suitable, easily biodegradable
garbage may be composted on the premises where they have accumulated.
Composting may be done only in a rodentproof container, in a sanitary manner,
with no objectionable odors, and in full compliance with all other applicable
requirements. (1982 Code § 8.416)
4-4A-8: RECYCLABLES:
Recyclables shall be kept in suitable containers or bundled neatly. The
containers or bundles shall be kept in an enclosed building or otherwise
protected from public view. Recyclables shall be taken to a place where they
are collected for recycling whenever necessary to prevent an excessive
accumulation of them. When stored on the premises, they shall be kept in a safe
and sanitary manner. (1982 Code § 8.417)
4-4A-9: JUNKED VEHICLES AND MACHINERY:
No person shall leave upon any property within the city, and no person in
charge or control of any property within the city, whether as owner, tenant,
occupant, lessee or otherwise, shall allow to remain on the property, any
partially dismantled, inoperative, wrecked, junked, unlicensed or discarded
vehicle or machinery for longer than ten (10) days, unless the vehicle or
machinery is in an enclosed building or on the premises of a lawfully operated
business engaged in the repair, storage or junking of such vehicles. (1982 Code
§ 8.419)
ARTICLE A. GENERAL REGULATIONS 1
SECTION:
4-4A-1: Definitions
4-4A-2: Use Of Municipal Or Licensed Collector Required
4-4A-3: Open Burning Prohibited
4-4A-4: Improper Deposit Of Refuse
4-4A-5: Scattering Refuse
4-4A-6: Removal Of Refuse
4-4A-7: Burying And Composting
4-4A-8: Recyclables
4-4A-9: Junked Vehicles And Machinery
 
Notes
1 1. MSA § 412.221, subd. 22.

ARTICLE B. REFUSE CONTAINERS
SECTION:
4-4B-1: Containers Required
4-4B-2: Specifications
4-4B-3: Bagging
4-4B-4: Bulk Containers
4-4B-5: Proper Disposal; Prohibited Materials
4-4B-6: Maintenance
4-4B-7: Storage And Placement
4-4B-1: CONTAINERS REQUIRED:
Every owner, occupant or other person in control or in possession of any
dwelling or any other building in the city shall provide on the premises one or
more containers to receive and contain all normal refuse which may accumulate
between collections. (1982 Code § 8.431)
4-4B-2: SPECIFICATIONS:
Each container shall have a tight cover, shall not exceed thirty (30) gallons
in capacity, and shall have handles or handholds on the side. Inorganic refuse
and paper, leaves, lawn clippings, twigs, shavings, and similar refuse may be
stored and placed for collection in any suitable, sanitary and litterproof
container. (1982 Code § 8.432)
4-4B-3: BAGGING:
In lieu of using a container meeting the requirements of section
4-4B-2 of this article, any person may place any refuse in an airtight,
waterproof disposable plastic or other bag of sufficient durability to contain
the refuse placed in it without puncturing or bursting open. (1982 Code §
8.433)
4-4B-4: BULK CONTAINERS:
Any apartment building, business or industry may use bulk or box type refuse
containers. When municipal collection services are used, such containers must
be of a type which can be mechanically emptied by the collection vehicle
serving the premises or, including its contents, be of such weight, mobility
and size that one collector can reasonably upturn it and empty its contents
into the collection vehicle. (1982 Code § 8.434)
4-4B-5: PROPER DISPOSAL; PROHIBITED MATERIALS:
Household garbage and similar refuse shall be drained of liquid and wrapped in
paper before being placed in a container. Highly flammable or explosive
material shall not be placed in a container for refuse collection. (1982 Code §
8.435)
4-4B-6: MAINTENANCE:
All containers shall be maintained in good and sanitary condition, shall be
kept rodentproof and shall be kept, as nearly as practicable, insectproof. Any
container which is broken, which has ragged or sharp edges, which has any
defect likely to hamper or injure the person collecting the contents, or which
fails to meet the requirements of this article shall be promptly replaced.
(1982 Code § 8.436)
4-4B-7: STORAGE AND PLACEMENT:
Containers shall be stored in a suitable place inside the building, at the rear
door, or on the rear or side part of the grounds to the building. Where the
container is not or cannot be stored in a location which is easily accessible
for collection and which is close to where it is emptied, the container shall
be placed in such a location for collection. No container may be placed along
the front property line for collection before eight o'clock (8:00) P.M. of the
night before collection or allowed to remain there after six o'clock (6:00)
P.M. of the day of collection. (1982 Code § 8.437)
ARTICLE C. MUNICIPAL REFUSE COLLECTION
SECTION:
4-4C-1: System Continued
4-4C-2: Supervision
4-4C-3: Refuse Collector
4-4C-4: Refuse Utility Fund
4-4C-5: Rates
4-4C-6: Billing; Payment
4-4C-7: Unusual Items
4-4C-8: Additional Rules
4-4C-1: SYSTEM CONTINUED:
A municipal refuse collection system is hereby continued for the collection and
disposal of refuse accumulated within the city. The city council shall employ
necessary employees and furnish such tools and equipment as may be necessary
for the efficient and sanitary collection of refuse accumulated within the
city. (1982 Code § 8.451)
4-4C-2: SUPERVISION:
The city manager shall supervise and control the municipal collection and
disposal of refuse. (1982 Code § 8.452)
4-4C-3: REFUSE COLLECTOR:
The city council may, by resolution, designate one or more refuse collectors
licensed by the city as the municipal refuse collector for all refuse to be
collected under the municipal collection system or for such part of it as the
city council deems best. (1982 Code § 8.453)
4-4C-4: REFUSE UTILITY FUND:
   A.   Income: All income from the operation of the municipal refuse
collection system, and all license fees collected from licensed refuse
collectors, shall be paid into a separate fund designated as the refuse utility
fund.
   B.   Expenses: All expenses of operation shall be paid from this fund. In
the event the revenues credited to the fund are insufficient to pay all
expenses, the council may transfer to the fund from the general fund such
amounts as may be necessary.
   C.   Net Revenue: Net revenue from the fund shall be used for improvement
and extension of the refuse collection system, including necessary landfill
facilities, or for such other municipal purposes as may be proper. (1982 Code §
8.458)
4-4C-5: RATES:
   A.   Residential: The charge for the removal and disposal of refuse from
each residence served shall be four dollars ($4.00) per month.
   B.   Other Users:
      1.   System Of Charges: The city council shall establish, by resolution,
a system of service charges for the removal and disposal of refuse from all
other premises served by the municipal refuse collection system.
      2.   Considerations: It may set maximum or minimum charges according to
the type of service provided and required, based on the type of business
conducted, the frequency of collection and such other factors as may be
appropriate.
      3.   Additional Charges: It may also establish such other charges as may
be reasonable and proper, including special charges for special handling or
special collection and hauling of unusual or abnormal quantities of refuse.
(1982 Code § 8.454)
4-4C-6: BILLING; PAYMENT:
The charge for a building or establishment shall be separately entered on the
city water or sewer bill. If the premises are not served by city water or
sewer, the charge shall be separately billed. Charges for refuse collection
services shall be payable at the same time, subject to the same conditions and
may be enforced in the same manner as charges for city water service. (1982
Code § 8.455)
4-4C-7: UNUSUAL ITEMS:
   A.   Appliances, Furniture, Etc.: Appliances, furniture and other refuse of
an unusual nature which require special pick ups, and other refuse which is not
normally incident to the particular class of user involved, shall be collected
by the municipal collection system, subject to such charge as may be imposed
for their collection.
   B.   Flammable Or Explosive Material: No person shall place for collection
any highly flammable or explosive material except by special arrangements made
prior to collection. (1982 Code § 8.456)
4-4C-8: ADDITIONAL RULES:
The city council may, by resolution, provide such additional rules and
regulations as may be necessary for the efficient operation of the municipal
refuse collection system. (1982 Code § 8.457)
ARTICLE D. MUNICIPAL DUMP
SECTION:
4-4D-1: Permit Required; Fee
4-4D-2: Noncombustible Refuse
4-4D-3: Further Restriction And Control
4-4D-1: PERMIT REQUIRED; FEE:
No person, except a licensed refuse collector or except the municipal refuse
collection service, shall dump any refuse at any dumping ground owned, used or
controlled by the city without having first obtained a dumping permit from the
city clerk or without paying such dumping fee as the council may, by
resolution, establish for use of the dump. (1982 Code § 8.491)
4-4D-2: NONCOMBUSTIBLE REFUSE:
No person shall dump any noncombustible refuse at any municipal dump. (1982
Code § 8.491)
4-4D-3: FURTHER RESTRICTION AND CONTROL:
The city council may, by resolution, further restrict and control the use of
any municipal dump. (1982 Code § 8.491)
CHAPTER 5
DUTCH ELM DISEASE
SECTION:
4-5-1: Policy
4-5-2: Program
4-5-3: Tree Inspector
4-5-4: Inspection; Investigation
4-5-5: Nuisance Declared
4-5-6: Procedure For Removal
4-5-7: Spraying
4-5-8: Transporting Wood
4-5-9: Interference
4-5-10: Penalty
4-5-1: POLICY:
The city council has determined that the health of the elm trees within the
municipal limits is threatened by a fatal disease known as Dutch elm disease.
It has further determined that the loss of elm trees growing upon public and
private property would substantially depreciate the value of property within
the city and impair the safety, good order, general welfare and convenience of
the public. It is declared to be the intention of the city council to control
and prevent the spread of this disease and this chapter is enacted for that
purpose. (1982 Code § 8.6102)
4-5-2: PROGRAM:
It is the intention of the city council to conduct a program of plant pest
control pursuant to the authority granted by Minnesota Statutes Annotated
sections 18.023 and 18.024. This program is directed specifically at the
control and elimination of Dutch elm disease fungus and elm bark beetles and is
undertaken at the recommendation of the commissioner of agriculture. The tree
inspector shall act as coordinator between the commissioner of agriculture and
the city council in the conduct of this program. (1982 Code § 8.6104)
4-5-3: TREE INSPECTOR:
   A.   Position Created: The tree inspector shall have the powers and duties
set forth in this chapter.
   B.   Appointment: The tree inspector shall be appointed annually by the city
council upon recommendation of the city park board.
   C.   Compensation: The tree inspector's salary shall be fixed by the city
council.
   D.   Duties: It is the duty of the tree inspector to coordinate, under the
direction and control of the council, all activities of the municipality
relating to the control and prevention of Dutch elm disease. He shall recommend
to the council the details of a program for the control of Dutch elm disease,
and perform the duties incident to such a program adopted by the city council.
(1982 Code § 8.6103)
4-5-4: INSPECTION; INVESTIGATION:
   A.   Annual Inspection: The tree inspector shall inspect all premises and
places within the city as often as practicable to determine whether any
condition described in section
4-5-5 of this chapter exists thereon. He shall investigate all reported
incidents of infestation by Dutch elm disease fungus or elm bark beetles.
   B.   Entry On Private Premises: The tree inspector or his duly authorized
agent may enter upon private premises at any reasonable time for the purpose of
carrying out any of the duties assigned him under this chapter.
   C.   Diagnosis: The tree inspector shall, upon finding conditions indicating
Dutch elm infestation, immediately send appropriate specimens or samples to the
commissioner of agriculture for analysis, or take such other steps for
diagnosis as may be recommended by the commissioner. Except as provided in
section
4-5-6 of this chapter, no action to remove infected trees or wood shall be
taken until positive diagnosis of the disease has been made. (1982 Code §
8.6106)
4-5-5: NUISANCE DECLARED:
   A.   Public Nuisance: The following things are public nuisances whenever
they may be found within the city:
      1.   Any living or standing elm tree or part thereof infected to any
degree with the Dutch elm disease fungus Ceratocystis ulmi (Buisman) moreau or
which harbors any of the elm bark beetles Scolytus multistraitus (Eichh.) or
Hylurgopinus rufipes (Marsh).
      2.   Any dead elm tree or part thereof, including logs, branches, stumps,
firewood or other elm material from which the bark has not been removed and
burned or sprayed with an effective elm bark beetle insecticide.
   B.   Unlawful: It is unlawful for any person to permit any public nuisance
as defined in subsection A of this section to remain on any premises owned or
controlled by him within the city. Such nuisances may be abated in the manner
prescribed by this chapter. (1982 Code § 8.6105)
   C.   Abatement: In abating the nuisances defined in subsection A of this
section, the tree inspector shall cause the infected tree or wood to be
sprayed, removed, burned or otherwise effectively treated so as to destroy and
prevent as fully as possible the spread of Dutch elm disease fungus and elm
bark beetles. Such abatement procedures shall be carried out in accordance with
current technical and expert opinions and plans as may be designated by the
commissioner of agriculture. (1982 Code § 8.6107)
4-5-6: PROCEDURE FOR REMOVAL:
   A.   Infestation: Whenever the tree inspector finds, with reasonable
certainty, that the infestation defined in subsection 4-5-5A of this chapter
exists in any tree or wood in any public or private place in the city, he shall
proceed as follows:
      1.   Nonimminent Danger: If the tree inspector finds that the danger of
infestation of other elm trees is not imminent because of elm dormancy, he
shall make a written report of his finding to the city council which shall
proceed by:
         a.   Abating the nuisance as a public improvement under Minnesota
Statutes Annotated section 429.101, or
         b.   Abating the nuisance as provided in subsection B of this section.
      2.   Imminent Danger: If the tree inspector finds that danger of
infestation of other elm trees is imminent, he shall notify the abutting
property owner by certified mail that the nuisance will be abated within a
specified time, not less than twenty (20) days from the date of mailing of such
notice. The tree inspector shall immediately report such action to the city
council, and after the expiration of the time limited by the notice, the
inspector may abate the nuisance.
   B.   Order To Abate:
      1.   Resolution Of City Council: Upon receipt of the tree inspector's
report required by subsection A1 of this section, the city council shall, by
resolution, order the nuisance abated.
      2.   Notice Of Hearing; Publication: Before action is taken on such
resolution, the city council shall publish notice of its intention to meet to
consider taking action to abate the nuisance. This notice shall be mailed to
affected property owners and published once no less than one week prior to such
meeting. The notice shall state the time and place of the meeting, the trees
affected, action proposed, the estimated cost of the abatement, and the
proposed basis of assessment, if any, of costs.
      3.   Public Hearing: At such hearing or adjournment thereof, the city
council shall hear property owners with reference to the scope and desirability
of the proposed project.
      4.   Readoption Of Resolution: The city council shall thereafter adopt a
resolution confirming the original resolution with such modifications as it
considers desirable and provide for the doing of the work by day labor or by
contract.
   C.   Costs; Report: The tree inspector shall keep a record of the costs of
abatement done under this section and shall report monthly to the city council
all work done for which assessments are to be made stating and certifying the
description of the land, lots, or parcels involved and the amount chargeable to
each.
   D.   Special Assessment: On or before September 1 of each year, the city
clerk shall list the total unpaid charges for each abatement against each
separate lot or parcel to which they are attributable under this chapter. The
city council may then spread the charges or any portion thereof against the
property involved as a special assessment under Minnesota Statutes Annotated
section 429.101 and other pertinent statutes for certification to the county
auditor and collection the following year along with current taxes. (1982 Code
§ 8.6108)
4-5-7: SPRAYING:
   A.   Fungus Infection: Whenever the tree inspector determines that any elm
tree or elm wood within the city is infected with Dutch elm disease fungus, he
may spray all nearby high value elm trees with an effective elm bark beetle
destroying concentrate.
   B.   Spraying Activities: Spraying activities authorized by this section
shall be conducted in accordance with technical and expert opinions and plans
of the commissioner of agriculture and under the supervision of the
commissioner and his agents whenever possible.
   C.   Notice: The notice provisions of section
4-5-6 of this chapter apply to spraying operations conducted under this
section. (1982 Code § 8.6109)
4-5-8: TRANSPORTING WOOD:
It is unlawful for any person to transport within the city any bark bearing elm
wood without having obtained a permit from the tree inspector. The tree
inspector shall grant such permits only when the purposes of this chapter will
be served thereby. (1982 Code § 8.6110)
4-5-9: INTERFERENCE:
It is unlawful for any person to prevent, delay or interfere with the tree
inspector or his agents while they are engaged in the performance of duties
imposed by this chapter. (1982 Code § 8.6111)
4-5-10: PENALTY:
Any person who violates section
4-5-8 or
4-5-9 of this chapter is guilty of a misdemeanor and may be punished by a fine
as provided in the general penalty in subsection 1-4-1B of this code. (1982
Code § 8.6112; amd. 2005 Code)
CHAPTER 6
WEEDS
SECTION:
4-6-1: Certain Weeds Prohibited
4-6-2: Certain Growths Prohibited
4-6-3: Weed Inspector
4-6-4: Notice And Removal By City
4-6-1: CERTAIN WEEDS PROHIBITED:
No person owning, occupying or in control of any property within the city shall
permit any ragweed, poison ivy, poison oak, poison sumac or any other noxious
weed to grow on it. (1982 Code § 8.631)
4-6-2: CERTAIN GROWTHS PROHIBITED:
All property owners, or persons occupying or in charge of any property, within
the city shall be responsible for the removal, cutting, or disposal and
elimination of weeds, grasses and rank vegetation or other uncontrolled plant
growth (generally referred to as plant matter) on their property, which at the
time of notice, is in excess of eight inches (8") in height. In addition, all
property owners, or persons occupying or in charge of any property, within the
city shall not allow clippings to remain on any city street, sidewalk or other
public property.
Any person, including the city, who believes there is property located within
the corporate limits of the city which has growing plant matter or clippings in
violation of this section shall make a complaint with the city clerk.
Upon receiving notice of the probable existence of plant matter or clippings in
violation of this section, the city shall inspect the property. If the property
is found to be in violation of this section, the property owner or the person
occupying the property shall be notified in writing of the violation.
The property owner may appeal by filing written notice of objections with the
city council within forty eight (48) hours of the notice, excluding weekends
and holidays.
In the event that the property owner shall fail to abate the violation within
five (5) regular business days and has not filed notice within forty eight (48)
hours to the city clerk of an intent to appeal, the city may employ the
services of city employees or outside contractors and remove the plant matter
to conform with this section by all lawful means. The property owner shall be
responsible for reimbursing the city for the full cost of abatement by outside
contractor or city employees at a rate established by city council resolution.
The city is not required to provide additional notices if the property owner
fails to abate the violation or otherwise appear on the matter for any
subsequent violations during the year.
All sums payable by the property owner may be collected as a special assessment
as provided by Minnesota statutes section 429.101, as it may be amended from
time to time. (Ord.
4-6-2, 8-5-2014)
4-6-3: WEED INSPECTOR:
Pursuant to the requirements of Minnesota Statutes Annotated section 18.80, the
mayor is hereby designated as weed inspector. The weed inspector may appoint
one or more assistant weed inspectors who shall have all the powers and
authority of the weed inspector. The weed inspector shall have such powers and
duties as are imposed by law or by this code. (1982 Code § 8.633)
4-6-4: NOTICE AND REMOVAL BY CITY:
Whenever any person fails to cut, destroy or otherwise eradicate any weeds or
other growths prohibited in this chapter, the weed inspector may cause them to
be cut, destroyed or otherwise eradicated. In doing so, the weed inspector
shall give notice to the owner, occupant or person in charge in accordance with
the requirements of Minnesota Statutes Annotated 18.83 and other applicable
laws. The cost and expense of the work done shall become a lien in favor of the
city and may be collected in the manner specified in Minnesota Statutes
Annotated 18.83 and other applicable laws. (1982 Code § 8.634)
CHAPTER 7
HANDBILLS AND NEWSPAPERS
SECTION:
4-7-1: Definitions
4-7-2: Distribution
4-7-3: Newspapers
4-7-4: Posting Handbills
4-7-5: Merchant Liability
4-7-6: Nuisance Declared
4-7-1: DEFINITIONS:
As used in this chapter, the following terms shall have the meaning given to
them:
COMMERCIAL HANDBILL: Any handbill which:
   A.   Advertises for sale any merchandise, produce, commodity or thing;
   B.   Directs attention to any business, mercantile or commercial
establishment, or to any other activity, for the purpose of directly or
indirectly promoting the interest of the establishment or activity by
increasing its sales;
   C.   Directs attention to or advertises any meeting, performance, exhibition
or other event for which an admission fee will be charged or collection taken
up for private gain or profit, but not for which the admission fee will be
charged or collection will be taken up for the purpose of defraying the
expenses incident to the event; or
   D.   While containing reading matter other than advertising, is
predominately and essentially an advertisement and is distributed for
advertising purposes or for the gain of any person engaged in advertising in or
distributing it.
HANDBILL: Any printed, written or reproduced bill, announcement, notice,
circular, dodger, leaflet, pamphlet, booklet or similar matter designed or
actually used for distribution to others of the information contained in or on
it by handing it to others, by posting it, or by leaving it upon or at any
property to be seen or picked up and examined, but it does not include any such
item distributed by mail or any newspaper.
NEWSPAPER: Any newspaper of general circulation as defined by law, any
newspaper duly entered with the United States postal service, any newspaper
filed and recorded with any officer as provided by law, and any periodical or
magazine regularly published with not less than four (4) issues per year and
sold to the public.
NONCOMMERCIAL HANDBILL: Any handbill not included in the definition of a
commercial handbill.
PRIVATE PREMISES: Any dwelling, building or other structure designed or used
wholly or in part for private residential purposes, whether inhabited or
temporarily or continuously uninhabited or vacant, and includes any driveway,
porch, steps, vestibule or mailbox belonging or appurtenant to the structure.
PUBLIC PARK: Any park, reservation, playground, beach, recreation center or any
other public area owned or used by the city and devoted to active or passive
recreation.
PUBLIC PLACE: Any street, sidewalk, boulevard, alley, public way, or any public
park, square, spaces, grounds, or buildings. (1982 Code § 7.341)
4-7-2: DISTRIBUTION:
   A.   Public Places: No person shall place, deposit or otherwise distribute a
handbill into or upon any public place, except by handing or transmitting
without charge a noncommercial handbill to a person willing to accept it. (1982
Code § 7.342)
   B.   Vehicles: No person shall place, deposit or otherwise distribute a
handbill into or upon any vehicle except by handing or transmitting without
charge a noncommercial handbill to an occupant of a vehicle willing to accept
it. (1982 Code § 7.343)
   C.   Uninhabited Or Vacant Premises: No person shall place, deposit or
otherwise distribute any handbill in or upon any private premises which are
temporarily or continuously uninhabited or vacant. (1982 Code § 7.344)
   D.   Posted Premises: No person shall place, deposit or otherwise distribute
any handbill in or upon any private premises conspicuously posted near the
entrance with a sign stating "No Trespassing", "No Peddlers", "No
Advertisements" or any other message indicating that the occupants do not want
to be disturbed, to have their privacy disturbed or to have any handbills left.
(1982 Code § 7.345)
   E.   Unposted Inhabited Premises: No person shall place, deposit or
otherwise distribute any handbill in or upon any inhabited private premises
which are not posted as provided in subsection 4-7-3D of this section if
requested by any person there not to do so. Otherwise, a handbill shall be
distributed at any unposted inhabited premises only by handing or transmitting
the handbill to a person then present at the premises or by securely placing
the handbill upon the premises so as to prevent it from being blown or carried
about or off the premises by the elements. Mailboxes may not be used if to do
so would violate federal law or regulations. (1982 Code § 7.346)
4-7-3: NEWSPAPERS:
Unless the newspaper is mailed, a newspaper shall be placed, deposited or
otherwise distributed at or to any premises only by handing or transmitting it
to a person then present at the premises or by securely placing it upon the
premises so as to prevent it from being blown or carried about or off the
premises by the elements. (1982 Code § 7.347)
4-7-4: POSTING HANDBILLS:
No person shall post or affix any handbill, notice, poster or other device
calculated to attract the attention of the public upon any public structure or
building, except as may be authorized or required by law; nor upon the property
of another, except by permission of that person. (1982 Code § 7.348)
4-7-5: MERCHANT LIABILITY:
Any merchant who advertises goods, wares or merchandise by causing the
advertising material to be distributed in violation of any of the provisions of
this chapter shall be guilty of violating this code to the same extent as the
person distributing the material. (1982 Code § 7.349)
4-7-6: NUISANCE DECLARED:
Each of the acts forbidden in this chapter are hereby declared to be a
nuisance. Any duly authorized city officer or employee may take such action as
may be proper to prevent, restrain, correct or abate any such nuisance. (1982
Code § 7.350)
TITLE 5
POLICE REGULATIONS
CHAPTER 1
POLICE DEPARTMENT
SECTION:
5-1-1: Establishment
5-1-2: Chief Of Police
5-1-3: Membership
5-1-4: Duties
5-1-1: ESTABLISHMENT:
There shall be a police department. (1982 Code § 2.411)
5-1-2: CHIEF OF POLICE:
The head of the police department shall be known as the chief of police. The
chief shall be appointed by the city council, receive such compensation as the
city council may fix, and serve at the pleasure of the city council subject to
supervisory authority of the city manager. The chief shall supervise the
operation of the police department and shall have such other powers and duties
and keep such records as are prescribed by law, by charter, by this code and as
the city council may determine. (1982 Code § 2.412)
5-1-3: MEMBERSHIP:
The number of additional members of the department, together with their ranks
and titles, shall be determined by the city council. The compensation to be
paid to members of the police department shall be fixed by the city council.
Members of the department shall be appointed by the city council. (1982 Code §
2.413)
5-1-4: DUTIES:
Members of the police department shall enforce the ordinances and laws
applicable to the city, prevent crimes, protect lives and property, maintain
the peace, serve process on behalf of the city, and have such additional powers
and duties as are prescribed by law, by charter, by this code and as the city
council may determine. (1982 Code § 2.414)
CHAPTER 2
WEAPONS 1
SECTION:
5-2-1: Prohibited Use; Exception
5-2-2: Law Enforcement Officers
 
Notes
1 1. MSA §§ 609.66, 624.71 et seq.
5-2-1: PROHIBITED USE; EXCEPTION:
No person shall aim, or threaten to fire or discharge, any rifle, pistol,
shotgun or other firearm, any air or gas rifle or pistol, and slingshot, any
bow and arrow or any other weapon or device for the propelling of missiles or
pellets which are capable of harming persons or property, whether loaded or
not, at any human being or at the property of another. These prohibitions shall
not apply:
   A.   Target Or Shooting Range: To aiming or firing or discharging at a
target located or thrown for such purpose when lawfully at an established
target or shooting range and exercising due regard for the rights and safety of
others and their property; or
   B.   Protection Of Person Or Property: When the aiming, firing or
discharging is reasonably necessary in the defense of one's person or property
or that of others. (1982 Code § 8.231)
5-2-2: LAW ENFORCEMENT OFFICERS:
The provisions of this chapter shall not apply to law enforcement officers or
other duly authorized persons whenever the lawful duties of their office or
occupation require them to carry loaded firearms or to perform an act which
conflicts with the provisions of this chapter. (1982 Code § 8.232)
CHAPTER 3
ANIMAL CONTROL
ARTICLE A. GENERAL PROVISIONS
SECTION:
5-3A-1: Keeper Deemed Owner
5-3A-2: Animals At Large
5-3A-3: Certain Animals Restricted
5-3A-3-1: Chicken Restrictions
5-3A-4: Manner Of Keeping
5-3A-5: Sanitation
5-3A-6: Dead Or Diseased Animals
5-3A-7: Cruelty To Animals
5-3A-1: KEEPER DEEMED OWNER:
Any person who keeps an animal on or about the person's premises shall be
deemed the owner of the animal for purposes of this chapter. This shall not
relieve the actual owner of the animal of any responsibilities or liabilities
imposed by this chapter. (1982 Code § 8.511)
5-3A-2: ANIMALS AT LARGE:
No person who is the owner, keeper or person in charge of any horse, mule,
donkey, cattle, sheep, goat, swine, rabbit, chicken, geese, duck or turkey
shall permit the same to be at large within the city. (1982 Code § 8.512)
5-3A-3: CERTAIN ANIMALS RESTRICTED:
No person shall keep or allow to be kept on premises owned or occupied by such
person, within the platted portion of the city, any horse, mule, donkey,
cattle, sheep, goat, swine, rabbit, chicken, geese, duck or turkey. An
exception shall be made to this section by allowing the keeping of chickens on
premises in the city subject to the provisions set forth in section
5-3A-3-1 of this article. (Ord. 293, 5-17-2011)
5-3A-3-1: CHICKEN RESTRICTIONS:
   A.   Chickens Limited: It is unlawful for any person to own, control, keep
or maintain or harbor hen chickens on any residential premises in the city
unless issued a permit to do so as provided herein. In the case of rental
residential property, including multi-family residential property, written
permission must be given by the property owner for a tenant to keep or harbor
chickens on said residential premises. No permit shall be issued for the
keeping or harboring of more than six (6) hen chickens on any premises. The
keeping of roosters is prohibited.
   B.   Definitions:
    AT LARGE: A chicken out of its chicken run, off the premises or not under
the custody and control of the owner.
   CHICKEN: A female chicken or hen.
   CHICKEN COOP: A structure providing housing for chickens made of wood or
other similar materials that provides shelter from the elements.
   CHICKEN RUN: A fenced outside yard for the keeping and exercising of
chickens.
   OWNER: The resident, property owner, custodian or keeper of any chicken.
   PREMISES: Any platted lot or group of contiguous lots, parcels or tracts of
land.
   C.   Permit: No person shall maintain a chicken coop and/or chicken run
unless granted a permit by the city. The permit shall be subject to all terms
and conditions of this section and any additional conditions deemed necessary
by the city to protect the public health, safety and welfare. The necessary
permit may be obtained from the city manager's office. Included with the
information required prior to issuance of the permit must be a scaled diagram
that indicates the location of any chicken coop and run, and the approximate
size and distance from adjoining structures and property lines. The owner must
also obtain written approval of the keeping of chickens from all abutting
owners. A permit for the keeping of chickens may be revoked or suspended by the
council for any violation of this section following written notice and a public
hearing. An annual fee of ten dollars ($10.00) will be charged for each permit
which shall expire on December 31 of each year.
   D.   Confinement: Every person who owns, controls, keeps, maintains or
harbors hen chickens must keep them confined on the premises at all times in a
chicken coop or chicken run while in the city. Any coop and run shall be
screened with a solid fence or landscaped buffer with a minimum height of four
feet (4'). Any coop and run shall be at least twenty five feet (25') from any
residential structure or any other premises on any adjacent lots.
   E.   Chicken Coops And Chicken Runs:
      1.   All chicken coops and runs must be located within the rear yard
subject to the required setbacks for the principal building and at least twenty
five feet (25') from any dwelling or any other premises on any adjacent lots.
All chicken coops must be a minimum of four (4) square feet per chicken in
size, must not exceed ten (10) square feet per chicken in size and must not
exceed six feet (6') in total height. Attached fenced in chicken runs must not
exceed twenty (20) square feet per chicken and fencing must not exceed six feet
(6') in total height. Chicken runs may be enclosed with wood and/or woven wire
materials, and may allow chickens to contact the ground. Chicken feed must be
kept in metal, predator proof containers. Chicken manure shall not be placed in
yard compost piles.
      2.   Chicken coops must either be:
         a.   Elevated with a clear open space of at least twenty four inches
(24") between the ground surface and framing/floor of the coop; or
         b.   The coop floor, foundation and footings must be constructed using
rodent resistant concrete construction.
      3.   Chicken coops are not allowed to be located in any part of a home
and/or garage.
      4.   Chickens must be secured in a chicken coop from sunset to sunrise
each day.
   F.   Conditions And Inspection: No person who owns, controls, keeps,
maintains or harbors hen chickens shall permit the premises where the hen
chickens are kept to be or remain in an unhealthy, unsanitary or noxious
condition or to permit the premises to be in such condition that noxious odors
are carried to adjacent public or private property. Any chicken coop and
chicken run authorized by permit under this section may be inspected at any
reasonable time by an agent of the city. Slaughter and breeding of chickens on
any premises within the city is prohibited.
   G.   Violations: Any person who owns, controls, keeps, maintains or harbors
hen chickens in the city limits of Dawson without obtaining or maintaining a
current permit or after a permit has been suspended or revoked by council
action shall be guilty of a petty misdemeanor. (Ord. 293, 5-17-2011)
5-3A-4: MANNER OF KEEPING 1 :
No person shall keep any dog, cat, or any other animal in the city which
constitutes a nuisance or disturbance by reason of barking, crying, howling,
fighting, or other noise, or in such a way as to permit the animal to annoy,
injure or endanger any person or property, or in any other way contrary to law
or the provisions of this chapter. (1982 Code § 8.514)
 
Notes
1 1. See also section 5-3C-5 of this chapter.
5-3A-5: SANITATION:
Every structure and yard in which animals are kept shall be maintained in a
clean and sanitary condition and free of all rodents, vermin and objectionable
odors. Manure shall be removed with sufficient frequency to avoid nuisance from
odors or from the breeding of flies. Unless used for fertilizer, manure shall
be removed beyond the city. If used for fertilizer, manure shall be spread upon
the ground evenly and turned under at once or as soon as the frost leaves the
ground. (1982 Code § 8.515)
5-3A-6: DEAD OR DISEASED ANIMALS:
   A.   Disposal Of Dead Animals: Dead animals shall be disposed of in a
sanitary manner as soon as possible after the death of the animal. No person
shall sell, offer for sale, or give away for human consumption the carcass of
any dead animal.
   B.   Contagious Disease: Any animal with a contagious disease shall be
securely confined so that it cannot come within fifty feet (50') of any public
roadway or any place where animals belonging to or kept by another are kept. No
owner or person having charge of any animal, knowing it to have any infectious
or contagious disease, or to have recently been exposed thereto, shall sell,
barter or dispose of the animal to any person without so informing the person.
(1982 Code § 8.516)
5-3A-7: CRUELTY TO ANIMALS:
No person shall unlawfully kill, poison, maim, entice, carry away or otherwise
harm any animal. No person owning or having control over any animal shall treat
the animal in a cruel or inhumane manner, deprive the animal of necessary food
or water, fail to provide the animal with sufficient shelter and care in cold
or inclement weather, or abandon the animal. (1982 Code § 8.517)
ARTICLE B. IMPOUNDMENT
SECTION:
5-3B-1: City Pound; Poundmaster
5-3B-2: Impoundment
5-3B-3: Notice
5-3B-4: Records
5-3B-5: Redemption
5-3B-6: Unclaimed Cats And Dogs
5-3B-7: Other Unclaimed Animals
5-3B-8: Interference With Impoundment
5-3B-1: CITY POUND; POUNDMASTER:
   A.   Poundmaster:
      1.   Chief Of Police: The chief of police shall be poundmaster.
      2.   Duties: The poundmaster shall maintain or cause to be maintained the
city pound and perform all other duties imposed upon the poundmaster by law or
by this code.
   B.   City Pound:
      1.   Maintenance: The poundmaster shall maintain the city pound at such
location within or outside the city as may be suitable.
      2.   Proper Care And Sustenance: The poundmaster shall provide proper
care and sustenance for every animal impounded.
      3.   Facilities: The poundmaster may, whenever suitable city impounding
facilities are not available, contract with any veterinarian, kennel or other
private person or public facility for the keeping of impounded animals. (1982
Code § 8.531)
5-3B-2: IMPOUNDMENT:
The poundmaster or any police officer may take up and impound in the city pound
any animal running at large, any cat or dog found not wearing a proper cat or
dog license tag, any dog not muzzled when muzzling is required, any animal kept
in violation of law or of this code, or any animal lawfully delivered for
impounding. (Ord. 209, 8-7-1990)
5-3B-3: NOTICE:
   A.   Owner Known: Upon delivery of any animal to the pound, the poundmaster
shall, without delay, notify the owner, personally or through United States
mail, if the owner is known or can be ascertained with reasonable effort.
   B.   Unknown Owner: If the owner is unknown or cannot be ascertained with
reasonable effort, the poundmaster shall post written notice in three (3)
public places in the city, one of them at the pound, describing the animal,
stating where it is impounded and the conditions upon which it will be
released. (1982 Code § 8.533)
5-3B-4: RECORDS:
The poundmaster shall maintain, in a form permitting easy examination by the
public, and keep, for at least such time as may be required, such records as
are required by law and as are otherwise reasonably necessary for proper
operation of the pound. (1982 Code § 8.534)
5-3B-5: REDEMPTION:
   A.   Viewing Impounded Animals: Any person may view the animals impounded at
any time during which the pound is open to the public.
   B.   Redemption By Owner: Except as otherwise provided by law, any animal
may be redeemed from the pound by its owner upon payment of actual costs of
care, including kennel fees, veterinarian fees and all other charges.
   C.   Unlicensed Animal: If any animal for which licensing is required was
unlicensed, the owner shall furnish a receipt showing payment of the required
license fee and any applicable penalties.
   D.   Proof Of Compliance: If the animal was impounded for being kept in
violation of law or of this code, the owner shall show satisfactory proof that
the animal will be kept in accordance with the provisions of law or of this
code previously violated. (1982 Code § 8.535)
5-3B-6: UNCLAIMED CATS AND DOGS:
Any cat or dog which is not redeemed within the time allowed in the notice,
such time shall not be less than five (5) business days for dogs and two (2)
business days for cats, may be sold for not less than the amount required upon
redemption of the cat or dog by the owner, unless the cat or dog is required
for scientific research by a licensed institution under Minnesota Statutes
Annotated section 35.71. All sums received beyond the fees specified in section
5-3B-5 of this article shall be paid to the owner if the owner makes a claim
within sixty (60) days of the sale and furnishes satisfactory proof of
ownership. Any unclaimed cat or dog shall be killed in a proper and humane
manner. (Ord. 209, 8-7-1990; amd. Ord. 249, 5-7-2002)
5-3B-7: OTHER UNCLAIMED ANIMALS:
   A.   Redemption Period: Unclaimed animals, other than dogs, shall be held
for redemption for at least six (6) business days.
   B.   Sale: Any animal which is not redeemed within that time shall be sold
if required by law and proceeds disposed of according to law. If sale is not
governed by law, and if the animal is not requested by a licensed institution
for scientific research pursuant to Minnesota Statutes Annotated section 35.71,
the animal may be sold in any manner calculated to bring the best price.
   C.   Excess Proceeds: All sums received from the sale of such animal less
the fees specified in section
5-3B-5 of this article shall be paid to the owner, if the owner makes a claim
within sixty (60) days of the sale and furnishes satisfactory proof of
ownership.
   D.   Humane Disposal: Any animal not claimed or sold shall be killed in a
proper and humane manner. (1982 Code § 8.537)
5-3B-8: INTERFERENCE WITH IMPOUNDMENT:
No unauthorized person shall remove from the pound any impounded animal, nor
shall any unauthorized person break open the pound or release any animals from
it. No person shall hinder, delay, or obstruct any duly authorized official or
other person lawfully in the process of impounding any animal. (1982 Code §
8.538)
ARTICLE C. CATS AND DOGS 1
SECTION:
5-3C-1: Running At Large
5-3C-2: Vicious Cats Or Dogs
5-3C-3: Quarantine
5-3C-4: Muzzling
5-3C-5: Creating Nuisance
5-3C-6: Impoundment
5-3C-7: Licenses
5-3C-8: Penalty
 
Notes
1 1. MSA ch. 347.
5-3C-1: RUNNING AT LARGE:
No person owning, keeping or having the control of any cat or dog shall permit
it to run at large within the city. A cat or dog shall not be deemed to be
running at large if on a leash, if in a motor vehicle, if within a confinement,
if at all times under the control of an accompanying person, or if upon the
premises of the owner or keeper of the cat or dog. (Ord. 209, 8-7-1990)
5-3C-2: VICIOUS CATS OR DOGS:
No person shall keep within the city any vicious cat or dog. The poundmaster or
any police officer may immediately confine any vicious cat or dog not confined
on its owner's premises or kill any such cat or dog when the cat or dog cannot
be safely taken up and impounded. (Ord. 209, 8-7-1990)
5-3C-3: QUARANTINE:
   A.   Biting Animal: Any cat or dog which bites a person shall be quarantined
for such time as may be directed by the city health officer.
   B.   Confinement: During quarantine the animal shall be securely confined
and kept from contact with any other animal. The owner shall bear all
quarantine costs. At the discretion of the health officer, the quarantine may
be on the premises of the owner.
   C.   Destruction Of Animal: Unless necessary for public safety, no
quarantined cat or dog shall be killed until so ordered by the health officer.
(Ord. 209, 8-7-1990)
5-3C-4: MUZZLING:
   A.   Proclamation: If, upon investigation, it is determined that the
presence of rabies jeopardizes the public health and safety, the mayor or city
health officer, or such other officer as is authorized by law, shall issue a
proclamation ordering every person owning or keeping a dog which is not
confined to muzzle it securely so that it cannot bite any other animal or any
person.
   B.   Violation: No person shall violate the proclamation. Any unmuzzled dog
unrestrained during the time fixed in the proclamation may be impounded as
provided in this chapter or killed as provided by law. (1982 Code § 8.554)
5-3C-5: CREATING NUISANCE 1 :
No person shall:
   A.   Keep any cat or dog which habitually or frequently barks, fights, cries
or howls.
   B.   Keep any cat or dog which chases vehicles or molests or annoys any
person lawfully upon any public way.
   C.   Allow any cat or dog to damage, defile or destroy any public or private
property. (Ord. 209, 8-7-1990)
 
Notes
1 1. See also section 5-3A-4 of this chapter.
5-3C-6: IMPOUNDMENT:
Cats or dogs kept or running in violation of this code may be impounded as
otherwise provided in this code 1 . (Ord. 209, 8-7-1990)
 
Notes
1 2. See article B of this chapter.
5-3C-7: LICENSES:
   A.   License Required; Exception: No person shall keep any cat or dog more
than six (6) months old within the city without having licensed the cat or dog
as required in this section. No license shall be required for any cat or dog
owned by a person not a resident of the city and brought temporarily into the
city for not to exceed thirty (30) days. (Ord. 209, 8-7-1990)
   B.   Application: Application shall be made in writing in the form
prescribed by the city clerk on or before May 1 for a two (2) year license for
that license year and the next license year. If any person acquires a cat or
dog after May 1, or if any person has a cat or dog which becomes six (6) months
old after May 1, the person shall apply for a license for the cat or dog within
thirty (30) days after the cat or dog is acquired or becomes six (6) months
old. (Ord. 304, 5-22-2013)
   C.   Fees; Costs: The city council shall, by resolution, establish dog
license fees. The city council shall also, by resolution, set a structure for
violations consisting of fees, fine and costs and the council shall also
establish that compliance and enforcement be managed through the police
department. (Ord. 232, 6-2-1998)
   D.   Certificate Of Veterinarian: Every application for a license shall be
accompanied by a certificate from a qualified veterinarian showing that the cat
or dog has been vaccinated for rabies within two (2) years previously. (Ord.
209, 8-7-1990)
   E.   Issuance; Record: Upon proper application and payment of the required
fees, the city clerk shall issue a license and shall issue to the owner a metal
tag for each license. The city clerk shall keep a record of all licenses
issued. (1982 Code § 8.575)
   F.   Term: A license shall be valid for two (2) years or the part of the
license year for which it is issued and shall expire on April 30 of the next
year following its issuance. (Ord. 304, 5-22-2013)
   G.   Transfer: No license or license tag issued for one cat or dog shall be
transferable to another cat or dog. The sale or transfer of any licensed cat or
dog shall transfer the license to the new owner.
   H.   Tags:
      1.   Collar: The licensee shall attach the tag to the collar of the cat
or dog licensed so that the tag may be easily seen. The licensee shall see that
the tag is worn at all times by the cat or dog.
      2.   Removal Of Tag: No person, except the licensee or the licensee's
authorized agent, shall remove any license tag from a cat or dog collar or
remove any collar with a license attached to it from any cat or dog.
      3.   Invalid License: No person shall place on any cat or dog a
fictitious, altered or invalid license tag, or a license tag not issued for
that cat or dog, nor shall any person keep any cat or dog wearing such tag.
(Ord. 209, 8-7-1990)
5-3C-8: PENALTY:
   A.   First Violation: Owner is responsible for all impound fees. If the
animal is not licensed, violators must pay fees and show documentation of
proper vaccinations, or have proper vaccinations administered before animal is
released. Twenty five dollar ($25.00) fine, plus all fees as stated in this
subsection.
   B.   Second Violation: Add a ten dollar ($10.00) fee to the twenty five
dollar ($25.00) fine for each time, plus all fees as stated in this section.
   C.   Enforcement: Compliance and enforcement shall be managed by the police
department. (Ord. 287, 10-5-2010)
CHAPTER 4
FAIR HOUSING 1
SECTION:
5-4-1: Purpose
5-4-2: Policy
5-4-3: Definitions
5-4-4: Prohibited Acts
5-4-5: Enforcement Procedures
5-4-6: Statute Of Limitations
5-4-7: Civil Enforcement Procedure
 
Notes
1 1. MSA ch. 363.
5-4-1: PURPOSE:
The city desires to affirm compliance with federal and state fair housing
legislation; and the city desires to resolve fair housing discrimination
complaints violations locally; therefore, the following is set forth as the
DAWSON FAIR HOUSING ORDINANCE. (1982 Code § 8.710)
5-4-2: POLICY:
Status with regard to public assistance and discrimination with regard to
housing on the basis of race, sex, creed, religion, marital status, and
disability adversely affects the health, welfare, peace, and safety of the
community. Persons subject to such discrimination suffer depressed living
conditions, and create conditions which endanger the public peace and order.
The public policy of the city is declared to be to foster equal opportunity for
all to obtain decent, safe and sanitary housing without regard to their race,
creed, color, national origin, marital status, disability status, sex, and
strictly in accord with their individual merits as human beings. It is also the
policy of the city to protect all persons from all unfounded charges of
discrimination. (1982 Code § 8.711)
5-4-3: DEFINITIONS:
For the purposes of this chapter, the following terms, phrases, words and their
deviations, shall have the meaning given herein unless the context otherwise
indicates:
DISABILITY: A mental or physical condition which constitutes a handicap.
Nothing in this chapter shall be construed to prohibit any program, service,
facility or privilege afforded to a person with a disability which is intended
to habilitate, rehabilitate or accommodate that person.
DISCRIMINATE OR DISCRIMINATION: Includes segregate or separate.
HRA: Housing redevelopment agency.
MARITAL STATUS: The standing, state or condition of one as single or married
person. (1982 Code § 8.712)
5-4-4: PROHIBITED ACTS:
It shall be an unlawful discriminatory practice and a misdemeanor offense:
   A.   Sale, Lease Or Rental: For any person to discriminate on the grounds of
race, creed, religion, color, sex, marital status, status with regard to public
assistance, national origin, age or disability, in the sale, lease, or rental
of any housing unit or units.
   B.   Broker, Agent, Or Salesman: For any broker, agent, salesperson or other
person acting in behalf of another to so discriminate in the sale, lease, or
rental of any housing unit or units belonging to such other person.
   C.   Financial; Insurance: For any person engaged in the business of
financing the purchase, rehabilitation, remodeling or repair of housing units
or in the business of selling insurance with respect to housing units to refuse
to provide such financing or insurance or to discriminate with regard to the
terms or conditions thereof by reason of the race, color, sex, religion, creed,
national origin, marital status, status with regard to public assistance, age
or disability of the applicant or because of the location of the unit or units
in areas of the city occupied by persons of a particular race, color, sex,
religion, creed, national origin, marital status, status with regard to public
assistance, age or disability; or to discriminate by treating differently any
person or group of persons who desire to purchase, lease, acquire, construct,
rehabilitate, repair or maintain real property in a specific urban area because
of social, economic or environmental conditions of the area in the granting,
withholding, extending, modifying or renewing, or in the rates, terms,
conditions or privileges of any such financial assistance or in the extension
of services in connection therewith. The bona fide programs of federal, state
or local governmental units or agencies, however structured or authorized to
upgrade or improve in any manner a specific urban area, shall not be deemed to
be a violation of this section.
   D.   Facilities, Services Or Privileges Of Occupancy: For any person having
sold, leased, or rented a housing unit or units to any person to discriminate
with respect to facilities, services, or privileges of occupancy by reason of
race, color, sex, creed, religion, national origin, age or disability, marital
status or status with regard to public assistance.
   E.   Make Or Publish Statement: For any person to make or publish any
statement evidencing an intent to discriminate, on grounds of race, creed,
religion, color, sex, national origin or ancestry, marital status, status with
regard to public assistance, age or disability, in the sale, lease, or rental
of a housing unit or units.
   F.   Inquiry: For any person to make any inquiry regarding race, color, sex,
creed, religion, national origin, marital status, status with regard to public
assistance, age or disability, or to keep any record or use any form of
application, designed to elicit such information, in connection with the sale,
lease, rental or financing of a housing unit or units.
   G.   Inducement: For any person, for the purpose of inducing a real estate
transaction from which he may benefit financially:
      1.   To represent that a change has occurred or will or may occur in the
composition of the block, neighborhood, or area in which the property is
located, in respect to the race, color, sex, creed, religion, national origin,
marital status, status with regard to public assistance, age or disability of
those living there; or
      2.   To represent that this change will or may result in the lowering of
property values, an increase in crime, or antisocial behavior, or a decline in
the quality of schools in the block, neighborhood, or area concerned.
   H.   Interpretation Of Provisions: Nothing in this chapter shall be
construed to required any person or group of persons selling, renting or
leasing property to modify the property in any way, or exercise a higher degree
of care for a person having a disability than for a person who does not have a
disability; nor shall this chapter be construed to relieve any person of any
obligation generally imposed on all persons regardless of any disability in a
written lease, rental agreement, or contract or purchase or sale, or to forbid
distinctions based on the inability to fulfill the terms and conditions,
including financial obligations of such lease, agreement or contract.
   I.   Exceptions: The provisions of this chapter shall not apply to:
      1.   The rental of a portion of a dwelling containing accommodations for
two (2) families, one of which is occupied by the owner; or
      2.   The rental by an owner or occupier of a one-family accommodation in
which he resides of a room or rooms in such accommodation to another person or
persons if the discrimination is by sex, marital status, status with regard to
public assistance or disability. Nothing in the chapter shall be construed to
require any person or group of persons selling, renting or leasing property to
modify the property in any way, or exercise a higher degree of care for a
person having a disability than for a person who does not have a disability;
nor shall this chapter be construed to relieve any person of any obligation
generally imposed on all persons regardless of any disability in a written
lease, rental agreement, or contract of purchase or sale, or to forbid
distinctions based on the inability to fulfill the terms and conditions,
including financial obligations, of such lease, agreement or contract. (1982
Code § 8.713)
5-4-5: ENFORCEMENT PROCEDURES:
   A.   Designation Of Authority: The housing and redevelopment authority in
and for the city is designated as the enforcement agency for this chapter and
shall have the power to receive, hear and determine complaints as provided
herein.
   B.   Investigation Of Complaints: The city manager or HRA shall promptly
investigate, upon complaint or upon his own motion, any violations of this
chapter.
   C.   Referral To City Attorney: If after investigation, he shall have reason
to believe a violation has occurred, he may refer the matter to the city
attorney for criminal prosecution, initiate civil enforcement procedures as
herein provided, or enter into a settlement agreement which, when approved by
the HRA, shall have the same force as the city order. (1982 Code § 8.714.)
5-4-6: STATUTE OF LIMITATIONS:
No action may be brought for civil enforcement or criminal prosecution unless
the charge of alleged discriminatory practice was filed with the city within
one hundred eighty (180) days from the occurrence of the practice. (1982 Code §
8.715)
5-4-7: CIVIL ENFORCEMENT PROCEDURE:
Civil enforcement procedures shall be prosecuted by the city attorney before
the HRA in the following manner:
   A.   Complaint: The city manager shall serve upon the respondent by
certified mail a complaint, signed by him, which shall set forth a clear and
concise statement of the facts constituting the violation, set a time and place
for hearing, and advise the respondent of his right to file an answer to appear
in person or by an attorney and to examine and cross examine witnesses.
   B.   Answer: The hearing shall not be less than twenty (20) days after
service of the complaint. At any time prior to the hearing, the respondent may
file an answer. Facts not denied by answer shall be deemed admitted. If the
answer sets out new matter, it shall be deemed denied by the HRA.
   C.   Amendment Of Pleadings: The complaint or answer may be amended at any
given time prior to the hearing, with the consent of the opposing party.
   D.   Hearing: Hearings shall be before the HRA.
   E.   Subpoenas: The HRA may obtain subpoenas from the district court to
compel the attendance of witnesses and the production of documents at any
hearing.
   F.   Findings; Order: If, after hearing, the panel shall conclude that a
violation has occurred, it shall prepare an order which may contain any
provision deemed desirable to do justice to the complainant or to prevent
further violations. It may include provisions which require the respondent to
rent, sell, or lease particular housing to the complainant or to do any other
thing as may be just. The panel's findings of fact and order shall be served on
the respondent and each member of the housing and redevelopment authority by
mail and shall become the findings and order of the HRA, unless, within ten
(10) days after mailing of the findings and order, the HRA shall revoke or
amend the order, but any order of a panel may be modified by the HRA at any
time. (1982 Code § 8.716)
CHAPTER 5
MINORS
SECTION:
5-5-1: Curfew
5-5-1: CURFEW:
   A.   Age Limitations:
      1.   Under Fifteen Years:
         a.   School Nights: Minors under fifteen (15) years of age shall not
be on or present at any public street, alley, park, playground or any other
public place, or place of business open to the public or any vacant property or
unsupervised place in the city between the hours of ten o'clock (10:00) P.M.
and five o'clock (5:00) A.M. of the following day, Sunday through Thursday
during the scheduled public school year.
         b.   Nonschool Nights: When the public school is not in session on the
following day such as summer vacation, holiday vacations, teacher workshops,
weekends, or any other days on which students are not required to be in school
attendance, the hours shall be between eleven o'clock (11:00) P.M. and five
o'clock (5:00) A.M. of the following day.
      2.   Fifteen To Eighteen:
         a.   School Nights: No person between fifteen (15) years of age and
under eighteen (18) years of age shall be on or present on any street, alley,
park, playground, or any other public place, or in any place of business open
to the public, or any vacant property or unsupervised place in the city between
the hours of eleven o'clock (11:00) P.M. and five o'clock (5:00) A.M. of the
following day, Sunday through Thursday during the scheduled public school year.
         b.   Nonschool Nights: When the public school is not in session on the
following day such as summer vacation, holiday vacations, teacher workshops,
weekends, or any other days on which students are not required to be in school
attendance, the hours shall be between twelve o'clock (12:00) midnight and five
o'clock (5:00) A.M. of the following day. (Ord. 206, 3-7-1989)
   B.   Exceptions: The provisions of subsection A of this section shall not
apply when the person under eighteen (18) years of age is accompanied by his or
her parent, guardian or other adult person having the care and custody of the
minor, or if the minor is upon an errand for which there exists a reasonable
necessity, or if the presence of the minor in the place or places is connected
with and required by some legitimate business, trade, profession or occupation
in which the minor is permitted by law to be engaged. (1982 Code § 8.913)
   C.   Responsible Persons:
      1.   Parents: No parent, guardian or other person having the lawful care
and custody of any person under eighteen (18) years of age shall allow or
permit that person to violate the provisions of subsection A of this section.
(1982 Code § 8.914)
      2.   Person In Charge Of Premises: No person in charge of any place of
amusement, entertainment or refreshment, or any other place of business, shall
permit any minor to be on or in such place in violation of subsection A of this
section. Whenever the person in charge of any such place finds a minor there in
violation of said subsection A of this section, the person in charge shall
immediately order the minor to leave. If the minor refuses to leave, the person
in charge shall immediately notify the police department. (1982 Code § 8.915)
   D.   Designated Nights: The chief of police, upon request of school
officials or other persons in charge of organizing and supervising educational,
athletic, musical, dramatic, religious, recreational or social activities of
minors, may designate certain nights and hours thereof as designated nights at
such time as the schools or other groups shall be engaged in educational,
athletic, musical, dramatic, religious, recreational or social activities for
the benefit or entertainment of persons under eighteen (18) years of age. In
that case, the provisions of subsection A of this section shall not apply to
any person under eighteen (18) years of age who is lawfully going to, attending
or returning from any function during the duly designated hours on a designated
night, but only for such period of time as is reasonably necessary for the
minor to go to, attend, and return from the function. In all other respects,
the provisions of subsection A of this section shall apply on a designated
night. (1982 Code § 8.916)
CHAPTER 6
PUBLIC USE OF CANNABIS
SECTION:
5-6-1: Purpose And Intent
5-6-2: Definitions
5-6-3: Prohibited Acts
5-6-4: Penalty
5-6-5: Severability
5-6-1:PURPOSE AND INTENT:
This chapter is adopted by the City of Dawson for the purpose of protecting
public health and safety by regulating/prohibiting the use of cannabis and
cannabis derived products in public places and places of public accommodation
within the City.
Minnesota Session Law 2023, Chapter 63, effective in relevant part August 1,
2023, establishes that the adult use, possession and personal growing of
cannabis is legal subject to the requirements and restrictions of Minnesota
Statutes.
Minnesota Session Law 2023, Chapter 63, Art. 4, section 19, codified as Minn.
Stat. 342.0263, subd. 5 authorizes the adoption of a local ordinance
establishing a petty misdemeanor offense for public use of cannabis.
The City intends to be proactive in protecting public health and safety by
enacting an ordinance that will mitigate threats presented to the public and
public health by the public use of cannabis.
The City of Dawson (hereinafter "the City") recognizes the risks that
unintended access and use of cannabis products and exposure to cannabis and its
effects present to the health, welfare, and safety of members of the public and
in particular the youth of the City. (Ord. 324, 10-3-2023)
5-6-2: DEFINITIONS:
Except as may otherwise be provided or clearly implied by context, all terms
shall be given their commonly accepted definitions. The following words, terms,
and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to
them except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning.
ADULT-USE CANNABIS FLOWER: A cannabis flower that is approved for sale by the
Minnesota Office of Cannabis Management or is substantially similar to a
product approved by the office. Adult-use cannabis flower does not include
medical cannabis flower, hemp plant parts, or hemp-derived consumer products.
ADULT-USE CANNABIS PRODUCTS: A cannabis product that is approved for sale by
the office or is substantially similar to a product approved by the office.
Adult-use cannabis product includes edible cannabis products but does not
include medical cannabinoid products or lower-potency hemp edibles.
CANNABIS FLOWER: The harvested flower, bud, leaves, and stems of a cannabis
plant. Cannabis flower includes adult-use cannabis flower and medical cannabis
flower. Cannabis flower does not include cannabis seed, hemp plant parts, or
hemp-derived consumer products.
CANNABIS PRODUCT: Any of the following:
   (1)   Cannabis concentrate;
   (2)   A product infused with cannabinoids, including but not limited to
tetrahydrocannabinol, extracted or derived from cannabis plants or cannabis
flower; or
   (3)   Any other product that contains cannabis concentrate.
HEMP DERIVED CONSUMER PRODUCTS:
   (1)   A product intended for human or animal consumption, does not contain
cannabis flower or cannabis concentrate, and:
      (a)   Contains or consists of hemp plant parts; or
      (b)   Contains hemp concentrate or artificially derived cannabinoids in
combination with other ingredients.
   (2)   Hemp-derived consumer products does not include artificially derived
cannabinoids, lower-potency hemp edibles, hemp-derived topical products, hemp
fiber products, or hemp grain.
LOWER-POTENCY HEMP EDIBLE:Any product that:
   (1)   Is intended to be eaten or consumed as a beverage by humans;
   (2)   Contains hemp concentrate or an artificially derived cannabinoid; in
combination with food ingredients;
   (3)   Is not a drug;
   (4)   Consists of servings that contain no more than five milligrams of
delta-9 tetrahydrocannabinol, 25 milligrams of cannabinol, 25 milligrams of
cannabinol, or any combination of those cannabinoids that does not exceed the
identified amounts;
   (5)   Does not contain more than a combined total of 0.5 milligrams of all
other cannabinoids per serving;
   (6)   Does not contain an artificially derived cannabinoid other than delta-
9 tetrahydrocannabinol;
   (7)   Does not contain a cannabinoid derived from cannabis plants or
cannabis flower; and
   (8)   Is a type of product approved for sale by the office or is
substantially similar to a product approved by the office, including but not
limited to products that resemble nonalcoholic beverages, candy, and baked
goods.
PUBLIC PLACE: A public park or trail, public street or sidewalk, any enclosed,
indoor area used by the general public, including, but not limited to,
theaters, restaurants, bars, food establishments, places licensed to sell
intoxicating liquor, wine, or malt beverages, retail businesses, gyms, common
areas in buildings, public shopping areas, auditoriums, arenas, or other places
of public accommodation.
PLACE OF PUBLIC ACCOMMODATION: A business, refreshment, entertainment,
recreation, or transportation facility of any kind, whose goods, services,
facilities, privileges, advantages, or accommodations are extended, offered,
sold, or otherwise made available to the public.Exceptions to the definition of
public place or place of public accommodation: "A public place" or "a place of
public accommodation" does not include the following:
   (1)   A private residence, including the individual's curtilage or yard.
   (2)   A private property, not generally accessible by the public, unless the
individual is explicitly prohibited from consuming cannabis flower, cannabis
products, lower-potency hemp edibles, or hemp-derived consumer products on the
property by the owner of the property; or
   (3)   On the premises of an establishment or event licensed to permit on-
site consumption.
SMOKING: Inhaling, exhaling, burning, or carrying any lighted or heated cigar,
cigarette, pipe, or any other lighted or heated product containing cannabis
flower, cannabis products, artificially derived cannabinoids, or hemp-derived
consumer products. Smoking includes carrying or using an activated electronic
delivery device for human consumption through inhalation of aerosol or vapor
from the product. (Ord. 324, 10-3-2023)
5-6-3: PROHIBITED ACTS:
   A.   No person shall use cannabis flower, cannabis products, lower-potency
hemp edibles, or hemp-derived consumer products in a public place or a place of
public accommodation unless the premises is an establishment or event licensed
to permit on-site consumption of adult-use cannabis flower and adult use
cannabis products. See Minnesota Session Law 2023, Chpt. 63, Art. I, Sec. 9
codified as Minn. Stat. 342.09, subd. 1(2) and 342.09, subd. 1 (7)(iii) and
Art. 4, Sec. 19 codified as Minn. Stat. Sec. 152.0263, subd. 5.
   B.   No person shall vaporize or smoke cannabis flower, cannabis products,
artificially derived cannabinoids, or hemp-derived consumer products in any
location where the smoke, aerosol, or vapor would be inhaled by a minor.
Minnesota Session Law 2023, Ch pt. 63, Art. 1, Sec. 9 codified as Minn. Stat.
Sec. 342.09, subd. 1 (7)(b)(9). (Ord. 324, 10-3-2023)
5-6-4: PENALTY:
   A.   Criminal Penalty: A violation of this chapter shall be a petty
misdemeanor punishable by a fine of up to three hundred dollars ($300.00), as
set by City Council. Nothing in this chapter shall prohibit the United States,
the State of Minnesota, or the City from investigating or prosecuting any other
activity that is a crime under any other federal or state statute or City
ordinance.
   B.   An alleged violation or violation of this chapter may be investigated
by a peace officer as defined in Minn. Stat. 626.84, Subd. 1. (Ord. 324, 10-3-
2023)
5-6-5: SEVERABILITY:
If any section or provision of this chapter is held invalid, such invalidity
will not affect any other section or provision that can be given force and
effect without the invalidated section or provision. (Ord. 324, 10-3-2023)
TITLE 6
MOTOR VEHICLES AND TRAFFIC
CHAPTER 1
ADMINISTRATION AND ENFORCEMENT 1
SECTION:
6-1-1: Power To Adopt; Compliance Required
6-1-2: Power Of Chief Of Police
6-1-3: Enforcement
6-1-4: Emergency Vehicles
6-1-5: Prima Facie Violation
6-1-6: Penalty
 
Notes
1 1. MSA § 412.211, subd. 6.
6-1-1: POWER TO ADOPT; COMPLIANCE REQUIRED:
The city council may, within the limits allowed by law, adopt additional
regulations over vehicles and traffic not in conflict with the provisions of
this code. No person shall fail to obey any sign, making, barricade or traffic
device erected pursuant to law. (1982 Code § 5.112; amd. 2005 Code)
6-1-2: POWER OF CHIEF OF POLICE:
   A.   Power To Regulate: To assist in the direction and control of traffic,
for orderly and safe use of city streets and other public ways for vehicular or
pedestrian travel, for the protection of city streets and other public ways and
for the convenience of the street department in maintaining the city streets
and other public ways, the chief of police may establish lanes of traffic,
establish stop or yield intersections, establish parking stalls and establish
other traffic regulations, to the extent that such regulations are not in
conflict with law, this code or provisions of the city council adopted pursuant
to this code. (1982 Code § 5.113; amd. 2005 Code)
   B.   Traffic Control Devices: To this end, the chief of police may cause the
installation of suitable signs, traffic control signals, markings, barricades
and other devices.
   C.   Compliance Required: No person shall fail to obey any sign, marking,
barricade or traffic device erected pursuant to such authority. (1982 Code §
5.113)
6-1-3: ENFORCEMENT:
   A.   Police Department: The police department shall enforce the provisions
of this title, police officers are authorized to direct all traffic within the
city, either in person or by means of visible or audible signal, in conformity
with this title and state traffic laws.
   B.   Emergency: During a fire or other emergency or to expedite traffic or
safeguard pedestrians, police officers may direct traffic as conditions
require, notwithstanding the provisions of this title and state traffic laws.
   C.   Fire Department: Officers of the fire department may direct traffic or
assist the police in directing traffic at the scene of a fire or in the
immediate vicinity of a fire. (1982 Code § 5.114)
6-1-4: EMERGENCY VEHICLES:
The provisions of this title shall not apply to the driver of an authorized
emergency vehicle, when responding to an emergency call or when at the scene of
a reported emergency. However, the driver shall operate and park the emergency
vehicle with due regard for the safety of others and in accordance with state
laws applicable to authorized emergency vehicles. (1982 Code § 5.115)
6-1-5: PRIMA FACIE VIOLATION:
The presence of a vehicle in or upon any public street, alley or highway, or
any other place in the city stopped, standing or parked in violation of any
part of this title regulating or prohibiting parking or traffic shall be prima
facie evidence that the person in whose name the vehicle is registered as owner
committed or authorized the commission of the violation. (1982 Code § 5.116)
6-1-6: PENALTY:
Any person violating any provision of this title shall be guilty of a petty
misdemeanor, except when another penalty is expressly provided in the
provision. (1982 Code § 5.111)
CHAPTER 2
GENERAL TRAFFIC PROVISIONS
SECTION:
6-2-1: Exhibition Driving
6-2-2: U-Turns
6-2-3: Inattentive Driving
6-2-4: Vehicle Noise
6-2-1: EXHIBITION DRIVING:
No person shall start, turn, accelerate, decelerate or otherwise operate a
motor vehicle on any public or private way or property within the city in any
manner which causes unnecessary engine noise or backfire, squealing of tires,
skidding, sliding, swaying, throwing of sand or gravel, or in a manner
simulating a race. Squealing or screeching sounds emitted by the tires or the
throwing of sand or gravel by the tires is prima facie evidence of a violation
of this section. (1982 Code § 5.211)
6-2-2: U-TURNS:
No person shall turn a vehicle so as to proceed in the opposite direction on
Oak Street, nor at any intersection designated by the city council and at which
a "No U-Turn" sign has been erected. (1982 Code § 5.212; amd. 2005 Code)
6-2-3: INATTENTIVE DRIVING:
No person shall operate or halt any motor vehicle upon any public or private
property within the city inattentively or imprudently in light of circumstances
then existing, or without reasonable care for the rights of others or the
safety of persons or property. Any person who violates this section shall be
guilty of the offense of inattentive driving. Inattentive driving shall be a
lesser offense than the offense of careless driving under state law. (1982 Code
§ 5.213)
6-2-4: VEHICLE NOISE:
   A.   Definitions: For the purposes of this section, the following phrases
are defined as follows:
    ABNORMAL OR EXCESSIVE NOISE: 1. Distinct and loudly audible noise that
unreasonably annoys, disturbs, injures, or endangers the comfort and repose of
any person or precludes their enjoyment of property or affects their property's
value,
      2.   Noise in excess of that permitted by Minnesota statutes section
169.69, as it may be amended from time to time, which requires every motor
vehicle to be equipped with a muffler in good working order, or
      3.   Noise in excess of that permitted by Minnesota statutes section
169.693 and Minnesota rules parts 7030.1000 through 7030.1050, as this statute
and these rules may be amended from time to time, which establish motor vehicle
noise standards.
   ENGINE RETARDING BRAKE: A dynamic brake, jake brake, jacobs brake, C-brake,
Paccar brake, transmission brake or other similar engine retarding brake system
which alters the normal compression of the engine and subsequently releases
that compression.
   B.   Prohibitions:
      1.   It shall be unlawful for any person to discharge the exhaust or
permit the discharge of the exhaust from any motor vehicle except through a
muffler that effectively prevents abnormal or excessive noise and complies with
all applicable state laws and regulations.
