      2.   It shall be unlawful for the operator of any truck to intentionally
use an engine retarding brake on any public highway, street, parking lot or
alley within the city which causes abnormal or excessive noise from the engine
because of an illegally modified or defective exhaust system, except in an
emergency.
   C.   Statutes Adopted: Minnesota statutes sections 169.69 and 169.693 (motor
vehicle noise limits) and Minnesota rules parts 7030.1000 through 7030.1050, as
these statutes and rules may be amended from time to time, are hereby adopted
by reference.
   D.   Signs: Signs stating "Vehicle Noise Laws Enforced" may be installed at
locations deemed appropriate by the city council to advise motorists of the
prohibitions contained in this section, except that no sign stating "Vehicle
Noise Laws Enforced" shall be installed on a state highway without a permit
from the Minnesota department of transportation. The provisions of this section
are in full force and effect even if no signs are installed.
   E.   Penalty: Any person, firm or corporation who violates any provision of
this section shall, upon conviction, be guilty of a petty misdemeanor and
punished by a fine of not more than three hundred dollars ($300.00). (Ord. 299,
3-20-2012)
CHAPTER 3
PARKING REGULATIONS
SECTION:
6-3-1: General Parking Restrictions
6-3-2: Angle Parking
6-3-3: Time Limitations
6-3-4: Trucks And Other Vehicles
6-3-5: Unauthorized Parking
6-3-6: Disabled Vehicles
6-3-7: Abandoned Vehicles
6-3-8: Impoundment
6-3-9: Citations
6-3-1: GENERAL PARKING RESTRICTIONS 1 :
No person shall stop, stand or park a vehicle, except when necessary to avoid
conflict with other traffic or in compliance with the directions of a police
officer or traffic control device in any of the following places:
   A.   In violation of the provisions of any law regulating the stopping,
standing or parking of vehicles.
   B.   When directed or ordered to proceed by any police officer, member of
the fire department or other authorized person.
   C.   Upon the paved, improved or traveled part of any public way when it is
practical to park the vehicle off such part of the public way.
   D.   Upon any public way so as to constitute a hazard to public safety or to
interfere with the free passage of other vehicles.
   E.   Upon any sidewalk or crosswalk.
   F.   In front of any public or private driveway or so close to it as to
prevent vehicles from entering or exiting the driveway.
   G.   Within an intersection.
   H.   Within ten feet (10') of a fire hydrant.
   I.   Within thirty feet (30') of any flashing beacon, traffic control
signal, stop sign, yield sign, or sign indicating the direction of travel.
   J.   Within twenty feet (20') of the driveway entrance to any fire station
and, if so posted by proper authority, on the side of a street opposite the
entrance to any fire station within seventy five feet (75') of the entrance.
   K.   On the roadway side of any vehicle stopped or parked at the edge or
curb of any public way.
   L.   Upon any bridge or other elevated structure or within a highway tunnel,
or upon the approach to any such structures.
   M.   Upon any boulevard.
   N.   Upon any public way to display any vehicle for sale or exchange. A
vehicle shall be deemed so displayed when bearing a sign indicating that it is
for sale or exchange.
   O.   Upon any public way for purposes of washing, cleaning or repairing a
vehicle, other than making emergency repairs necessary before removal of the
vehicle from the public way.
   P.   In such a manner that a vehicle is parked straddling two (2) or more
parking spaces when parking spaces have been duly marked.
   Q.   Contrary to any duly erected signs or contrary to any duly placed stall
marks, box marks, or other legend or device restricting parking.
   R.   In any duly designated and posted no parking zone. (1982 Code § 5.222)
 
Notes
1 1. MSA § 169.34.
6-3-2: ANGLE PARKING:
   A.   All vehicles parked within the city shall be parked according the
markings or signs, as may directed by city officials, or otherwise in
accordance with law. (Ord. 233, 9-1-1998; amd. Ord. 233, 5-16-2023)
6-3-3: TIME LIMITATIONS:
   A.   Specific Limits: No vehicle shall be parked in the following areas for
a continuous period exceeding the time specified:
   Sixth Street between Walnut Street and Oak Street   3 hours
   All other streets   24 hours
   B.   Restricted Parking: No person shall leave a vehicle standing on any
portion of Sixth Street between Walnut Street and Spruce Street between two
o'clock (2:00) A.M. and five o'clock (5:00) A.M. (1982 Code § 5.225)
6-3-4: TRUCKS AND OTHER VEHICLES:
   A.   Vehicles Exceeding Eighteen Feet: No truck, bus or other vehicle
exceeding eighteen feet (18') in length shall park on Sixth Street between Oak
Street and Hickory Street except for such time as is reasonably necessary in
taking on or discharging loads or passengers.
   B.   Two Hour Limit: In no event shall any such truck, bus or other vehicle,
nor shall any heavy or loaded industrial, commercial or farming vehicle or
equipment be parked or left standing, whether attended or unattended, upon the
paved, improved or main traveled portion of any street, alley or other public
way in the city for a continuous period of time exceeding two (2) hours, or for
such longer time as is actually necessary in loading or unloading such vehicle.
(1982 Code § 5.226)
6-3-5: UNAUTHORIZED PARKING:
   A.   Private Property: No person shall park or stand any vehicle upon the
private property of any other person without the consent of the owner,
occupant, lessee or other person in charge of the property.
   B.   Public Property: No person shall park or stand any vehicle upon any
public park or other public property, except along any roadway where parking is
permitted or in an area set aside for parking of vehicles. (1982 Code § 5.227)
6-3-6: DISABLED VEHICLES:
   A.   Parking Specifications: The driver of any vehicle which becomes
disabled while traveling on any street or alley such that it is impossible to
avoid stopping and temporarily leaving the vehicle on the street or alley shall
move the vehicle as close to the curb or edge of the roadway as may be done.
   B.   Report To Police: If the vehicle cannot be immediately moved or towed
away, the driver shall immediately report the disability to the police
department.
   C.   Time Limitation: No owner or driver of a vehicle which is disabled
shall allow it to remain upon the traveled portion of any street or alley, or
allow a disabled vehicle to be parked along any street or alley even though
parking of it would otherwise be lawful, for any longer than reasonably
necessary to cause the vehicle to be moved or towed away. (1982 Code § 5.223)
6-3-7: ABANDONED VEHICLES:
No driver or owner shall abandon any vehicle upon any street, alley or public
property within the city. The leaving of any vehicle not reasonably capable of
being driven for transportation, or which cannot be driven without being
repaired, upon any street, alley or public property for more than five (5) days
is prima facie evidence of a violation of this section. (1982 Code § 5.224)
6-3-8: IMPOUNDMENT:
   A.   Authority To Remove: Any police officer may remove an unattended
vehicle from a street, alley or other public property to a garage or other
place of safety when the vehicle constitutes an obstruction to traffic,
endangers others, or is parked in violation of law or this code and thereby
hinders snow removal or street improvement or maintenance operations.
   B.   Redemption: The vehicle shall not be released until the fees for towing
and storage are paid.
   C.   Citation: The officer may also issue a ticket for time violation. (1982
Code § 5.281)
6-3-9: CITATIONS:
   A.   Parking Citation: A parking citation shall be issued to the owner or
operator of any vehicle in violation of any of the provisions of this chapter.
The citation shall indicate the nature of the violation, the amount of the
fine, the method by which the fine shall be paid, and the procedure by which
the person receiving the citation may obtain a hearing to contest the issuance
of the citation. (1982 Code § 5.291)
   B.   Administration: The city clerk, or a designated agent of the city
clerk, shall receive, process and make records of all parking citations issued
and fines paid. The city clerk shall submit summarized monthly reports to the
city council of all fines collected and the nature of the violations. All
monies obtained from the fines shall be deposited with the city treasurer and
shall be a part of the general fund. (1982 Code § 5.292)
   C.   Hearing:
      1.   Request For Hearing: Any person who desires to contest a parking
citation shall, within seven (7) days of its issuance, submit to the city clerk
a written request for a formal hearing.
      2.   Schedule Of Hearing; Notice: The request shall be forwarded to the
proper court, at which time a court hearing shall be scheduled and notification
of it sent to the alleged violator.
      3.   Court Costs: If the court determines that the alleged violator was
in violation of a provision of this chapter, the court may assess the violator
reasonable court costs in addition to any penalty imposed. (1982 Code § 5.293)
   D.   Nonpayment Of Fine: Any violator who fails to pay the fine indicated or
submit a written request for hearing within seven (7) days from the date of
issuance of the citation shall be guilty of a petty misdemeanor, except that
when preceded by two (2) or more violations within the preceding twelve (12)
months, a violation shall constitute a misdemeanor. (1982 Code § 5.294)
CHAPTER 4
RECREATIONAL VEHICLES
SECTION:
6-4-1: Definition
6-4-2: Entry On Private Property
6-4-3: Operation On Sidewalks
6-4-4: Parental Responsibility
6-4-5: Owner Responsibility
6-4-1: DEFINITION:
"Recreational motor vehicle" means any self-propelled vehicle and any vehicle
propelled or drawn by a self-propelled vehicle used for recreational purposes,
including, but not limited to, a snowmobile, trail bike or other all terrain
vehicle, hovercraft or motor vehicle licensed for highway operation which is
being used for off road recreational purposes. (1982 Code § 5.311)
6-4-2: ENTRY ON PRIVATE PROPERTY:
No person shall enter on any private property within the city for the purpose
of operating a recreational motor vehicle without the consent of the owner,
occupant, lessee or other person in charge of the property to do so. (1982 Code
§ 5.312)
6-4-3: OPERATION ON SIDEWALKS:
No person shall operate a recreational motor vehicle upon a public sidewalk nor
upon any trail or other public way set aside for the exclusive use of
pedestrians. (1982 Code § 5.313)
6-4-4: PARENTAL RESPONSIBILITY:
No parent of any minor child, nor the guardian of any ward, shall authorize or
knowingly permit the child or ward to violate any provision of this code
relating to the operation of a snowmobile or other recreational motor vehicle.
(1982 Code § 5.314)
6-4-5: OWNER RESPONSIBILITY:
No owner of a snowmobile or any other recreational motor vehicle shall permit
the vehicle to be operated contrary to the provisions of this code, or of any
law or regulation regarding snowmobiles or other recreational motor vehicles.
(1982 Code § 5.315)
ARTICLE A. SNOWMOBILES 1
SECTION:
6-4A-1: Operation Restricted
6-4A-2: Emergency Travel
6-4A-3: Snowmobile Recreation Areas
6-4A-4: Speed Limits
6-4A-5: Careless Operation
6-4A-6: Unreasonable Operation
6-4A-7: Hours
6-4A-8: Age Restriction; Certification Requirement
 
Notes
1 1. MSA § 84.81 et seq.
6-4A-1: OPERATION RESTRICTED:
No person shall operate any snowmobile on any public street, alley or other
roadway, or on any river or other public place, in the city, except for the
purpose of travel between the place of storage of the snowmobile and a place
outside of the city or a snowmobile recreation area, or for the purpose of
traveling between recreation areas, by means of a direct, reasonably convenient
route, or except in such areas or places as may be designated as snowmobile
recreation areas. (1982 Code § 5.321)
6-4A-2: EMERGENCY TRAVEL:
A snowmobile may be operated on a public street, alley, river or other public
place within the city during any time that snow upon the roadways of the city
renders travel by automobile impractical. Snowmobiles may be operated by police
officers and firefighters in the performance of their official duties and by
physicians and veterinarians making professional calls when other means of
transportation are impractical or less efficient. (1982 Code § 5.322)
6-4A-3: SNOWMOBILE RECREATION AREAS:
   A.   Designation: The following areas within the city are hereby designated
as snowmobile recreation areas:
Lac Qui Parle River at and including its intersection with Sixth Street and
downstream from there.
Lac Qui Parle River at and including its intersection with Eleventh Street and
upstream from there. (1982 Code § 5.323)
   B.   Additional Areas: The city council may designate additional areas as
snowmobile recreation areas. (1982 Code § 5.323; amd. 2005 Code)
6-4A-4: SPEED LIMITS:
No person shall operate any snowmobile within the following designated places
within the city at speeds greater than that indicated:
   A.   Five (5) miles per hour, while traversing any ice rink in travel
between snowmobile recreation areas;
   B.   Fifteen (15) miles per hour in a snowmobile recreation area;
   C.   Ten (10) miles per hour, in any other place within the city. (1982 Code
§ 5.324)
6-4A-5: CARELESS OPERATION:
No person shall operate any snowmobile within the city carelessly or heedlessly
in disregard of the rights or the safety of others. In no event shall any
person operate a snowmobile in a manner so as to endanger or harass others or
any animal or so as to interfere with skaters on any ice rink. (1982 Code §
5.325)
6-4A-6: UNREASONABLE OPERATION:
No person shall start, turn, accelerate, decelerate or otherwise operate a
snowmobile within the city in a manner that causes unnecessary engine noise or
backfire, skidding, sliding, swaying, throwing of snow or dirt or in a manner
simulating a race. (1982 Code § 5.326)
6-4A-7: HOURS:
Except when using a snowmobile in accordance with the provisions of section
6-4A-2 of this article, or except when returning to the place of storage of a
snowmobile by the most direct route from recreational use outside the city, no
person shall operate any snowmobile within the city before twelve o'clock (12:
00) noon on Sunday or before eight o'clock (8:00) A.M. on any other day, nor
after ten o'clock (10:00) P.M. on any day. (1982 Code § 5.327)
6-4A-8: AGE RESTRICTION; CERTIFICATION REQUIREMENT:
No person under fourteen (14) years of age shall operate a snowmobile on any
street, alley, river or other public way or public property within the city. A
person at least fourteen (14) years of age but less than eighteen (18) years of
age may operate a snowmobile within the city only while having actual
possession of a valid Minnesota snowmobile safety certificate while operating
the snowmobile. (1982 Code § 5.328)
ARTICLE B. BICYCLES 1
SECTION:
6-4B-1: Definition
6-4B-2: Traffic Regulations
6-4B-3: Operation Restricted
6-4B-4: Parking
6-4B-5: Motorized Bicycles
6-4B-6: Prohibited Acts
6-4B-7: Parental Responsibility
 
Notes
1 1. MSA § 169.222.
6-4B-1: DEFINITION:
"Bicycle" means every device propelled solely by human power upon which a
person may ride, having two (2) tandem wheels either of which is over fourteen
inches (14") in diameter, or any device generally recognized as a bicycle
though equipped with two (2) front or two (2) rear wheels, or a unicycle, but
excluding scooters and similar devices. (1982 Code § 5.411)
6-4B-2: TRAFFIC REGULATIONS:
Every person operating a bicycle shall have all the rights and duties
applicable by law or this title to the driver of any other vehicle, except in
respect to those provisions relating expressly to bicycles and in respect to
those provisions which by their nature cannot reasonably be applied to
bicycles. (1982 Code § 5.421)
6-4B-3: OPERATION RESTRICTED:
No person shall operate a bicycle upon a sidewalk on Sixth Street between
Lincoln and Spruce Street. In any other area of the city, a person may operate
a bicycle upon a sidewalk or within a crosswalk, but only in compliance with
law and only with due regard for the safety of pedestrians upon the sidewalk or
within the crosswalk. (1982 Code § 6.422)
6-4B-4: PARKING:
No person may park a bicycle on a sidewalk so as to interfere with access to or
from any building or so as to block the sidewalk or otherwise impede the normal
reasonable movement of pedestrian or other traffic, nor shall any person park a
bicycle on a roadway in a manner that obstructs the movement of any legally
parked motor vehicle. (1982 Code § 5.423)
6-4B-5: MOTORIZED BICYCLES:
Except as otherwise provided by law or by this title, and except as such are
inapplicable, the provisions of this article relating to the operation of
bicycles within the city are applicable to the operation of motorize bicycles
within the city. No person shall operate a motorized bicycle on any bicycleway
or bicycle lane. No person shall operate a motorized bicycle upon a sidewalk at
any time, except when necessary for the most direct access to the roadway from
a driveway, alley or building. (1982 Code § 5.511)
6-4B-6: PROHIBITED ACTS:
Any person who violates the following provisions shall be guilty of a
misdemeanor:
   A.   Unauthorized Use And Sale: No person shall take, use, sell or offer for
sale another's bicycle without the consent of the owner. (1982 Code § 5.412)
   B.   Tampering: No person not the owner of the bicycle shall remove any
license plate, serial number or other identification from the bicycle, nor
shall any person tamper with any bicycle which has been locked or placed in a
rack or otherwise secured. (1982 Code § 5.413)
6-4B-7: PARENTAL RESPONSIBILITY:
No parent of any minor child, nor the guardian of any ward, shall authorize or
knowingly permit the child or ward to violate any provision of this article
regarding bicycles. (1982 Code § 5.414)
ARTICLE C. SKATEBOARDS AND ROLLERBLADES, SKATES AND SKIS
SECTION:
6-4C-1: Purpose
6-4C-2: Interpretation
6-4C-3: Definitions
6-4C-4: Restricted Areas
6-4C-5: Rules Of The Road
6-4C-6: Future Prohibited Areas
6-4C-7: Penalty
6-4C-1: PURPOSE:
The purpose of this article is to protect the public health and safety arising
out of the use of skateboards, rollerblades, roller skates and roller skis
within the city. The city council finds that there are certain public streets,
sidewalks and public property wherein the operation and use of skateboards,
rollerblades, roller skates and roller skis create an unnecessary potential
danger to either the use of such devices or the general public and that the use
of such devices in an improper manner may cause destruction of property. (Ord.
222, 9-5-1995)
6-4C-2: INTERPRETATION:
Nothing in this article shall be construed to prohibit the use of a wheelchair
or any other wheeled device designed to assist a disabled person on any of the
places mentioned in this article. (Ord. 222, 9-5-1995)
6-4C-3: DEFINITIONS:
"Roller device" shall mean any one of the following devices:
ROLLER SKATES AND ROLLERBLADES: A shoe with wheels attached or a device with
wheels which is designed to be attached to a shoe.
ROLLER SKIS: A pair of skis platformed with wheels attached which is intended
to simulate skiing.
SKATEBOARD: A wheeled self-propelled and manually propelled device to transport
a rider which device is not otherwise secured to the rider's feet or shoes.
(Ord. 222, 9-5-1995)
6-4C-4: RESTRICTED AREAS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to ride or propel himself upon a "roller
device" as defined herein in or on the following areas in the city:
   A.   Downtown Business Area: On any public street, alley, sidewalk or other
public property within the following area, same being the downtown business
area: Sixth Street and its adjoining sidewalks between Walnut Street and Spruce
Street in the city, between the hours of seven o'clock (7:00) A.M. and six
o'clock (6:00) P.M., Monday through Saturday.
   B.   Public Building/Area: In any public building/area owned by the city,
the same being the library, city building and on any tennis and basketball
courts at the city parks.
   C.   While Being Propelled: In any area within the city while being pushed,
pulled or in any way propelled by any motorized vehicle or by a person on a
bicycle. (Ord. 222, 9-5-1995)
6-4C-5: RULES OF THE ROAD:
Any person who is using any roller device on any of the streets or roadways
within the city which are not specified above as prohibited must observe the
same rules of the road as required of bicycles pursuant to Minnesota Statutes
Annotated section 169.222. (Ord. 222, 9-5-1995)
6-4C-6: FUTURE PROHIBITED AREAS:
In the future, the city council may prohibit the use of "roller devices"
defined in section
6-4C-3 of this article in areas of the city in addition to those prohibited in
section
6-4C-4 of this article upon recommendation of the chief of police or the parks
and recreation director. (Ord. 222, 9-5-1995; amd. 2005 Code)
6-4C-7: PENALTY:
   A.   First Offense: The skateboard, roller skates or rollerblades will be
confiscated immediately for a period of five (5) days. After the five (5) day
period, the skateboard, rollerblades or roller skates shall be picked up by a
parent or guardian.
   B.   Second Offense: The skateboard, roller skates or rollerblades will be
confiscated immediately for a period of ten (10) days. At the end of the ten
(10) day period, the skateboard, rollerblades or roller skates shall be picked
up by a parent or guardian.
   C.   Third Offense: The skateboard, roller skates or rollerblades will be
confiscated immediately and the party shall be charged with a petty
misdemeanor, as provided in the general penalty in subsection 1-4-1A of this
code. (Ord. 222, 9-5-1995; amd. 2005 Code)
ARTICLE D. MOTORIZED RECREATIONAL VEHICLES
SECTION:
6-4D-1: Purpose; Intent; Definitions
6-4D-2: Use Of Recreational Vehicles
6-4D-3: Penalty
6-4D-1: PURPOSE; INTENT; DEFINITIONS:
   A.   1.   The purpose of this chapter is to provide reasonable regulations
for the use of recreational motor vehicles on public property in the city.
      2.   This chapter is not intended to allow what the Minnesota Statutes
prohibit or to prohibit what the Minnesota Statutes expressly allow.
   B.   It is intended to ensure the public safety and prevent a public
nuisance.
   C.   For purposes of this Ordinance, a recreational vehicle is defined as
follows:
 
                      Any motorized flotation-tired vehicles with at least
ALL-TERRAIN VEHICLE:  three but no more than six low pressure tires that have
                      an engine displacement of less than 960 cubic centimeters
                      and total dry weight of less than 1,000 pounds.
                      Any passenger conveyance being driven with three or four
MOTORIZED GOLF CART:  wheels with three or four low-pressure tires that is
                      limited in engine displacement of less than 800 cubic
                      centimeters and total dry weight less than 800 pounds.
                      A side-by-side, four-wheel drive, off-road vehicle that
                      has four wheels, is propelled by an internal combustion
UTILITY TASK VEHICLE: engine with a piston displacement capacity of 1,200 cubic
                      centimeters or less, and has a total dry weight of 1,800
                      but less than 2,600 pounds. (Ord. 309, 9-16-2014; amd.
                      Ord. 309, 6-3-2025)
 
6-4D-2: USE OF RECREATIONAL VEHICLES:
   A.   1.   No person shall operate a recreational vehicle on streets, alleys,
sidewalks or other public property without obtaining a permit as provided
herein.
      2.   Every application for a permit shall be made on a form supplied by
the city and shall contain all of the following information:
         a.   The name and address of the applicant; Add names of all household
members who will be driving the recreational vehicle.
         b.   Model name, make, color, and year and number of the recreational
vehicle;
         c.   Current driver’s license and copy of all driver’s licenses for
those who share the same household that will be operating the vehicle; and
         d.   Other information as the city may require.
      3.   The permit fee shall be paid on an annual basis at the rate
established by The City Council, in accordance with Minn. Stat § 169.045. The
City Council shall have the authority to adjust the fee by resolution from time
to time.
      4.   No permit shall be granted or renewed unless the following
conditions are met:
         a.   The applicant must demonstrate that he or she currently holds a
valid Minnesota driver’s license; or
         b.   The applicant may submit a certificate signed by a physician that
the applicant is able to safely operate a recreational vehicle on the roadways
designated. If a valid driver’s license is not obtainable, this certificate
will be required annually.
         c.   The applicant must provide evidence of insurance in compliance
with the provisions of Minnesota Statutes concerning insurance coverage for the
recreational vehicle. A copy of insurance must be submitted with each
application.
         d.   The applicant has not had his or her driver’s license revoked as
the result of criminal proceedings.
      5.   Recreational vehicles are permitted to operate only on city streets,
not state or federal highways, from sunrise to sunset. Recreational vehicles
shall not be operated on county roads. They shall not be operated in inclement
weather, except during emergency conditions as provided in the ordinance, or
when visibility is impaired by weather, smoke, fog, or other conditions, or at
any time when there is insufficient light visibility to clearly see persons and
vehicles on the roadway at a distance of 500 feet.
      6.   All recreational vehicles must be equipped with functioning
headlights and taillights and all golf carts shall display the slow-moving
vehicle emblem per Minn. Stat. § 169.045 and shall be equipped with a rear-view
mirror to provide the driver with adequate vision from behind as required by
Minn. Stat. § 169.70
      7.   Every person operating a recreational vehicle under permit on
designated roadways has all the rights and duties applicable to the driver of
any other vehicle under the provisions of Minn. Stat., ch. 169, as it may be
amended from time to time, except when these provisions cannot reasonably be
applied to recreational vehicles and except as otherwise specifically provided
in Minn. Stat. § 169.045(7), as it may be amended from time to time.
      8.   The Police Chief and officers may suspend or revoke a permit granted
hereunder upon a finding that the holder thereof has violated any of the
provisions of this section or Minn. Stat. ch. 169, as it may be amended from
time to time, investigation of report of incident, or if there is evidence that
the permit holder cannot safely operate the recreational vehicle on the
designated roadways. Repercussions may include verbal/ written warning,
ordinance violation, State Administrative Ticket, or revocation.
      9.   Recreational vehicles may not operate with a greater number of
passengers than the vehicle is designed to carry, and all passengers must be in
the seated position while the vehicle is moving. Children must be properly
secured in vehicle as would be required by Minn. Statutes. All lap riding is
prohibited.
   B.   Authorized city staff may operate city owned recreational vehicles
without obtaining a permit within the city, on city streets, sidewalks, trails,
rights-of-way, and public property when conducting city business. (Ord. 309, 9-
16-2014; amd. Ord. 309, 8-1-2023; Ord.309, 6-3-2025)
6-4D-3: PENALTY:
Any person convicted of violating any provision of this article is guilty of a
misdemeanor and may be subject to a fine as established by the city council.
(Ord. 309, 9-16-2014)
TITLE 7
PUBLIC WAYS AND PROPERTY
CHAPTER 1
STREETS, SIDEWALKS AND PUBLIC WAYS 1
SECTION:
7-1-1: Permit Requirements
7-1-2: Obstructions

7-1-5: Parking

7-1-11: Weight Restrictions, Truck Routes, Truck Parking And Truck Traffic

1 1. MSA § 412.221, subd. 6.
7-1-1: PERMIT REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Permit Required:
      1.   Application: Any person desiring to use public property shall apply
for a permit or renewal of a permit a minimum of two (2) working days before
starting work and must submit detailed plans for street or sidewalk use and
pedestrian safety on major projects.
      2.   Waiver: This provision or portions thereof may be waived by the
director of public works in the event of an emergency.
   B.   Insurance:
      1.   Insurance Required: The permittee shall obtain liability insurance
for both personal injury and property damage in an amount not less than one
million dollars ($1,000,000.00).
      2.   Additional Insured: The city shall be named as an additional insured
under that insurance for the services provided under the permit. The
permittee's insurance will be the primary insurance for the city.
      3.   Certificate Of Insurance: Permittee shall provide a certificate of
insurance on the city's approved form which verifies the existence of the
required liability insurance coverage as well as workers' compensation
coverage.
   C.   Display Of Permit: Permits issued under this section by the department
of public works shall be conspicuously displayed at all times for ease of
inspection on the indicated work site.
   D.   Double Fee: Should any person begin work of any kind without having
first secured the necessary permit therefor, such person shall be required to
pay double the fee provided for such permit.
   E.   Revocation: Any permit issued by the director of public works under
this section may be revoked when he finds revocation in the best interests of
the city. (Ord. 225, 9-5-1995)
7-1-2: OBSTRUCTIONS:
   A.   Barricades; Guards: Any permittee obstructing any street, alley,
sidewalk or other public property shall keep such obstruction properly guarded
at all times;
   B.   Warning Lights: From sunset to sunrise, all obstructions must be
guarded by a sufficient number of warning lights placed in such manner that
they will give proper warning of said obstruction.
   C.   Fencing: The director of public works may require any permittee
obstructing a sidewalk to build adjacent to such obstruction a tight board
fence at least six feet (6') high, except at street intersections where a six
foot (6') open board fence shall be built and maintained.
   D.   Walkway:
      1.   Required: Adjacent to each such fence shall be built and maintained
a temporary walk at least four feet (4') in width for the use of the public
with a railing along the outside edge of the walk at least thirty six inches
(36") high.
      2.   Waiver: The director of public works may waive the requirement for a
temporary walk when it is determined that a temporary walk is not necessary and
that pedestrians can more properly be protected by rerouting them to a walk
across the street. (Ord. 225, 9-5-1995)
7-1-3: FLAGGERS:
The director of public works may direct that flaggers, as described in section
6F of the manual on uniform traffic control devices for streets and highways,
state of Minnesota, be used to control traffic. (Ord. 225, 9-5-1995)
7-1-4: TRAFFIC CLOSURE:
The permittee shall notify the director of public works when the permit area is
closed to pedestrian and vehicular traffic and again when it is open to such
traffic. (Ord. 225, 9-5-1995)
7-1-5: PARKING:
The parking of private vehicles within or adjacent to the permit area is
prohibited. The loading or unloading of trucks adjacent to the permit area is
prohibited unless specifically authorized by the permit. (Ord. 225, 9-5-1995)
7-1-6: DERRICKS AND HOISTS:
No person shall place or use derricks or hoists of any kind or any portion
thereof, including outriggers and pads, upon any sidewalk unless the permit
specifically permits such action. (Ord. 225, 9-5-1995)
7-1-7: ENCLOSED PEDESTRIAN WALKWAY REQUIRED:
Whenever any person applies for a permit for the use of a street or sidewalk or
portion thereof for the purpose of hoisting or lifting equipment or material
over, across and above such street or sidewalk, he shall provide for closing
off those portions of the street and/or sidewalk encompassed within the lifting
area with suitable barricades, signs, and warning lights and shall provide a
four foot (4') pedestrian walkway around such lifting area, such walkway to be
suitably enclosed on the street side with barricades and warning lights. (Ord.
225, 9-5-1995)
7-1-8: OVERHANGING DEVICES:
No person shall place or maintain any wire, cable, rope, arch, strut, or other
artificial device or structure, or any thing or device carried thereon or
suspended therefrom, over or across any street or alley at a height of less
than fourteen feet (14') above the traveled portion of the street or alley.
(1982 Code § 4.211)
7-1-9: SIDEWALKS:
   A.   Width: All cement sidewalks hereafter constructed on the following
streets shall be of at least the following indicated width:
 
Chestnut Street between Sixth           6 feet wide
and Ninth Streets
Pine Street between Sixth and
Seventh Streets
West half of block 51                   5 feet wide
East half of block 51                   8 feet wide
Sixth Street between the intersection
with the Minneapolis St. Louis Railroad 10 feet wide, including
right of way and the bridge on Sixth    curb
Street over the Lac Qui Parle River.
Seventh Street, east side, between      6 feet wide
Pine and Chestnut Streets
All other sidewalks                     5 feet wide
 
   (Ord. 229, 10-7-1997)
   B.   Cleaning And Repair:
      1.   By Owner/Occupant: The owner and the occupant or other person in
control of any property adjacent to a public sidewalk shall use diligence to
keep the walk in good repair, clear of all snow, ice, dirt and rubbish, and
otherwise safe for pedestrians. No such person shall allow snow, ice, dirt or
rubbish to remain on a sidewalk longer than twenty four (24) hours after its
deposit thereon or after the snow has ceased to fall. Owners and occupants or
other persons in control of residential property adjacent to a public sidewalk
shall use diligence to keep the walk in good repair, clear of all snow, ice,
dirt and rubbish and otherwise safe for pedestrians. (Ord. 258, 4-19-2005)
      2.   By City:
         a.   Notice To Clear Or Repair: Whenever any sidewalk has not been
cleared or repaired as required by subsection B1 of this section the Dawson
chief of police may give written notice to the owner, occupant or other person
in control of the property that the sidewalk must be cleared or repaired within
such time as the Dawson chief of police determines is necessary for protection
of the public health, safety and welfare.
         b.   Failure To Comply: No notice shall be required respecting the
clearing of snow, ice, dirt or rubbish which has remained on the walk beyond
the time specified in subsection B1 of this section. If the sidewalk is not
cleared or repaired within the time required, the Dawson chief of police may
have the sidewalk cleared or repaired.
         c.   Costs: The owner of the property shall be responsible for all
costs and expenses of clearing or repairing the sidewalk. The Dawson chief of
police shall keep a record showing the cost of the work adjacent to each
separate lot and parcel and shall deliver the information to the city clerk.
(Ord. 305, 6-4-2013)
         d.   Failure To Pay: If the owner fails to make payment or
satisfactory payment arrangements within ten (10) days of billing, the cost
shall be taxed against the property as provided by law. (1982 Code § 4.223)
   C.   Liability: The owner, the occupant and the lessee of any property
adjacent to a public sidewalk shall indemnify the city for any liability
including the cost of defending against any claim incurred by the city by
reason of improper maintenance of the sidewalk or by reason of failure to keep
the sidewalk clear of snow, ice, dirt and rubbish. (1982 Code § 4.224)
   D.   Removal Of Sidewalk: No existing sidewalk may be removed unless allowed
by permit granted by the Dawson city council. If a sidewalk is removed without
a permit, the landowner may be required to replace the sidewalk.
   E.   Emergency Permit For The Removal Of Sidewalk: The city maintenance
superintendent or his designee is authorized to issue an emergency permit to
remove a sidewalk or a portion thereof. The landowner must either replace the
sidewalk or obtain a permit under subsection D of this section to remove the
sidewalk permanently.
   F.   Permit Fee: A permit fee in the amount of fifteen dollars ($15.00) is
required for permit under subsections D and E of this section. (Ord. 305, 6-4-
2013)
7-1-10: STREET SNOW REMOVAL OPERATIONS:
   A.   Streets To Be Cleared:
      1.   Between the hours of ten o'clock (10:00) P.M. until seven o'clock
(7:00) A.M., any vehicle, trailer, camper, trailer home, dumpster or like
property parked on all city streets or any city parking lot after one inch (1")
or more of snowfall shall be removed until the street or city parking lot has
been completely plowed from curb to curb. Any establishment normally open for
business during the hours of ten o'clock (10:00) P.M. until seven o'clock (7:
00) A.M. shall be excluded from the requirements of this section until the
establishment's closing time.
      2.   Any vehicle, trailer, camper, trailer home, dumpster or like
property which shall be left parked or standing in violation of this section
may be summarily removed, without notice to the owner or operator, by officers
of the police department, or persons employed or designated by them, and stored
in any appropriate place. All necessary costs and expenses of towing, removing
and storage of such property shall be first paid to the person, or person
designated by the person, claiming the property before release of same.
      3.   The city shall not be responsible for any damage to such vehicle,
trailer, camper, trailer home, dumpster or like property removed in accordance
with the provisions of this section.
   B.   Violation; Penalty: It shall be unlawful for any person, firm or
corporation to cause, allow, suffer or permit any vehicle, trailer, camper,
trailer home, dumpster or like property operated by or registered in the name
of such person, firm or corporation to be parked contrary to the provisions of
this section. Any person, firm or corporation violating the provisions of this
section shall be guilty of a petty misdemeanor. (Ord. 256, 12-16-2004)
7-1-11: WEIGHT RESTRICTIONS, TRUCK ROUTES, TRUCK PARKING AND TRUCK TRAFFIC:
   A.   In accordance with the powers granted in Minnesota statutes chapters
169.87 and 169.34, the city of Dawson hereby restricts truck traffic to an
improved route within the city. This action is to prevent the continued
deterioration of streets not designed for such traffic, the potential safety
hazards, and the abatement of noise, odors, and other nuisances associated with
truck traffic in residential areas and other areas where such traffic may be in
conflict with the existing land use.
   B.   For the purpose of this section, the following terms will be defined as
follows:
    TRUCK: Any motor vehicle that weighs in excess of ten (10) tons (20,000
gross vehicle weight rating - GVWR) but does not include the following
vehicles:
      1.   Sanitation/garbage trucks.
      2.   Emergency vehicles.
      3.   Public maintenance vehicles.
      4.   Moving vans or vehicles at such times as the same is used to move an
individual, family, or business and their possessions to or from a residence or
business.
      5.   Delivery and construction vehicles that are in route to or from a
place of delivery of goods and services or the construction site (but such
delivery and construction vehicles must use truck routes when the same are
available).
      6.   Recreation vehicles, motor homes, camping trailers, travel trailers,
fifth wheel camping trailers.
      7.   Tree trimming service vehicles.
      8.   Buses.
   C.   No person, firm or corporation shall operate, drive, tow or park any
vehicle, or combination of vehicles, with a gross vehicle weight rating of over
twenty thousand (20,000) pounds on any city street which has not been
classified as a truck route.
   D.   All tractors and tractor trailer combinations are prohibited from
parking on any residential street except in designated truck routes. All
tractor trailer combinations must remain hooked together at all times when
parked. No vehicle or combinations shall remain parked for more than six (6)
hours. Seasonal parking restrictions will apply.
   E.   The chief of police or his designated person may authorize an
overweight vehicle to use a street or roadway other than a truck route in an
emergency situation.
   F.   The city streets or roadways designated as truck routes are:
Alley between 8th Street and 9th Street between Walnut and Locust
Chestnut Street between 5th Street and 7th Street
County State A #37 runs from 5th Street SE to city limits
Diagonal Street
Johnson Street between 5th Street and 7th Street
Lincoln Place between 6th Street and 8th Street
Lincoln Place from Highway 212 to 12th Street
Locust Street between 5th and 6th Street
Locust Street between 8th Street and Memorial Place
North Park Street and Northeast 1st Street
Pine Street between 5th Street and 7th Street
Spruce Street between 6th Street and 7th Street
Walnut Street between 7th Street and 9th Street
North 3rd Street
Southeast 3rd Street and East Linden Street
5th Street between Pine Street and Johnson Street
6th Street
North 6th Street East
North 6th Street West
7th Street between Spruce Street and Walnut Street
North 7th Street
12th Street between Highway 212 and Locust Street
   G.   Any person or entity violating any provisions of this section may
either be levied an administrative fee or issued a state citation at the
discretion of the officer. A violation shall be considered a misdemeanor with a
maximum penalty of one thousand dollars ($1,000.00) and/or ninety (90) days'
jail. (Ord. 317, 7-5-2016)
CHAPTER 2
EXCAVATIONS 1
SECTION:
7-2-1: Permit Required; Fee
7-2-2: Procedures; Applicable Requirements
7-2-3: Conditions Of Permit
7-2-4: Street Restoration Fee
7-2-5: Subsurface Installation
 
Notes
1 1. MSA § 412.221, subd. 6.
7-2-1: PERMIT REQUIRED; FEE:
No person shall make any excavation in any street, alley, sidewalk or on any
public property without first obtaining from the city clerk a permit to do so.
The fee for an excavation permit shall be the same as that required for a water
or sewer construction permit. No separate excavation permit shall be required
for excavation incidental to water or sewer construction for which a water or
sewer construction permit is required. (1982 Code § 4.131)
7-2-2: PROCEDURES; APPLICABLE REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   All procedures for obtaining and all conditions of water and sewer
construction permits, insofar as they can be made applicable, apply to
excavation permits, including all insurance requirements.
   B.   A public utility corporation shall not be required to carry insurance.
(1982 Code § 4.132)
7-2-3: CONDITIONS OF PERMIT:
The following conditions shall be deemed to be incorporated in each permit
granted whenever any excavation is made in or along any public street, alley,
sidewalk or other public property:
   A.   Inconvenience To Public: The work shall be done so as to cause the
least possible inconvenience to the public.
   B.   Passage Of Water: Provision shall be made for the passage of water
along the gutters.
   C.   Vehicular Traffic: Unless closing of the street is authorized, at least
one-half (1/2) of the street shall be left clear for vehicles.
   D.   Pedestrian Traffic: Safe bridgeways on sidewalks shall be provided for
foot passengers.
   E.   Barricades; Lights: All excavations and piles of dirt or other
materials shall be adequately guarded with barriers and lights so as to protect
others from hazards.
   F.   Pipes And Mains: Pipes and mains shall be protected from freezing.
   G.   Filling Excavations: Excavations shall be refilled as soon as
reasonably possible.
   H.   Restoration: Streets, sidewalks and other property disturbed shall be
restored as nearly as practicable to their condition prior to the work.
   I.   Rubbish; Dirt: All rubbish and dirt shall be promptly removed. (1982
Code § 4.133)
7-2-4: STREET RESTORATION FEE:
The city council may, by resolution, establish a reasonable fee which must be
paid by the person doing the work to cover the cost of road restoration
whenever pavement or other hard surfacing on any street or alley is damaged by
any excavation. (1982 Code § 4.134)
7-2-5: SUBSURFACE INSTALLATION:
   A.   Map:
      1.   Required: The applicant for any excavation permit, or for any water
or sewer construction permit involving excavation in or along any public
street, alley, sidewalk or other public property shall submit a detailed map
showing the location and depth of any subsurface installation to be installed
altered, repaired or removed.
      2.   Corrective Information: If upon completion of the work the actual
location and depth varies from that proposed, the person to whom the permit is
issued shall file such corrective information as may be necessary with the city
clerk. (1982 Code § 4.135)
   B.   Records:
      1.   Maintenance Of Records: The city clerk shall maintain a map or other
record showing the location of all utility and other installations made beneath
the surface of any public street, alley, sidewalk or other public property.
      2.   Completeness And Accuracy Of Information: The information shall be
sufficiently complete and accurate as to permit anyone making an excavation to
avoid damage to any existing underground installation and to properly locate
any new installation.
      3.   Recording Of Information: New information shall be recorded as soon
as practicable upon the issuance of a permit or the completion of an
underground installation. (1982 Code § 4.136)
CHAPTER 3
BUILDING NUMBERS 1
SECTION:
7-3-1: Assignment Of Numbers
7-3-2: Base Streets
7-3-3: Numbering System
7-3-4: Unusual Situations
7-3-5: New Buildings
7-3-6: Record
7-3-7: Use Of Numbers
 
Notes
1 1. MSA § 412.221, subd. 18.
7-3-1: ASSIGNMENT OF NUMBERS:
The city clerk shall assign a building number to each residence, public
building, commercial building, industrial building and other building within
the city except outbuildings and accessory buildings. (1982 Code § 4.111)
7-3-2: BASE STREETS:
For the purpose of assigning building numbers and street directional
designations, Oak Street and First Street are hereby designated as base
streets. Streets lying south of Oak Street and west of First Street shall not
bear any directional designation. Streets running north and south and lying
north of Oak Street shall bear the directional designation "North" followed by
the street name or number. Streets running east and west and lying east of
First Street shall bear the directional designation "East" followed by the
street name or number. (1982 Code § 4.112)
7-3-3: NUMBERING SYSTEM:
   A.   Block Designations: The building numbering system shall be such that
each block along a street is allocated a hundred number designation beginning
in the block adjacent to the base street and running progressively, in one
hundred (100) number intervals per block, away from the base street.
   B.   Odd/Even Numbers: Odd numbers shall be used on one side of all streets,
and even numbers on the opposite side.
   C.   Numbers Assigned In Block: The numbers assigned in a block shall be
allocated in equal units of frontage as nearly as practical.
   D.   Building Numbers: Numbers for buildings shall coincide as nearly as
possible to the location of the main entrance to the building upon the lot.
(1982 Code § 4.113)
7-3-4: UNUSUAL SITUATIONS:
When a block is of unusual size, when any street does not run in a generally
east-west or generally north-south direction, or when for any other reason the
usual numbering requirements cannot be followed, the city clerk shall assign
block and building numbers in a manner corresponding as nearly as practical to
the numbering provided for in this code, or such other numbering as is most
practical and convenient. (1982 Code § 4.114)
7-3-5: NEW BUILDINGS:
Whenever a building permit is issued for the construction of a principal
building on any property within the city, the city clerk shall assign the
appropriate building number and street address to the building. (1982 Code §
4.115)
7-3-6: RECORD:
The city clerk shall keep and maintain a permanent record of building numbers
and street addresses assigned. All assignments shall be final except that the
city clerk may correct any erroneous assignment and may change any assignment
which, though correct, is impractical. (1982 Code § 4.116)
7-3-7: USE OF NUMBERS:
Each property owner shall obtain from the city clerk the correct building
number for the property and cause the number to be placed upon the building, in
a suitable location at the main entrance, in figures not less than two and one-
half inches (21/2") high. (1982 Code § 4.117)
CHAPTER 4
TREES AND VEGETATION
SECTION:
7-4-1: Interference Prohibited
7-4-2: Authority Over Vegetation
7-4-1: INTERFERENCE PROHIBITED:
No person shall plant or remove any trees, plants, shrubs or flowers growing or
planted in or on or overhanging any park, street, alley, sidewalk or boulevard
of the city except by permission of the road and bridge department. (1982 Code
§ 4.151)
7-4-2: AUTHORITY OVER VEGETATION:
   A.   Care And Maintenance: The road and bridge department shall have full
power to maintain, trim, prune, remove and otherwise care for all trees,
plants, shrubs, flowers and other vegetation growing in all parks, and on,
adjacent to or overhanging all streets, alleys, sidewalks and boulevards of the
city.
   B.   Formulation Of General Plan: The road and bridge department shall
formulate general plans for the trimming, maintenance and pruning of trees,
plants, shrubs, flowers and other vegetation in such places and for the removal
of any trees, plants, shrubs, flowers or other vegetation which has become
diseased, damaged, noxious or dangerous.
   C.   Entry Upon Private Premises: The road and bridge department shall have
the power to enter upon private property for the purpose of inspection and for
carrying out the provisions of this section. (1982 Code § 4.152)
CHAPTER 5
TELECOMMUNICATIONS
SECTION:
7-5-1: Definitions
7-5-2: Permit Procedure
7-5-3: Security
7-5-4: Inspection
7-5-5: Conditions Of Use
7-5-6: Restoration; Relocation
7-5-7: Indemnification
7-5-8: Company Default
7-5-9: Existing Facilities
7-5-1: DEFINITIONS:
The terms defined in this section have the meanings given them:
COMPANY: A natural or corporate person, business association, political
subdivision, public or private agency of any kind, its successors and assigns,
who or which seeks or is required to construct, install, operate, repair,
maintain, remove or relocate facilities in the city.
DIRECTOR: The director of public works, or equivalent position at the city, or
designated representative.
FACILITIES: Telecommunications equipment of any kind, including but not limited
to audio, video, paging, facsimile or similar service, not governed by
Minnesota Statutes Annotated chapter 238, including all trunks, lines,
circuits, physical connections, switching equipment, wireless communication
equipment of all kinds, and any necessary appurtenances owned, leased or
operated by a company on, over, in, under, across or along public ground.
PUBLIC GROUND: Highways, roads, streets, alleys, public ways, utility easements
and public grounds in the city. (Ord. 223, 9-5-1995)
7-5-2: PERMIT PROCEDURE:
   A.   Permit Required: A company may not construct, install, repair, remove
or relocate facilities, or any part thereof, in, on, over, under or along
public ground without first obtaining a permit from the city.
   B.   Application: Application for a permit is made to the director.
   C.   Permit Fee: The application must be accompanied by the permit fee set
by the city council by resolution.
   D.   Acceptance Of Requirements: By receiving a permit pursuant to this
chapter, the company accepts and agrees to comply with all of the requirements
of this chapter.
   E.   Issuance:
      1.   Permit Approval: If the director determines that the applicant has
satisfied the requirements of this chapter, the director may issue a permit to
the company.
      2.   Hearing:
         a.   Request For Hearing: An applicant may contest a permit denial or
the conditions of approval by written notice to the city clerk requesting a
city council review within fourteen (14) days of the director's action.
         b.   Time For Hearing: The city council shall hear any contest of the
director's actions under this chapter within forty five (45) days of the city
clerk's receipt of the contest notice.
      3.   Franchise Agreement: Nothing in this chapter precludes the city from
requiring a franchise agreement with the applicant, as allowed by law, in
addition to the issuance of a permit set forth herein. (Ord. 223, 9-5-1995)
7-5-3: SECURITY:
   A.   Security Required: Prior to commencement of work, the company must
deposit with the city security in the form of certified check, letter of credit
or construction bond, in a sufficient amount as determined by the director for
the completion of the work.
   B.   Term: The security will be held until the work is completed plus a
period of two (2) months thereafter to guarantee that restoration work has been
satisfactorily completed.
   C.   Multiple Projects: Upon application of the company, providing such
information as the director may require, if two (2) or more work projects are
to be constructed during a calendar year, the director may accept, in lieu of
separate security for each project, a single security for multiple projects in
such form and amount as determined, in the discretion of the director, to be
sufficient to assure completion of all projects which may be in progress at any
one time during that calendar year and to guarantee that restoration work will
be satisfactorily completed. The security will then be returned to the company
with interest if required by law and then interest at the applicable statutory
rate. (Ord. 223, 9-5-1995)
7-5-4: INSPECTION:
When the work is completed, the company must request an inspection by the
director. The director will determine if the work has been satisfactorily
completed and provide the company with a written report of the inspection and
approval. (Ord. 223, 9-5-1995)
7-5-5: CONDITIONS OF USE:
   A.   Regulation; Permit Schedule: The director is authorized and directed to
prepare suitable regulations and schedules for the administration of permits
issued under this chapter.
   B.   Use Of Public Ground: Facilities must be located, constructed,
installed, maintained or relocated so as not to endanger or unnecessarily
interfere with the usual and customary traffic, travel, and use of public
ground. The facilities are subject to additional conditions of the permit as
established by the director including, but not limited to:
      1.   The right of inspection by the city at reasonable times and places;
      2.   The obligation to relocate the facilities pursuant to subsections 7-
5-6C and D of this chapter; and
      3.   Compliance with all applicable regulations imposed by the Minnesota
public utilities commission and other state and federal law, including prompt
compliance with the requirements of the gopher state one call program,
Minnesota Statutes Annotated chapter 216D.
   C.   Location: The facilities must be placed in a location agreed to by the
city. The company shall give the city forty five (45) days' advanced written
notice of the company's proposed location of facilities within the public
ground. No later than forty five (45) days after the city's receipt of the
company's written notice, the city will notify the company in writing of the
city's acceptance or rejection of the proposed location. If the city rejects
the company's proposed location, the city shall propose alternative locations.
The city does not waive or forfeit its right to reject the location of
facilities by failure to respond within the forty five (45) days.
   D.   Emergency Work: A company may open and disturb the surface of public
ground without a permit where an emergency exists requiring the immediate
repair of its facilities. In such event the company must request a permit not
later than the second working day thereafter and comply with the applicable
conditions of the permit. In no event, may the company undertake such an
activity which will result in the closing of a street or alley without prior
notification to the city.
   E.   Street Improvements: The city will give the company written notice of
plans for street improvements where permanent paving or resurfacing is
involved. The notice must contain:
      1.   The nature and character of the improvements;
      2.   The streets upon which the improvements are to be made;
      3.   The extent of the improvements, the time when the city will start
the work; and
      4.   If more than one street is involved, the sequence in which the work
is to proceed.
   F.   Protection Of Facilities: The company must take reasonable measures to
prevent the facilities from causing damage to persons or property. The company
must take reasonable measures to protect its facilities from damage that could
be inflicted on the facilities by persons, property, or the elements. The
company must take specific protective measures when the city performs work near
the facilities.
   G.   Prior Service Connections: In cases where the city is undertaking the
paving or resurfacing of streets and the facilities are located under such
street, the company may be required to install service connections prior to the
paving or resurfacing if it is apparent that service will be required during
the five (5) year period following the paving or resurfacing.
   H.   Nonright Of Way Public Ground: Nothing in this chapter is intended to
grant to the company authority beyond that given by Minnesota Statutes
Annotated section 222.37 for use of the public right of ways for construction
and operation of facilities. If the city allows the company to use its nonright
of way public ground, the terms of this chapter apply to the extent they are
consistent with the contract, statutory and common law rights the city owns in
such property. (Ord. 223, 9-5-1995)
7-5-6: RESTORATION; RELOCATION:
   A.   Restoration:
      1.   Required: Upon completion of the work, the company must restore the
general area of the work, including paving and its foundations, to the same
condition that existed prior to commencement of the work and must exercise
reasonable care to maintain the same condition for two (2) years thereafter.
The work must be completed as promptly as weather permits.
      2.   Noncompliance:
         a.   Work Performed By City: If the company does not promptly perform
and complete the work, remove all dirt, rubbish, equipment and material, and
restore the public ground to the same condition, the city may put it in the
same condition at the expense of the company.
         b.   Reimbursement Of Costs: The company must, upon demand, pay to the
city the direct and indirect cost of the work done for or performed by the
city, including, but not limited to, the city's administrative costs. To
recover its costs, the city will first draw on the security posted by the
company and then recover the balance of the costs incurred from the company
directly by written demand. This remedy is in addition to any other remedies
available to the city.
   B.   Company Initiated Relocation: The company must give the city written
notice prior to a company initiated relocation of facilities. A company
initiated relocation must be at the company's expense and must be approved by
the city, such approval not to be unreasonably withheld.
   C.   City Initiated Relocation: The company must promptly and at its own
expense, with due regard for seasonal working conditions, permanently relocate
its facilities whenever the city requires such relocation.
   D.   Vacation Of Public Ground: The vacation of public ground does not
deprive the company of the right to operate and maintain its facilities in the
city. If the vacation proceedings are initiated by the company, the company
must pay the relocation costs. If the vacation proceedings are initiated by the
city or other persons, the company must pay the relocation costs unless
otherwise agreed to by the city, company and other persons. (Ord. 223, 9-5-
1995)
7-5-7: INDEMNIFICATION:
   A.   Scope: The company will indemnify, keep and hold the city, its elected
officials, officers, employees, and agents free and harmless from any and all
claims and actions on account of injury or death of persons or damage to
property occasioned by the construction, installation, maintenance, repair,
removal, relocation or operation of the facilities affecting public ground,
unless such injury or damage is the result of the negligence of the city, its
elected officials, employees, officers, or agents. The city will notify the
company of claims or actions and provide a reasonable opportunity for the
company to accept and undertake the defense.
   B.   Claim Defense:
      1.   Notice Of Claim: If a claim or action is brought against the city
under circumstances where indemnification applies, the company, at its sole
expense, shall defend the city if written notice of the claim or action is
given to the company within a period wherein the company is not prejudiced in
the defense of such claim or action by lack of such notice.
      2.   Control Of Litigation: If the company undertakes the defense, the
company shall have complete control of such claim or action, but it may not
settle without the consent of the city, which shall not be unreasonably
withheld.
      3.   Third Party Claim: This subsection is not, as to third parties, a
waiver of any defense or immunity otherwise available to the city. In defending
any action on behalf of the city, the company is entitled to assert every
defense or immunity that the city could assert in its own behalf. (Ord. 223, 9-
5-1995)
7-5-8: COMPANY DEFAULT:
   A.   Notice: If the company is in default in the performance of the work
authorized by the permit, including, but not limited to, restoration
requirements, for more than thirty (30) days after receiving written notice
from the city of the default, the city may terminate the rights of the company
under the permit. The notice of default must be in writing and specify the
provisions of the permit under which the default is claimed and state the
grounds of the claim. The notice must be served on the company by personally
delivering it to an officer thereof at its principal place of business in
Minnesota or by certified mail to that address.
   B.   City Action On Default: If the company is in default in the performance
of the work authorized by the permit, the city may, after the above notice to
the company and failure of the company to cure the default, take such action as
may be reasonably necessary to abate the condition caused by the default. The
company must reimburse the city for the city's reasonable costs, including
costs of collection and attorney fees incurred as a result of the company
default. The security posted under section
7-5-3 of this chapter will be applied by the city first toward payment for such
reimbursement. (Ord. 223, 9-5-1995)
7-5-9: EXISTING FACILITIES:
Companies with facilities, in, on, over, under or along public ground on the
effective date hereof must take prompt action to comply with this chapter and
the permits authorized for this chapter. A company, however, is not required to
reapply for a permit obtained from the city prior to the effective date hereof.
A company is not required to pay the difference between the permit fee of a
previously obtained permit and the equivalent newly obtained permit under this
chapter. All other provisions of this chapter apply to existing facilities.
(Ord. 223, 9-5-1995)
TITLE 8
